1. Excellence
1.0 Introduction to the industrial need 
Lightweight materials have become increasingly critical for producing components for aircrafts, cars, trains, ships, 
and defence equipment. Especially, lightweight metal and alloys possess high strength-to-weight ratios and low 
density. [1] Common applications are met in the automotive, aerospace, manufacturing, railway and other large 
niche applications. For example, lighter vehicles consume less fuel, emit less harmful gases and provide a better 
performance. It should be noted that the aforementioned sectors (based on recent Eurostat data [ 2]) are of crucial 
importance for the European Manufacturing Industry providing more than 6 million jobs and contributing ~11% 
to the EC-28 GDP. As lightweight metals we consider aluminum, magnesium, and titanium alloys. Moreover, 
 
1 F.C. Campbell, “Lightweight Materials – understanding the basics”, ASM International, 2012 
2 Manufacturing statistics - NACE Rev. 2, Data extracted in May 2017. 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [6 of 70] 
 
metal matrix composite materials that traditionally incorporate micron scale reinforcements in a bulk metallic 
matrix offer opportunities to tailor material properties such as hardness, tensile strength, thermal stability, ductility, 
density, thermal and elect rical conductivity, and wear resistance. With the advent of nanomaterials, 
nanocomposites are envisioned, and are being developed, with properties that overcome technical limitations 
of pure metals or composites that contain micron scale reinforcements. In the past decade, much work has been 
done towards developing polymer matrix nanocomposites and such materials are already used in various 
applications. [
3] However, Metal matrix composites containing nanoparticles (NPs) or carbon nanotubes could 
offer distinct advantages over polymer composites due to the inherent high temperature stability, high strength, high 
stiffness, wear resistance, thermal and electrical conductivity of the metal matrix. [4]  
The LightMe project aspires to be a point of reference for boosting innovation in the field of lightweight metal 
matrix nanocomposites (MMnC)  setting up an O pen Innovation Ecosystem (test bed) that will boost  the 
introduction of new functionalities , features and capabilities  to lightweight metals. The LightMe Ecosystem 
will provide the necessary infrastructure (6 Pilot Lines – PL) and knowhow for upscaling the new materials concepts  
related to lightweight MMnC 
and advance materials, in a cost 
effective and sustainable way. 
Besides the upscaling units the 
Ecosystem will provide services 
including monitoring, testing, 
modelling & simulation, 
standardization, regulatory 
compliance
, nanosafety and 
innovation management (IM) 
addressing the industrial needs 
of SMEs and large enterp rises 
that will access the Ecosystem  
and thus, ensuring the 
technology transfer to the 
market. ( Figure 1.1 ). The 
LightMe ecosystem  
 
Figure 1.1: LightMe open access innovation Ecosystem structure 
will consist of 17 core aligned and complementary partners, members of the LightMe consortium, established 
in 11 EC countries and will offer open, non-discriminated access to clients, including SMEs and start-ups, acting 
as a one stop shop. The LightMe ecosystem will be represented by a legal entity – a Non for Profit Organization 
(NPO) – that will be the Single Entry Point  for the customers – and will have the mandate to sign contracts on 
behalf of the Ecosystem. The positioning of LightMe in the innovation value chain will allow to function as a bridge 
between upstream (material developers  and knowhow suppliers as Universities and Research  Centers) and 
downstream (end users) industries.
1.1 Objectives  
A. Objectives related to the set up and operation of the LightMe Ecosystem 
1. Set up a sustainable open innovation ecosystem for efficient , low cost  and fast upscaling of lightweight 
metal alloys and nanocomposites and related products, consisting of 6 operational building blocks (Figure 
1.1) 
2. Determine administrative structure and define procedures and roles – avoiding any overlapping that can 
potentially lead to internal conflicts – securing a smooth operation of the ecosystem,  
3. Establish a Non-for-profit Organization acting as a Single-Entry Point (SEP) for the clients of the ecosystem 
and undertaking the responsibility of administrative and legal aspects. 
4. Clarify governance, organization and operational procedures, including knowledge management and IPR 
handling between the members of the Ecosystem as well as between the clients and the ecosystem 
5. Develop a decision-making process in the ecosystem enabling the identification and evaluation of the needs 
of test cases brought by clients and translating them in upscaling, characterization and services workflows. 
6. Enhance the operation and implement additional features to the 6 PL of the ecosystem in order to cope with 
the industrial requirements demanded by the customers (SMES, industries) in terms of novel lightwe ight 
products development including usage of nanoparticles.  
 
3 Muller K. et. Al. Nanomaterials 2017, 7, 74; doi:10.3390/nano7040074. 
4 P.K. Rohatgi, et. al., “Lightweight MMNCs – stretching the boundaries of metals”, Materials Matters, 2007, Vol 2.No 4, 16

7. Το integrate novel introduction method by ultrasound of nanoparticles in a batch process with suitable 
volume. For LPDC in a pilot scale production up to 150 kg and in rapid processing of small volumes for 
GSC.  
8. To increase volume production of HPDC by optimizing the following processing parameters:  melt volume, 
melt temperature, stirring rate (mechanical stirring), stirring vane design, ultrasonic probe shape/material 
and depth, ultrasonic frequencies and pulse rates, and melt feed rates into the shot die. Modelling can utilised 
to determine the effect of NPs on the die filling of the composite and thus limit defects. By determining the 
optimum NP addition levels, pouring temperatures, and plunger speeds scrap levels can be reduced thereby 
increasing production rates. The modelling will give insights into optimal casting for changing component 
geometries and alloys 
9. For the WLAM pilot line, a specific procedure for process parameters develop ment will be employed 
consisting of 3 steps: 1) definition of the AM setup, 2) DoE for process window adjustment and 3) validation 
through manufacturing of standard test artefacts
5. All test results (imaging and material characterization), 
stored continuously in a DB, will speed up the development of new MMnC by WLAM based on previous 
developments stored in the DB making each new development faster. 
10. Reduce by 70% the amount of faulty parts per day produced by the Borealis machine thanks to the 
integration of a closed loop control able to detect and correct online the deposition errors occurring during 
the DED process.   
11. To enhance the operation of SPS -KOBO PL modification of SPS tool and tool assembling system, 
improvement of KOBO process and tool design to increase a PL productivity (up to 20-40%) and decrease 
the production cost (up to 30%). SPS -KOBO pilot line targets in the production of light weight bearing 
rings and profiles for cold forging of fasteners and other elements for aircraft/automotive industry from 
nanocomposite powders 
B. Objectives related to the validation and demonstration of the LightMe ecosystem 
12. Validate the proper operation of the ecosystem based on 8 selected test cases for upscaling, testing and 
demonstrating in operation environment of nanoenabled materials concept introduced by SMEs and 
industry demonstrating a 20% faster validation of materials compared to current SoA validation 
methodologies.   
13. Launch an open call of interest for test cases (at least 10) dedicated to SMEs that will be able to access the 
ecosystem during the last two years of the project for free. 
14. Proceed with improvements of operational procedures based on the feedback received from the test cases 
C. Objectives related to the LightMe sustainability 
15. To establish clustering and networking channels with EPPN (European Pilot Production Network) , ΑΜ-
Motion, European Materials Characterization and Modelling council etc., and other test beds (upscaling, 
characterization and modelling), particularly in the field of metal Alloys and composites, for cooperation 
and developing synergies towards a pan European integrated and sustainable ecosystem. 
16. Collaborate with European initiatives  including open data repositories (e.g. EPPN, Nanosafety cluster, 
enanomapper etc) and regulatory agencies. 
17. Undertake communication/dissemination activities for promoting the ecosystem in targeted audiences, 
advertising the “success case” stories that will arise from the test cases. 
18. To continuously update the initial business plan of the LightMe ecosystem 
19. Liaise with potential investors (venture capitals and business angels) seeking extra funding  and thus 
facilitating the access to funding for potential customers as well as with relevant Associations.
1.2 Relation to the work programme  
Specific challenge 
The field of new smart lightweight nano-enabled materials … composite components and structures.  
There have been sustained efforts since the 1970’s oil crises to reduce weight in transport systems in ord er to 
achieve improved energy efficiency. [ 6] Especially, when it comes to lightweight metals, Al, Mg and Ti alloys 
have been applied in various cases. Their wider applicability in the manufacturing industry demands enhancement 
of their mechanical properties  as well as other functions . For example, although Mg is the lightest structural 
metal, its strength and stiffness need to be increased in order to be applied in high demand applications. Ceramic 
particles have long been considered as 
a potential way to make metals stronger. However, with microscale 
ceramic particles, the infusion process results in a loss of plasticity. [ 7] Nanoscale particles, in contrast, can 
enhance strength (due to phenomena like load transfer effect, Hall -Petch and Orowan Strengthening), maintain 
 
5 To be performed in accordance with ISO ASTM 52902, in development for PBF/DED.  
6 T. Mason, “New and advanced materials”, Future of Manufacturing Project, Foresight, Government Office for Science, 2013 
7 R. Casati, M. Vedani,  “MMC reinforced by nanoparticles – a review”, 4, (2014), Metals, 65  
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [8 of 70] 
 
or even improve metals’ plasticity (CTE and EM mismatch effect) [ 8, 9], even provide additional functionalities 
e.g. self-cleaning, anti-bacterial as in the case of TiO2 NPs, or self-lubrication for the case of Graphene or MoS2. 
The greatest challenges industry has faced for the development of MMnCs in wide application were on one 
hand the cost of nanoscale reinforcements and on the other hand the cost and the complexity in synthesis 
and processing of nanocomposites. [4] The last years, advances in synthesis of NPs have led to the decrease of 
their cost while, new technologies (e.g. additive manufacturing – 3D printing) have allowed the design and 
manufacturing of geometrical complex objects. LightMe ecosystem has brought together European Leaders in 
technologies related to manufacturing, modelling and characterization of MMnC to promote innovation through 
open access to their Pilot line facilities and services. Thus, LightME will provide the means to stakeholders in 
the field of lightweight metals (e.g. SMEs, end users, industry), to develop novel materials and products with 
enhanced properties and functionalities. Assessment of environmental impact , application of innovation  
management, standards & regulatory compliance, training & technology transfer will allow the wide adoption 
the technologies in the market.  
Scope 
Open Innovation Test Beds should upgrade …  including nano -particle/objects; 
The core of the LightMe Ecosystem is the upscaling Building block containing the 6 PL, located in 5 different 
countries along Europe. These existing PL (described in paragraph 1.3.1a) will be further enhanced and 
improved (analytical description in table 1.4) so as to be used for upscaling new material concepts and products 
based on lightweight MMnC. The modifications will target in the safe and sustainable incorporation of NPs in 
the production lines, leading to composite lightweight metals (Al, Mg and Ti alloys reinforced by various types 
of NPs e.g. carbides, oxides, carbon NPs) with enhanced properties and/or additional functionalities. The PLs 
will be open to be accessed by SMEs, industry and research organization via the SEP, under fair terms and 
conditions in order to upscale their test cases. The LightMe ecosystem will also provide additional services to its 
customers in order to ensure the successful development of the novel materials and products. These services span 
from modelling and simulation (aiming in the reduction of experimental trials and processes optimization), testing 
and characterization, including field tests. Focus will be given in the H&S aspects. Assessment of risks, including 
the ones derived from the use of NPs will take place for each of the PL and the test cases introduced on the 
Ecosystem.   
Attention should be given to materials new functions … to the association of dissimilar materials;  
The integration of NPs in metal matrices results in properties enhancement or in acquisition of new functionalities 
as described in the first paragraph of this chapter. However, the main barriers to overcome in the production lines 
are the inhomogeneous dispersion of reinforcement in the matrix and particle agglomeration . These two 
defects may lead to degradation of properties and pre-mature failure of the products, which in turns hinders their 
market adoption. The LightMe ecosystem will offer all necessary tools: manufacturing & processing expertise, 
advanced technologies, online monitoring and control systems, modelling and simulation of processes, and 
characterization techniques for both structural and morphological characterization as well as for testing of 
functional properties. Correlation of manufacturing parameters with the end application will provide more robust 
processes.  
Potential regulatory, economic and technical barriers should be identified and assessed; 
The European manufacturing sector is subject to various nat ional and European regulatory and voluntary 
requirements and certifications, concerning energy consumption, environmental risks and impact, health and 
safety, material qualification and certification of products, etc. , which implies a big time and cost eff ort from 
industry, particularly for SMEs. Additionally, especially for the latter, there is a lack of specialized personal to 
deal with regulatory and standardization components. These surplus and mismatch of regulations and standards 
at national and EU level are quite hard for the companies to comply, as they are responsible of high administrative 
burdens and costs. Finally, a major issue for start-ups and SMEs is the high cost of acquiring pilot lines for testing. 
LightMe besides the access to PL, intends to provide high level consultancy concerning regulations and standards 
in order to ensure the alignment of the upscaling activities with the standards of the corresponding sectors and 
specific applications. Technoeconomic analysis, LCA/LCC and assessment of environmental impact of the new 
materials and processes will be also offered by the ecosystem services to its clients. 
Finally, technical barriers are often inhibiting or even stop innovative ideas. However, there is a plenty of 
knowledge generated in r esearch institutes, universities and research -intensive companies, that could provide 
solutions to many such barriers. LightMe aspires to provide a safe and neutral open innovation environment 
where transfer of knowledge and experience will become available to industry for providing technical solutions.  
A methodology for providing open access at fair conditions … and dissemination across Europe;

The LightMe ecosystem will provide open access to various potential stakeholders, particularly to SMEs  and 
midcaps, which will take advantage of the PL and the services provided. In order to achieve a self -sustainable 
ecosystem, the terms and condition for accessing it should be attractive. There are four  main issues that are of 
high concern by the potential customers: costs, time, IP protection and confidentiality. LightMe will be in the 
position to offer highly competitive prices since the synergies that will be developed inside the test bed will 
decrease administrative and operational costs and will maintain very low marginal costs. The partners of the 
ecosystem will focus on factors that can enable and accelerate the pace of innovation and increase the yield of 
major innovation such as teamwork, commitment, standardized portfolio management, clear goals, well defined 
milestones and effective technology transfer  and Innovation Management. Results protection strategy and IPR 
issues will be of high importance thus, patentability and freedom to operated analysis Non -Disclosure 
Agreements ( NDAs), and contracts will  guide the developments evolution and regulate and cover the 
collaboration between LightMe and customers. This will be achieved through the establishment of a N on-for-
profit organization that will act as a Single Entry Point. The NPO will have the mandate to represent legally the 
ecosystem to its potential clients, singing contracts and arranging agreements. LightMe will also put a lot of effort 
in dissemination, communication and exploitation activities 
across the European industry in the field of 
lightweight metals and composites. This will be done by a series of activities including workshops, participation 
in trade and fairs, liaison with professional and trade associations in the relevant fields and networking/clustering 
with similar initiatives.  
Quality control processes and tools should be validated to allow on-line quality controls; 
Besides the broad range of post process materials’ characterization equi pment that will be available in the 
ecosystem, the Monitoring Building Block of the Ecosystem (Figure 1.1) will provide process analytical 
technologies control based on the introduction of in line process and materials sensors in the pilot lines for the 
monitoring of key quality parameters, such as the surface homogeneity, absence of defects, etc. They will greatly 
support a number of objectives: 1) replicability and technology transfer when the developed process would be 
implemented in the industry where similar systems could be used for in line quality analysis purposes, 2) decrease 
of the process ramp up time  at the pilot line when approaching a new end user case taking outmost benefit of 
generated past knowledge and quick reply on the compliance with clients’ needs. 3) The quality control system 
design and execution will follow a validation protocol, that will be developed within the LightMe in a step-by-
step format. The QC processes and tools will meet criteria such as ease of use; ability to be automated and 
controlled by computer systems; costs; sample throughput; environmental, H&S requirements. 
Materials should be demonstrated in relevant industrial environments. 
One of the main targets of the LightMe ecosystem is to operate as a bridge between upstream industry (raw 
material providers, developers of alloys and nanomaterials) and downstream industry (end users). Thus, the 
ecosystem will cooperate closely with industrial partners in order to carry out demonstration activities of the new 
processes, materials and products in relevant industrial environment (TRL6) or even in operational environment 
(TRL 7). In this way a fast and efficient adoption of the new technologies by the market will be achieved. 
Proposals submitted under this … and reusability of data produced in the course of the project.  
A main part of this project concerns the positioning of the LightMe ecosystem in the European R&D&I reality. 
Thus, activities related to networking, cooperation and clustering with other similar initiatives and established 
data repositories (e.g. Zenodo, enanoMapper and others) will take place in parallel with disse mination and 
communication activities. A robust Data Management Plan will be developed to facilitate these activities, without 
setting in jeopardy the generated IPs of the clients.
1.3  Concept and methodology 
1.3.1 Concept of LightMe project 
1.3.1.a Advance and composite lightweight metal materials 
The main target of the LightMe Open Innovation Ecosystem is to result in innovative nano reinforced metal 
matrix composites produced by casting methods (High and Low Pressure Die Casting) , Additive Manufacturing 
and Spark Plasma Sintering, exhibiting advance properties and/or multifunctionality. Advanced characteristics such 
as high hardness, ultimate tensile strength, flexural strength, wear and corrosion resistance while increasing 
the weight fraction of reinforcement in an upscaling manner is desired . Thus, state of the art unreinforced Ti, 
Al and Mg metal matrix composite need modifications in order to achieve enhanced performance and 
multifunctionality. [
10]. For example, composites reinforced with oxides, carbides and 2D nanomaterials have been 
reported under different load conditions to show outstanding performance and multifunctionality accompanied 
always by lightweight characteristics (Table 1.1). 
 
 
10 Kumar, R., Dhiman, S., A study of sliding wear behaviors of Al-7075 alloy and Al-7075 hybrid composite by response surface methodology 
analysis. Materials & Design 50(0): 351-359. (2013). 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 10 of 70] 
 
Table 1.1: Effect of the incorporation of NPs in lightweight matrices 
NPs category NPs Lightweight & Characteristics 
Oxides 
Al2O3 [11] Flexural strength, wear resistance, hardness & tensile 
strength 
TiO2 [12] Self-cleaning and better corrosion potential 
Y2O3 [13] Tribological enhanced performance, Self-lubricating, 
Carbides 
SiC [14] Tensile and compression strength & ductility decrease 
B4C [15] Toughness, hardness and elastic modulus 
TiC [16] Advanced wear behaviour and hardness 
2D nano 
materials 
CNT [17] Reducing the friction coefficient & lubrication 
Graphene [18] Strength, strain, high shock/vibration absorbency  
MoS2, hBN [19] Self-lubricating, friction control 
 
Al Matrix Composites: Processed by Casting Pilots, AM, SPS -KOBO. During the last two decades, a lot of 
research has been conducted on Al  matrix composites (AMCs). Important AMCs applications in aerospace , 
automotive and infrastructure industries are enabled by functional properties provided by nano scale reinforcements 
including high structural efficiency, excellent wear resistance, and attractive thermal and electrical characteristics. 
[20]. Challenging technical issues are overcome including compatibilit y between reinforcement and matrix, 
affordable primary and secondary processing techniques capable of adequately controlling reinforcement [21]. The 
great enhancement in strength values of these composites is attributed to grain refinement  (Hall – Petch effect), 
strong multidirectional thermal stress at the matrix/NP interface, small size of NPs, good distribution and low degree 
of porosity which leads to effective transfer of applied tensile load to the uniformly distributed strong NPs . More 
than 50% improvement in yield strength of A356 alloy has been observed with nano-sized SiC particles [22]. Finally, 
Al /SiC produced by SPS present a substantial increase of mechanical and tensile and compression strength 
properties. CNT reinforced composites have  also been evaluated with AM processing methods concluding on 
uniform dispersions. [
23]  
Ti matrix composites (TMCs): Processed by MWAM, Borealis & SPS -KOBO: Ti-6Al-4V, an α (hcp)/β (bcc) 
titanium (Ti), is the most widely used Ti alloy which account for more than half of all commercial Ti applications 
[24]. 80% of the produced Ti -6Al-4V is used in aerospace applications and the rest is found in other applications 
including defence, marine, medical, chemical, and other industries [25]. Manufacturing complex metal structures is 
one of the major challenges of developing advanced precision manufacturing as when components are machined 
through conventional techniques, nearly 80% of input metal is  wastes [ 26]. The recent years metallic alloy s 
processed by additive manufacturing (AM) using different alloys, has started to gain the industrial interest. With 
nano reinforced Ti -6Al-4V for example the emphasis is placed on the formation of metallurgical defects and 
microstructures induced by AM and their role on mechanical properties. Due to their high surface area, NP  and 
nanotubes naturally tend to agglomerate to reduce their overall surface energy, making it difficult to obtain a uniform 
dispersion by most conventional processing methods. Among different candidates to reinforce the titanium matrix, 
TiC, TiB and TiB2 have been proven the most suitable for Spark Plasma Sintering (SPS) due to their thermodynamic

stability and similar coefficient of thermal expansion. The properties that these intermetallic Ti-Al alloys exhibit 
are thus highly attractive for lightweight and high-temperature structural applications produced by SPS. 
Mg matrix composites (TMCs) : Processed by HPDC, GSC, MWAM : Mg alloys have been in use for weight 
critical applications. Today Mg based MMC are widely used in aerospace, structural, oceanic and automobile 
applications for its light weight, low density (two thirds that of aluminium), good high temperature mechanical 
properties and good to excellent corrosion resistance. Disadvantages such as vulnerability to corrosion, limited high 
temperature strength, and creep resistance are to be overcome by the development of advanced magnesium alloys. 
However, improvements achiev ed through novel alloy development are limited. This limit can only be stunned 
through reinforcing magnesium alloys with NP improving strength [
27] , wear [28], creep resistance [29] and fatigue 
strength [30]. High Pressure Die Casting using magnesium alloys such as AM60 reinforced with various percentages 
of nanoparticles have been produced with different weight percentages of SiC reinforced nanoparticles using stir 
casting method, the presence of nanoparticle improves the hardness values, tensile strength and the ductility value. 
Similarly, Metal Wire additive manufacturing (MWAM) offers on additional approach to fabricate large -scale 
magnesium alloy components with low cost and high efficiency. It is a promising method for manufacturing 
complex and large scale monolithic components.  
 
1.3.1.b The LightMe Ecosystem 
The concept of innovation ecosystems is receiving increasing attention worldwide. Industrial stakeholders are keen 
to foster innovation ecosystems to systematically cultivate favorabl e environments and encourage innovators to 
create knowledge and capture business value. In particular open innovation ecosystems require specific attention 
when faced with fast-developing emerging industries that closely link science, technology, and business. [
31] 
LightMe aspires to cover a real 
industrial need related to the 
upscaling and development of novel 
lightweight MMnC with advanced 
functionalities and foster their 
adoption by the market. The 
boundaries and value functions of 
the LightMe are depicted in Figure 
1.2 based upon the expertise of its 
member and are positioned across 
upscaling and testing, 
environmental impact and issues 
and market-based aspects.

In the following paragraphs the description of the technological excellence of the E cosystem and the 
corresponding expertise is given. The managerial and operational procedures are provided in the section 2 of the 
proposal.

A. Building Block 1: Pilot lines and fast prototyping units 
Members: OGI, UBrun, AIMEN, Iris, INOP 
1. Low Pressure Die Casting PL (LPDC) 
 
Location Austria 
Partner OGI 
Processing Al alloys and Al MMCs 
Capacity 400 object/day 
Cost/day 2.500 € 
Description 
The objects in this PL are produced with the utilization of dies. 
One half of the die is attached to a fixed machine plate and the 
other to a movable one on a die -casting machine that is 
vertically aligned. The furnace for molten metal is located 
beneath the fixed plate and by applying pressure of up to max 
1 bar to the furnace pushes the molten metal up through an 
intake port into the die chamber. After filling the die, the 
pressure is maintained as the 
metal cools to enable the addition of further molten metal to counter any volume deficits (shrinkage cavities) as the 
metal passes from its molten to solid state. The method can produce components with complex geometries and high 
dimensional accuracy in slower casting cycles compared to HPDC . It is fully automated and needs low complexity 
die technology. 
Main Innovations during LightMe project: Improvement of NPs distribution in the melt (increased wetting 
conditions) and consequently in the final products by application of ultrasonication and electro magnetic stirring 
systems. Use of cover gases will lead to stabilization of NPs and prevention of reactions at elevated temperature that 
causes the release of deleterious gases. NDT monitoring systems applied will lead in  reliable results with low 
variability, consistent cycles that will provide predictable material structures and therefore higher repeatability and 
quality standards.  
The main materials that will be processed are MMC of Aluminum and Magnesium alloys. More specifically the 
following two commercial alloys will be used, combined with various ceramic nanoparticles (e.g. SiC or Al
2O3 etc.) 
1. A 356. It is a Aluminum alloy with 7Si-0.3Mg alloy with 0.2 Fe and 0.1 Zn. It present great elongation, 
high strength and increased ductility. Due to its low iron content it presents improved mechanical 
properties. 
2. AZ91D. It is the most widely used magnesium die cast alloy and has excellent combination of mechanical 
properties, corrosion resistance and castability. 

[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 13 of 70] 
 
 
 
 
2. High Pressure Die Casting PL (HPDC) 
 
Location UK 
Partner Brunel University London (Ubrun) 
Processing Al and Mg alloys and MMCs 
Capacity 1000 object/day 
Cost/day 3.000 €/day 
Description 
Objects produced in this PL also utilize dies; however, in this 
case the dies are horizontally aligned. Due to the high pressure 
used when casting, detailed, thin walled components are 
produced.  The high clamping press ure – up to 1,200 bars – 
holds the two halves of the die together. Cold- chamber, high 
pressure die casting machines such as this one, are mainly used 
for Al and Mg alloys. 
Here, the casting assembly is located outside the two independent melting furnaces. The molten metal is fed into a 
shot chamber, from where a piston drives the metal into the die. At the same time, a high vacuum system removes all 
air/gas within the die cavity.  After filling the die, the injection pressure is maintained as the metal cools.  Once the 
metal has cooled and solidified, the two halves of the die are opened,  and the casting is automatically ejected from 
the die by ejector pins, enabling a robotic arm to then remove the casting from the die chamber.  The method has short 
casting cycles and is suitable for thin-walled components with smooth surfaces. The method is also fully automated. 
Due to the high investment and operation costs and the complicated and expensive dies, the method is used for 
production of large volume components. 
Main Innovations during LightMe project: Besides the innovations referred already in the LPDC, cover gases will 
allow the safer use of novel castable magnesium alloys. Overall the optimization of the following aspects is targeted: 
optimum NP addition levels, optimum processing time, improved distribution of NPs, reduced porosity due to 
agglomeration, improved wetting, and reduced deleterious in situ reactions. Key performance i ndicators; increased 
wear resistance, reduced porosity ensuring the component is leak tight, and a reduction in weight over traditional steel. 
The following innovations will be achieved: 
1. Understanding the effect of the quantity of heterogeneous NP on vi scosity and how this impacts on filling of the 
die and resultant defects. 
2. Integration of ultrasonication, mechanical stirring and electromagnetic stirring systems improve the homogeneity 
of NPs dispersion in the melt. 
3. Use of cover gases. Prevent the formation of deleterious reaction products 
 
Materials to be processed:  
1. (EN AC-AlSi9Cu3(Fe) with SiC NP additions fo application in steering pinion 
2. Mg (ZK60) with CNT additions for applications in transport industry 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
3. Green Sand Casting PL (GSC) 
Location Austria 
Partner OGI 
Processing Al and Mg alloys and MMCs 
Capacity Objects up to 3 tn, 1-20 objects/day  
Cost/day 1.500 € 
Description 

[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 14 of 70] 
 
 
In the Green Sand Casting the molten metal is poured in molds. The metal 
is melt by utilizing induction furnaces. The molds are made of wet sand 
mixed with bentonite clay or organic binders. The molds can be easily 
created in automated assembly lines. The ability to quickly make molds 
through automated machines makes green sand casting economical and 
popular for making medium to high volume castings since the automated 
processes allows for a lot of molds to be quickly made at an affordable 
cost. Besides the low cost, the method is suitable for manufacturing very large castings up to 3 tons. GSC is the most 
widely used casting method for small volume components. On the other hand green sand molds for casting don’t have 
tight dimensional tolerance and thus when precise dimensions are required or smooth surfaces the components should 
be further processed by machining and surface finishing.  
Main Innovations during LightMe project: Advance stirring methods (e.g. ultrasonication. Electromagnetic 
stirring) will lead to enhance NPs distribution in melt. A Melt-on- demand continuous batch processing route by 
induction heating will be followed as based on EXOMET project treatment of smaller quantities (e.g. melts ups to 10-
15 gr) results also in NP enh
anced distribution. Use of cover gases will result in safer operation with Mg alloys. 
Utilization of green bonding systems for sand dies preparation.  
The materials that will be processed in the GSC pilot line are: 
1. Al MMC reinforced with TiO2 presenting photocatalytic activity expressed as anti-bacterial and self-
cleaning properties 
2. Mg MMC reinforced by carbon nanoparticles, presenting reduced weight compared to aluminium products 
and high fatigue strength 
3. Al MMC reinforced with SiC presenting high fatigue and wear resistance properties. 
 
 
4. Metal Wire Additive Manufacturing PL (MWAM) 
 
 
Location Spain 
Partner AIMEN 
Processing Al, Mg and Ti alloys and MMCs 
Capacity Weight: 500kg, Max Size: 1x2x1m . 
Productivity upon the objects size 
Cost/day 2.100 € 
Description 
The Pilot Test Bed Facility for wire AM at AIMEN uses 
the Laser Metal Deposition (LMD) concept to process 
various metallic alloys including Aluminum and Al 
composites 
The metallic wire is supplied in the laser focal point, molten and deposited in weldseams. The final set of weldseams 
composes the three-dimensional component. The system consists of a robotic arm (e.g. ABB IRB 4400),a TruDisk 
16002 16kW laser source coupled to a 200mμ fiber and laser beam quality of 8mm mrad. The laser head is a Trumph 
BEO D70, but a specific one will be incorporated in the project (e.g. Precitec CoaxPrinter). The wire supply is based 
on Fronius TPS 5000 with Robacta drive wire feeder (Ø0.8-2.4mm wires) that allows the adjustment of laser beam-
wire position with a 3 degrees of freedom mechanical positioning system.  The unit is accompanied by a laser radiation 
protective enclosure which will be sealed in the project and equipped with continuous gas supply. 
Main Innovations during LightMe project: Installation of a real time m onitoring system for Al and Mg wire 
processing. New protocols for processing wires containing NPs. Application of inert atmosphere to avoid oxidation 
and reaction when operating Ti and Mg alloys. The target materials of WLAM pilot line are: 
1. Al MMnC: excellent grain shaping improvement leading to higher fatigue properties - large size aircraft 
components, lightweight naval structures; 
2. Ti MMnC: highly superior tensile and fatigue properties: structural components in aircraft industry,  
3. Mg MMnC: high strength – weight ratio - ultralight automotive components,  
4. Steel MMnC significant improvement of hardness and wear resistance – moulds and dies for stamping and 
deep drawing.  
The standardized procedure for process parameters optimization (AM setup, process window setup and validation by 
test artefacts manufacturing), on one hand side, and a fully controlled pilot line (atmosphere with below 50ppm in 

[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 15 of 70] 
 
Oxigen and IR imaging for process monitoring) will lead to significant stability in the process. Together w ith 
incremental approach to build the incoming process development on the basis of previous developments, it will enable 
faster setup of a process for an MMnC (target: 2 weeks for process optimization of a material in comparison to today’s 
more than a 10 weeks of process development for common materials). 
 
 
5. Borealis PL (Borealis)   
 
 
Location Italy 
Partner IRIS srl 
Processing Al and Ti alloys and MMCs 
Capacity Weight: 500kg, Max Size: 1x2x1m. Productivity upon 
the objects size 
Cost/day 1.800 € 
Description 
IRIS’ facilities include a 400 m2 owned lab for experimental testing 
of laser/plasma processing, which have been equipped in 2015 with 
a robotic island for smart hybrid welding as a result of the regional 
founded project ECOWELD and, in 2016, 
with a Prima Industrie 
AM machine, developed and integrated within the Borealis project, 
which 
main result is a novel DED (Directed Energy Deposition)  machine for the production of large and complex (in 
geometry, functionality, composition) parts embracing a multi -technology and multi -material approach in order to 
meet the requirements of aerospace, med -tech and motorsport sectors. Every module of the Borealis Machine has 
been firstly integrated, tested and optimized by using the ECOWELD welding solution which will be the key enabling 
factor for the LightMe pilot lines upgrades, thus strongly boosting the quality of parts produced and the knowledge 
of the AM processes for metal and co mposites. The focused thermal energy coming from a laser source is used to 
fuse metallic powders locally injected by a customized and movable multi -nozzle system which concurs to the 11 
degrees of freedom of the redundant machine (4 on the deposition head, 3 on the machine portal, 2 on the galvo scan 
head and 2 on a roto-
tilting table) designed for big components (working volume up to 4000x1500x750 mm). The 
ablation technology, based on the galvo scan system integrated on the deposition head, supports the A M fabrication 
process for metal manufacturing to allow surface finishing, micro texturing and micro holes that would be otherwise 
unfeasible in traditional machines. The powder feeding system have been designed and developed as a modular 
solution which can integrate several tanks to be connected to the 4 nozzles mounted on the deposition head, thus 
ensuring the chance to create new alloys or composites directly on site by adjusting separately the material flow rate 
for each nozzle.  
Main Innovations during LightMe project: Optimization of closed loop control system and implementation of new 
algorithms for automatic management of process parameters based on real time monitoring. Installation of powder 
recovery system for proper management of unused powder and increase of process efficiency. The monitoring system 
together with the closed loop control will ensure the chance to detect and correct online the deposition errors occurring 
during the DED process, thus reducing by 70% the amount of faulty parts per day and increasing the productivity of 
the machine. Thanks to the closed loop control, the machine will be able to process not only titanium and aluminium 
alloys, but also Metal Matrix Composites which main challenge is to maintain the homogeneous distribution of 
enforcement material in the matrix; indeed, by updating the process parameter layer by layer on the base of the sensors 
feedback, the temperature of the growing part can be kept under control as well as the microstructure and the properties 
of the final material.  
The LightMe upgrade for the Borealis machine will represent a strategical step forward within several sectors such as 
construction, transportation and above all, aerospace which will be able to take advantage of the powerful synergy 
between 
the flexibility in design (in terms of shape but especially size of parts, thanks to the Borealis working volume) 
together with the high performance and the good mechanical properties offers by MMCs. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
6. SPS-KOBO extrusion PL 

[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 16 of 70] 
 
 Location Poland 
Partner INOP 
Processing Al and Ti alloys and MMCs 
Capacity Max Size: 15x15x15 cm. Productivity upon the 
objects size 
Cost/day 2.000 € 
Description 
Existing INOP pilot line consists of spark plasma sintering 
machine HP D 25 -3 (FCT Systeme GmbH) and hydraulic 
KOBO press  of 2000t capacity  equipped with special 
accessory for die rotation. The INOP facility is equipped with 
SPS machine (national Project FNiTP, 2011) for SPS 
technology of nanostructured components manufacturing 
developed within FP6 Bearing and FP7 Pilotmanu projects. 
KOBO extrusion system is installed in INOP facility for 
manufacturing of various profiles of Al alloy based 
nanostructured MMCs for automotive and aircraft industries 
(national Project Nanomet). The SPS  
technology modified within Pilotmanu Project allowed to take into account the self propagation high temperature 
synthesis reactions (during SPS) and find the regimes of ductile Cu based MMC structure formation. The cold KOBO 
extrusion process of SPS allows to obtain profiles at ambient temperature due to development of effective dynamic 
softening processes at the nanoscale. The upgraded pilot line will allow to produce: i) the  light weight Ti based 
composite bearing rings  for aircraft/automotive industry with SPS of nanostructured High energy ball milling 
(HEBM) composite powders made by MBN, and ii) Al alloy (AA6061 and AA7075) based composite profiles with 
SPS-KOBO extrusion for further production of aircraft and automotive fasteners and suspension/frame elements by 
cold forging. Typical fastener alloys are 2024- T4 and 6061- T6 (cold-formed bolts, screws, rivets, machine- screw 
nuts). Additionally, AA7075 HEBM powders will be applied.        
Main Innovations during LightMe project: Installation of monitoring system for more efficient control of process 
parameters. Use of higher strength tools and dies (e.g. graphite and ceramic materials) leading to enhanced 
dimensional accuracy and decrease o f production cost. A replacement the graphite foil of high thickness (400 μm) 
with tungsten foil of low thickness (25 μm) will allow to achieve a higher dimensional accuracy of the sintered parts. 
Application of monitoring system for the external die temperature & modification of software of temperature control 
will allow to improve the quality of sintered products.  New designs and tool assembling and disassembling modules 
of SPS and KOBO will increase the SPS-KOBO PL productivity. 
The target materials of SPS -KOBO pilot line are  pre- alloyed aluminium and titanium alloys reinforced by 
nanoparticles such as SiC, BC4 etc.

B. Building Block 2:  Monitoring of PLs  
Members: Stam, Iris Tech, ISQ 
Monitoring and control are essential in any process to make sure the expected quality is reached. The clients of 
LightMe will have access to validated processes and tools for on-line quality monitoring and control. In particular, 
quality control and process verification systems will be coupled with innovative automated tools to increase the 
process control and ensure the required productivity as well as monitoring the quality of materials and products. 
Process monitoring, and control will be upgraded in all the Pilot Lines, using user-friendly control systems, assuring 
the remotely monitored control and the continuous and safe operation of the processes. Monitoring and control 
systems will promote the ability to suppress external disturbances and assess the status of the processes with the use 
of sensor measurements: this will lead to reliable results with low variability, consistent cycles that will provide 
predictable material structures and therefore higher repeatability and quality standards.  
Process Monitoring 
A number of monitoring techniques exist when it comes to characterizing structures in the nano- and micro-metre 
ranges including SEM (scanning electron microscopy) and AFM (atomic force microscopy)  [
41 42]. Fourier 
transform analysis of the SEM images has been used to quantify the periodicity of the structures. This approach 
enables a global value of spatial period to be quickly calculated, rather than estimating line thickness and spacings 
line by line, and generating a mean value, which is a more laborious process. However, most commonly used 
techniques at this dimensional scale are in fact implemented off line and require sample preparation. Optical 
techniques offer the best opportunity for inline process monitoring, as they are non-contact, non-destructive and can 
be applied to samples as they are, without pre-treatment. The main optical techniques that will be used are: 
White light Interferometry is a non-contact optical method for surface height measurement on 3-D structures with 
surface profiles varying between a mm up to few cm. Surface features ranging from gradual slopes to vertical steps, 
with rough or smooth finishes. An inline spectral reflectance system was developed in the THIME project 43 to 
measure Organic PV films. White light interferometry has been developed into an inline system by Dr Schwab 44 
for measuring the thickness of spacer and cover layers of Blu- Ray discs but can also be applied to measure the 
surface topography of reflective materials. However, while this system measures topography with a high level of 
accuracy (<100nm), it’s lateral resolution is limited to 10s of micrometres. An inline system has been developed by 
Nanometrics [ 45] employing spectral reflectometery in single point scanning arrangement, which enables lateral 
critical dimension measurement with greater accuracy, but still diffraction limited to the spot size of around 1 
micrometre. 
Scatterometry is an optical metrology technique designed for the characterization of test samples from lithography. 
These samples are diffraction gratings with the width of the lines reproducing the critical dimension. Scatterometry 
consists in ellipsometric measurements of the light diffracted from the samples in various experimental 
configurations and the fitting of the data to theoretic predictions. The parameters of the best fit are the most probable 
values for the parameters of the sample.  Scatterometry involves optical instrumentation, diffraction theories, and 
data reduction and sensitivity analysis. It is possible to obtain higher resolution in lateral dimension measurements 
regarding the ones of SEM and AFM techniques, using optical techniques based on scatterometery and 
diffractometry, which can be applied to periodic structures of the type being developed in Laser4Surf. Scatterometry 
uses the instrumentation of a spectroscopic ellipsometer, along with complex mathematical modelling  [
46] and is 
widely used in the microelectronics industry, for example the Nanometrics Atlas [47], and the Nova T600 [48].  
 
39 P. Rey et al., Manufacturing of AA6005A-nanoTiC composite by mechanical alloying, hot extrusion and friction stir welding, accepted to 
be published on the Proceedings of the EuroPM2018 (October, 14-18, Bilbao, 2018)

48 Nova T600, http://www.novameasuring.com/t600.html 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 18 of 70] 
 
Diffractometry using multiple diffraction orders imaged in the far-field is a versatile technique that has potential to 
provide comprehensive information regarding the 3 dimensional features of textured samples. Furthermore, when 
combined with different light source, it covers a broad resolution range: UV light can detect structures with period 
in the few hundreds nm range, whereas cost competitive blue laser can be used for structures with period betwee n 
500 and 700 nm. It has been effectively implemented in several versions for characterising the quality of the grooves 
in DVD and Blu -Ray discs, for example Dr. Schwab’s DOMS  [
49], and Singulus Mastering B.V. [ 50] There are 
some barriers to be tackled in order to be able to implement on in-line systems: careful and time-consuming sample 
preparation are still needed, many samples are vulnerable to radiation damage caused by the incident electrons and 
the optical system is quite complex to be settled in a typical laser equipment. 
Confocal Microscopy most frequently confocal laser scanning microscopy (CLSM), is an optical imaging technique 
for increasing optical resolution and contrast of a micrograph by means of adding a spatial pinhole placed at the 
confocal plane of the lens to eliminate out -of-focus light. It enables the reconstruction of three-dimensional 
structures from sets of images obtained at different depths (a process known as optical sectioning) within a thick 
object. This technique has gaine d popularity in the scientific and industrial communities and typical applications 
are in life sciences, semiconductor inspection and materials science. It may be used to obtain spatial resolution 
below the diffraction limit with resolution of 0.09 μm reported [
51], however once again it is not implemented inline. 
A more salient feature of this technique is that it provides an image of the surface structure, from which specific, 
local dimensions can be calculated, whereas for the current technology under development, it is desirable to obtain 
a general overview of the shape and common dimensions repeated in the periodic pattern, especially where the sizes 
of individual lines can vary over a range. For this reason, it is more effective to employ a metrology that makes use 
of the structure periodicity, such as diffractometry or scatterometery, and provides a description of key features, 
including height, width, sidewall slope and symmetry. Diffractometry is the more attractive option of these two for 
inline process monitoring since it can provide simple information quickly with less data processing. 
Process Control 
In pilot lines, the selection of optimal input parameters for a given output is usually done manually through a trial-
error method. We plan to work on automation of the production parameters. We will implement Machine Learning 
(ML) in LightMe to make calibration of production parameters more automatic, faster and easier than the existing 
practices (manual, empirical). The goal of developing machine learning techniques in the LightMe project is to 
optimise the parameters and settings during production processes thus identifying the control requirements to 
automatize corrections in real time.  
 
C. Building Block 3: Testing and environmental assessment services 
Members: PoliMi, ISQ, UBrun, AIMEN, OGI, INOP, ICCRAM 
The members of the Testing building block (PoliMi, LeUn, UBrun , INOP, ISQ & ICCRAM) have high expertise 
in advance and fast characterization techniques and their interpretation of them in the environmental impact. The 
purpose of testing is to provide the necessary feedback for process optimization, as well as the verification of the 
compliance with corresponding standards (ISO, ASTM). Characterization will take place in structural level as well 
as at functional (mechanical and chemical) properties level. Evaluation of the environmental impact of the new 
materials will take place by LCA/LCC. Finally, in close collaboration with end users real field test will be applied, 
bringing the technologies  up to TRL7. The active involvement of end users (large companies, representative of 
automotive and aerospace sector, are already included in the consortium) will have a significant positive impact in 
the fast adoption of the new technologies by the market. The elements of the building blocks are: 
Structural characterization : In order to provide feedback for process optimization, a set of characterization 
techniques will be applied on developed test cases. This task will be in charge of characterizing the structural and 
morphological properties of the materials used to produce lightweight composites. The composition and crystal 
structure of nanomaterials will be determined with e.g. x -ray diffraction (XRD), x-ray fluorescence (XRF). Their 
surface composition will be determined with e.g. x-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS), while their behaviour in 
suspension will be determined with e.g. dynamic light scattering (DLS), Fourier transformed infrared spectroscopy 
(FT-IR), static light scattering (SLS), nanoparticle tracking analysis (NTA), and others. Microscopic techniques, 
such as electron microscopy, atomic force microscopy, scanning tunnelling microscopy, etc. will be employed to 
analyze both structurally and chemically individual parts of nanomaterials or bulk materials of interest (e.g. surface 
composition of a metal alloy with embedded nanomaterials). Spectroscopic techniques, including XRD, XPS, XRF, 
etc. will be employed to determine the composition and atomic structure of bulk materials and composites.  
Functional properties testing: The key advantage of the developed metal alloy composites is their lower weight 
combined with mechanical properties that meet or exceed the ones of currently used materials. Light metals ensure

the lighter weight, while mechanical properties, such as stress, strain, tensile strength, shear stre ngth, fatigue 
strength, compressive strength, elasticity, ductility, brittleness, plasticity, toughness, hardness, wear resistance etc. 
will be tested using standard techniques. A number of state of the art equipment (Vickers sclerometers, pin-on-disc 
tribometer, abrasion tester, gauge sensors, universal tension testing, salt spray chambers, Taffel tests etc)  will be 
used to determine the functional properties of nano-enabled metal alloy composites. Additional functionalities, such 
as enhanced conductivity, or self-cleaning properties will be tested using dedicated testing protocols. 
inspection a camera is used to monitor the me lting 
process, layer -by-layer. These techniques are not 
influenced by the surface roughness, which is a plus in 
these methods. The offline NDT in AM of big 
components mainly focuses on two issues: component 
warpage due to high thermal stresses caused by high 
process temperature and appearance of defects due to it 
(delamination, pores and cracks, etc.) For that reason, 
the mainly employed NDT in AM pilot lines such as 
Borealis or WLAM are 1) RX to detect any structural 
integrity problem and 2) metrological analysis to 
determine the disparity map of the manufactured 
component using the part scan compared to the original 
part model.

techniques in AM 
Environmental impact, Resource Efficiency  and LCA : The main objective of this element is to assess the 
environmental impact of the new materials and products as well as of the sustainability of the pilot lines and final 
product’s production. In addition, the potential end-of-life scenarios of final lightweight metal alloys products will 
be evaluated, including recyclability and circularity of the resources. The potential environmental impacts of the 
pilot lines and the final products will be determined by means of LCA, using specialized software tool such a s 
Simapro 8. The analysis will involve the following stages: the definition of scope and goal, the development of 
relevant inventory inputs and outputs of the system, the assessment of their potential impacts and the interpretation 
of the results within the context of proposed targets. LCA will be carried out taking into account the guidelines of 
ISO 14040/14044 on products life cycle assessment. The environmental impact categories to be analysed include: 
global warming potential, cumulative energy demand, cumulative exergy demand, resources depletion, ecotoxicity 
among others. The analysis will be based on existing data from the pilot lines as well as on outputs from final 
products and the outcome will be the development of a LCA approach that is specifically tailored for LightMe final 
products. Capital, operational costs and potential cost reductions resulting from implementing the proposed plant 
will be determined by means of a life cycle costing study (LCC). Costs linked to the planning, design, acquisition, 
operation, maintenance, manufacturing and disposal (where applicable) of the pilot lines and the proposed final 
products will be assessed. As indirect costs, environmental externalities linked to their implementation throughout 
its life-cycle will be addressed, provided that their monetary value can be determined and verified. The LCC will 
present a similar structure and will be conducted in parallel to the LCA and the results will make it possible to 
compare the implementation of the final products with the current scenarios from an economic point of view. End-
of-life scenarios will be evaluated including recycling scenarios from the final products considering the inherent 
costs, environmental impacts and associated logistics. Appropriate Circular Economy Indicators will be defined for 
the LightMe’s final products with the aim to assess how well the final products value chains perform in the context 
of a circular economy.  
Additional, for resource efficiency, ecosystem can offer, on request, the application of an eco-efficiency framework 
– ecoPROSYS© (ISQ) with the objective to assist decision -making aiming to improve the environmental and 
economic performance of new products, materials or processes. The ecoPROSYS© (Eco -Efficiency Integrated

fluxes that most contribute for the product and process eco efficiency, through the generation of useful information 
for decision-making in what concerns profit maximization and positive environmental impacts.  
 
D. Building Block 4: Modelling & simulation services 
Members: Access, AIMEN, INOP, Stam, Ubrun  
Materials modelling on multiscale has become an essential part of research, development and engineering to 
optimize existing production processes and a lso to accelerate development or upscaling of advanced materials. 
Success of application of multiscale materials modelling software tools, originating from different scientific and 
engineering communities has been well established under the banner of Integrated Computational Materials 
Engineering (ICME), strongly promoted by communities such as European Materials Modelling Council and TMS. 
These tools may include thermodynamic modelling, atomistic simulations based on molecular dynamics (MD) or 
Density Functional Theory (DFT) to understand local properties in the final product, microstructural simulation 
based on phase field to understand relation between solidification and microstructural parameters and also process 
modelling based on continuum modelling approach to predict defects and aid in process development. In the current 
proposed ecosystem, due to the presence of nanoparticles leading to lightweight MMnC for industrial applications, 
a combination of modelling tools with high degree of integration and interoperability will be essential for predicting 
and linking physical quantities on different length scales to the property of the final product. The LightMe clients 
will have access to a wide variety of modelling and simulation tools that will allow a faster optimization process in 
the upscale (e.g. utilization of ProCAST and STAR -Cast and or MAGMASOFT, MICRESS) or for prediction of 
properties via modelling of the nanostructure. Synergies between modelling and testing building blocks will provide 
the valuable input to the upscaling and monitoring group for the improvement of yields and efficiency of the 
production processes. 
Casting processes modelling and simulation:  
ACCESS and the Virtual Engineering Centre (VEC) of Ubrun will support development of the casting upscaling 
lines of UBrun and OGI. They have access and will offer modelling activities, ranging from atomistic simulation of 
materials structures to microstructure predictions to modelling of materials processes and component performance. 
Access e.V and UBrun, have access to high performance computing clusters at their places and will be used for the 
LightMe ecosystem. Specifically, within the LightMe ecosystem, for casting process modelling, the focus will be 
on continuum mechanics based tools: STAR-Cast (jointly developed by Access and Siemens PLM), ProCAST (and 
or MAGMASOFT). Dedicated microstructure modelling based on MICRESS can also be provided to the clients, if 
necessary. The strengths of different software packages will be synergized to provide a wide range of solutions to 
the clients of the ecosystem. Specifically: 
STAR-Cast is based on finite volume method based solver and has been integrated into the c omputational fluid 
dynamics solver (CFD) STAR-CCM+ owned by Siemens PLM. It can address a wide range of thermal and fluid 
dynamic issues and casting defects during the upscaling of casting pilot lines. It uses a fully coupled model, in a 
single set of governing equations, involving all the three phases i.e., gas, melt, solid and solidification and the sharp 
interface between the gas and the liquid phase is modelled based on Volume-of-Fluid model using High-Resolution-
Interface-Capturing (HRIC) scheme, which is the state-of-art in computing multi-fluids with sharp interfaces.  
Nanocomposite Particle Flow:   The behaviour of the nanocomposite particles will be simulated, to investigate 
issues during production process related to inhomogeneous dispersion of rein forcement in the matrix and particle 
agglomeration. This will be incorporated in the casting simulation model mentioned above in STAR-Cast. Broadly 
two different approaches are available. The first one is the Dispersed Multiphase (DiMP) model simulates dispersed 
phases in a Eulerian manner. DiMP can be used as both one -way coupling and two-way coupling: the continuous 
phase influences the dispersed phase particles and vice versa, whenever necessary.  The second one is based on 
Lagrangian numerical methods can be used in conjunction with Eulerian numerical methods to describe situations 
where individual particle dynamics impact the solution on the scale that is resolved in the Eulerian field. Different 
types of NP can be modelled: material particles, massless particles, multi-component particles, and discrete element 
method (DEM) particles. The DEM particles are the most advanced model, which can handle different shapes, sizes, 
types and have the ability to handle inter -particle interaction, leading to particle clustering and break up. The first 
approach can be used in conjunction with the casting process models to aid design the complete casting process. 
The second approach is computationally intensive and restricted by the number of particles used and can be used to 
representatively to optimize particle properties like shape, size under different casting conditions.    
ProCAST simulation software offers an extensive suite of modules and foundry tools to meet the challenging 
industrial requirements. ProCAST software, based on powerful Finite Element Technology, is well suited to predict 
filling and solidification defects, mechanical properties and distortions and residual stresses etc. It provides foundry 
tailored wizards to check and guide users to set -up their casting process. ProCAST also offers advanced analysis 
for microstructure and heat treatment, advanced porosity modelling of shrinkage and gas porosity, also includes a 
gas segregation model along with the proper treatment of solubility limit and pore nucleation. 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 21 of 70] 
 
Built on the similar lines  of ProCAST, software MAGMASOFT based on finite difference method, is a 
comprehensive and effective optimization tool for improving metal casting quality, optimizing process conditions 
and reducing production costs. It is a tool highly popular among the automotive casting industry and can also be 
used to offer as services from Access e.V. to the LightMe clients.  
To summarize, the computational fluid dynamics approach by STAR -Cast, will provide necessary innovation in 
casting processes and especially modelling of nanoparticle flows and understanding its behaviour in casting process. 
ProCAST and or MAGMASOFT, due to their tailor -made tools for foundry industry can used in synergy with 
STAR-Cast to provide quick and predictive design solutions to the clients of LightMe ecosystem.  
 
AM processes modelling and simulation: AM is proven to be able to overcome the main drawbacks of traditional 
subtractive production methods in terms of flexibility and possibility to reproduce complex shapes and undercuts, 
then it is considered a key technology for LightMe project. In the case of metal AM process, the material has to 
pass through a double change of phase for the object to be formed and welded together: it starts from a raw material 
solid phase (e.g., metal wire), and it is subject to local melting (liquid phase) for a brief peri od of transition; 
afterwards, it locally turns back into solid phase. In most of cases, and in particular when manufacturing parts 
require very strict geometrical precision, the high temperature gradients generated during AM induce distortions on 
the fabricated structure, posing difficulties for later assembling processes and generating high contact pressures, 
thus reducing the efficiency of the products (e.g., the efficiency of a mechanical part for automotive applications). 
To mitigate these defects, the most straightforward possibility to find the best operative conditions and 
manufacturing parameters is the trial-and-error approach, where the choice of parameters is based on the experience 
of the single operator and the final result can be modified only repeating the AM process and discarding the defected 
product. Of course, very high costs can be encountered by this approach due to the time and raw material used to 
produce the trial parts. Modelling the AM process via software and simulating the material  behaviour is a 
promising alternative to the expensive and time-consuming trial-and-error method. Thanks to modelling, both 
the thermal and the mechanical behaviour of materials can be predicted, leading to optimize the manufacturing 
parameter before launching the real AM process.  
The approach that LightMe aims to follow starts with the creation of a proper 3D geometry of the part to be produced 
by a CAD/CAE tool (e.g. PTC Creo, SolidWorks, Alibre Design, etc.). Directed Energy Deposition process implies 
a relevant number of parameters, characterized by a wide range of variability and whose correlation has a 
considerable influence on the properties and geometry of the final material and, therefore, the CAD generation as 
well as the selection of the deposition strategy will be supported by the simulation of material transfer, influenced 
by the interaction between feedstock (powder or wire) and the heat source. Also, t he bead shape generated by this 
material transfer determines build rate, needed bead overlap and the local cooling rate of deposited material. In the 
case of a powder feedstock a detailed investigation of two specific process aspects is carried out: 
Particles distribution on the powder jet: the powders leaving the deposition nozzles move along the ejecting direction 
within a gas cone that widens as it moves away from the nozzle itself. The size and the shape of the powder jet is 
of critical importance for the interaction between powders and laser beam. A modelling tool developed by IRIS 
within the OpenFOAM toolbox will provide a CFD simulation describing the behaviour of the multi -material 
powder jet thus ensuring a homogeneous and constant concentration of pre -mixed materials rather than a variable 
and controlled concentration when different materi als are ejected by different nozzles, thus creating in -situ alloys 
and giving internal customized material properties to different parts of the same component. As the NPs  are 
integrated in the powder particles (pre-alloyed), they do not have influence in the powder jet dynamics. 
Interaction between laser and particles: the energy provided by the laser is partially absorbed by the flying particles 
and partially utilized for creating the melt pool. The balance of the powder flow rate , the laser power and process 
speed are the keystone for controlling the internal porosity of the deposited material as well as the surface roughness 
resulting from the AM process. The simulation of the interaction between laser and powder jet will be perfor med 
by using the ESI Additive Manufacturing module in order to identify the optimized parameters for the creation of a 
stable melt pool without internal porosity and characterized by a good surface roughness once solidified. 
While for wire feedstock is a more straightforward study, being the laser absorbed by the wire and partially by the 
substrate. Defect formation is also predicted in relation to the AM process parameters (laser power, processes speed, 
wire speed), in order to understand how/why/where the defects form in the deposited material. In this case, also ESI 
AM module will be used to study the laser -wire interaction and search for optimal parameters and a stable melt 
pool. 
The process parameters resulting from the integration of th e aforementioned simulations will be the starting point 
for the identification of the best deposition strategy, taking into account all the possible issues that can affect the 
final quality of AM process (degree of complexity, part orientation in the printing room, minimum size of details to 
be printed, etc). Once consolidated the geometry, LightMe workflow will foresee to import it into a software tool 
(such as FEMPAR, already used by Stam in the CloudFlow project), where the definition of physical properties and 
the creation of the mesh will be the key passages for the process simulation. Indeed, the material to be simulated 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 22 of 70] 
 
has to be defined through its fundamental properties related to the manufacturing process, such as the melting point 
of the selected metal alloy. On the other hand, meshing operation represents a discretization of the object volume, 
which will be needed to define the spatial path of the AM tool. The shape and size of each element of the mesh 
strongly depend on the requirements of the operator in terms of spatial precision of the information; generally, 
smaller elements are needed in the areas of finest details of geometry, and a higher number of elements requires a 
longer simulation time and computational power to solve the simulation. 
Efficient distortion and residual stress models will be utilized to predict the final shape and as-built residual stresses 
which will later be checked by the use of NDT, as mentioned before. The models will be take account not only the 
process parameters but also sequential change of build direction. The overall component thermal history drives the 
mechanical properties and distortions of built metal components – both are key metrics for manufacturability and 
as-built material quality. Optimisation of build parameters and the thermal distribution will be pursued via parameter 
studies for the development of new components. Results from data analytics will be used to accelerate the physics-
based models and might be used in the form of reduced order models to accelerate optimization loops. 
 
SPS processes modelling and simulation : A coordinated experimental and computational analysis will be 
undertaken to predict the temperature field, heat generation, and stress distribution within a SPS tooling-specimen 
system during single- and multi-part sintering of Ti based components (bearing rings, inserts and oth). For single -
part manufacture, the importance of the die dimensions in relation to punch length and their influence on temperature 
distribution in the pellet were analyzed. The analysis will be performed to propose methods for reducing the overall 
power consumption of the SPS fabrication process by optimizing the dimensions and configurations of tooling for 
simultaneous sintering of multiple parts in each processing cycle.  Moreover, for the multiple part fabrication, the 
optimum spacing between the parts as well as the distance between the die cavities and the outer surface of the die 
wall will be determined for each specific case. It will allow to considerably increase productivity of the SPS process. 
 
The following workflows are provided for the three cases:

ers: ISQ, EWF, PoliMi  
Adherence to standards and regulations helps to ensure safety, reliability and environmental care. Users perceive 
standardized products and services as more dependable – this in turn raises user confidence, increasing sales and 
the take-up of new technologies. A main barrier in terms of regulation and standards is related to the burden and 
uncertainty due to legislation (e.g. REACH) which can put a halt on innovation. Also, there are differences in Europe 
and elsewhere (US, Asia). e.g. multiple region-specific labelling systems with different approaches. This group will 
undertake all necessary consultancy activities in order to guarantee compliance of the new materials and products, 

[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 24 of 70] 
 
including clustering and networking activities with regulatory bodies, identifying standardization issues at proposal 
level and supporting ISO working groups.  
Environment and worker's safety services:  To support industry on the identification of uncertainties and 
potentials risks, a risk management process will be available, for selected test cases and for  clients, following the 
principles and guidelines of the standard ISO 31000 and 31010, which comprises three main phases: establishing 
the context, assessment of risk and risk treatment. Taking into consideration the risk analysis results, HSE 
specifications and recommendations will be defined aiming at risk prevention and control, during product 
processing and handling. The decision of either implementing the measure or assuming to control the risk will be 
based on a cost -benefit analysis, under the responsibility of the partner/clientes developers. Identified risks and 
control parameters to control regarding the industrial process will be included as specifications to be considered for 
the automatic control of the prototypes to be tested at the pilot lines. Communication and consultation with external 
and internal stakeholders should take place during all stages of the risk management process. During the production 
of the pilot line the determination in the indoor air of the concentration of nanoparticles will be offered, based on 
the workflows and needs of the test cases that will be defined, in order to verify the effectiveness of the control 
measures implemented with the aim to eliminate or reduce the exposure to engineered nanomaterials for acceptable 
limits. The equipment that will be used to do this monitoring is capable of measure particle size range between 10 
nm and 420 nm. For the development of this task, the information collecting process from the test case partners and 
(e.g. description and ident ification of the chemical/substances/mixture used, etc., material characterization, 
toxicological profiles, other information deemed appropriate). are paramount and should be provided by the 
partners.  
Consulting services on nanosafety will be available to support industry on the identification of information gaps 
and needs based on the information provided by the clients and according to their innovation development TRL 
taking in consideration current recommendations, guidelines (OECD, WHO, other European and international 
entities) and standards (CEN/TC 352 and ISO/TC229) to support industry to meet regulatory requirements, namely 
REACH and CLP. It is out of the scope of this ecosystem to provide ecotoxicology, toxicology testing and related 
testing services to their clients. Nevertheless, within the task 13.3 liaisons  with nanosafety initiatives and 
infrastructures are envisage to foster the promotion of knowledge exchange and appropriate channels to identify 
external services that can be proposed to the ecosystem clients (on their expenses), if needed. This building block 
will seek liasions with Nanosafety cluster, EC4nano H2020 projects and other nanosafety projects, EPPN, 
NanoFutures, and nanosafety platforms and will used and promote the use by the clients, whenever needed, of data 
repository’s such as the eNanoMapper database, NANoREG Toolbox, DANA, Prosafe, among others.

The introduction and homogeneous distribution of NPs is often problematic. Agglomeration 
arises due to high surface tensions which can be overcome by ultrasound, cover gases and stir 
mixing technologies. These techniques will be combined with well established LPDC, HPDC 
and sand casting techniques. To date there are no large scale high volume processes for

material, since the sintering is carried out inside a high-density graphite die. During LightMe 
initiation phase, an integration of monitoring system will take place together with process 
optimization for lightweight metals.  The study will focus on Ti-SiC, Al-based, Mg-based and 
other composite components SPS manufacturing that  will result in the TRL 7.
