1.3.3 Overall approach and methodology 
The LightMe project will have a duration of 48 months and is divided into the following activities: Management 
(WP 1), R&D&I activities (WP 2 -3), D&I and Demonstration (WP 4-12), Extroversion, Dissemination & 
Exploitation of Ecosystem (WP13-14). The Gantt Chart of the project is depicted in Figure 3.2 at section 3. The 
project will be implemented in three phases as follow: 
 
Phase 1: Set up the structural and operational aspects (WP2, 3). During this phase the LightMe Ecosystem will 
be set up. The building blocks of the ecosystem will be organized while internal and external interactions will b e 
developed. The legal and operational procedures of the Ecosystem will be defined in WP2. Partner TimeLex, as 
a law firm will undertake the necessary legal actions leading to the foundation of a Non for Profit Organization 
that will act as the SEP of the Ecosystem. The exact status of the NPO and the country that will be established will 
be defined in the first period of the project. In parallel, the Ecosystem partners will work to develop the appropriate 
procedures for the  operations of the Ecosystem, the decision-making mechanisms, the internal structures (SEP, 
communication channels) and the external relationships with the clients. Focus will be given in the proper operation 
of the 6 building blocks of LightMe and how these blocks will interact to develop synergies inside the ecosystem. 
Moreover, during this phase the tools of the Ecosystem  will be set up. The core of the Ecosystem are its 6 pilot 
lines. Thus, all necessary upgrades and modifications to the pilot lines will be implemented. Table 1.4 summarizes 
a series of modifications and upgrades that are proposed to take place in the existing pilot lines. In italic fonts the 
expected impact of each modification/upgrade is also given. 
 
Table 1.4: Modification of PLs during the LightMe project

Besides the modification and upgrade of the Pilot Lines, a series of other actions will be undertaken during this 
phase. The building blocks will proceed in all necessary preparatory actions (e.g. upgrade and calibration of testing 
equipment, definition of data basis for modelling/simulation and LCA, updates on similar data basis etc. Finally , 
the internal and external communication tools will be developed. Specific focus will be given in the data 
management (DM) plan. IRES will be responsible for the DM that will be developed the onset of the project DM 
plan, being a key element of efficient data management, will describe the data management life cycle for the data 
that will be collected, processed and generated by LightMe project. Additionally, DM plan will provide information 
about the data created throughout the project including information about "sensitive" data that should be kept 
private. To this, the creation of a document that will be easy to handle, updated and support the nature of being a 
‘living document’ is important for the lifetime of the LightMe project. Moreover, as part of making research data 
findable, accessible, interoperable and re- usable (FAIR), Lightme DM plan will include information on:  1) the 
handling of research data during and after the end of the project, 2)what data will be collected, processed and/or 
generated, 3)which methodology and standards will be applied, 4)whether data will be shared or made open access, 
and 5)how data will be curated and preserved. In addition, the data provided by clients would be added to those 
already produced by the partners of the LightMe project in a win-win situation: the former will gain access to data 
already produced and to the know -how of processes and operations concerning MMnC materials and  the 
latter will be in position to enhance their databases and direct their expertise in order to cover clients' needs. 
Data evaluation and supporting protocols development will be a concurrent activity to materials characterisation 
and modelling. Also, metadata will be used to describe the data of the project, to provide the relationship to other 
information objects and documenting and maintaining data’s relationships. The project will extensively use recent 
European infrastructure for large dataset warehousing (e.g. EuDAT’s B2Drop, OpenAir’s Zenodo and NOMAD). 
Additionally, the project will extend the current ability of these infrastructures with protocol standards and 
additional characterisation-targeted domain-specific metadata. Finally, RDC Informatics will undertake the whole 
IT support of the Ecosystem, including the set up of the Web- platform where clients will be able to apply their 
applications for access to the Ecosystem, the cloud and storage infrastructure.

will be validated. The validation will take place in two parts . During the first part  selected test cases will be 
analysed, targeting to cover and evaluate most of the services that LightMe can offer.

The above diagram (Figure 1.6) presents is details the access of the 8 test cases in the various elements of the 
building blocks of LightMe Ecosystem. It is evident that the performance of all elements of the Ecosystem will be 
validated by at least two end users. Thus, besides the access to pilot lines, characterization, testing, LCA/LCC, 
application of modelling and consultancy in standardization, regulation compliance, nanosafety, training and 
innovation management will be provided to the selected test cases. The eight end users will provide the necessary 
feedback to the Ecosystem (e.g. assessment of communication with the ecosystem and the elements, quality of 
services, adherence to time- schedule and workflows, flexibility, risks identification, final assessment of the 
experience) targeting in the improvement of its services and the internal communication between the elements of 
the LightMe. 
The second part of validation will start at month 26 during which LightMe will proceed in an open call to attract 
additional test cases for access ing free of charge  the ecosystem through the established SEP ( web platform). It is 
intended that 10-15 test cases will be selected based on the assessment of SEP. The selection will be based on the 
evaluation of technical feasibility, market impact and TRL.

of actions promoting extroversion and targeting to its sustainability. Dissemination activities will take place (e.g. 
workshops, participation in fairs, exhibitions & conferences, development of leaflets, posters, videos, establishment 
of LightMe Biannual International Conference ), clustering with other similar projects and initiatives, including 
European standardization bodies and established clusters (e.g. EPPN,  NanoFutures, ECTC, EMMC, EMCC, 
EC4nano, nanosafety cluster) and liaison with stakeholders and possible investors will be planned. Targeting in the 
sustainability of the ecosystem post-project the initial business plan will be continuously updated, focusing on the 
foundation of a non-profit entity that will undertake the management and running of the ecosystem and in attraction 
of potential client.   
 
1.3.4 Considerations on Gender aspects 
The LightMe consortium supports the objectives of the European Commission to promote gender equality in 
research and innovation, as outlined in Article 16 of Horizon 2020. [ 54]. Women’ under-representation in science 
due to the lack of attention to gender aspects constitute a major concern in the EU as stated within the Commission’s 
Action Plan on Science and Society, adopted in 2001 (last modification at 2013). [ 55] Gender aspects have been 
carefully considered within the consortium in order to ascertain that the promotion of gender equality is present in 
as many aspects of the project as possible. Equal opportunities are provisioned for all project activities. In this sense, 
LightMe has foreseen a series of actions to promote the participation of women and to provide equal opportunities

based on gender equality or positive discrimination. [56]
1.4 Ambition 
Towards lightweight metal nanocomposites with enhanced properties 
MMCs with micron -size reinforcements have been used with outstanding success in the automotive, aerospace, 
manufacturing and railway industries, as well as in small engines and other applications. [
57] In the case of MMnCs, 
incorporation of as little as one volume percentage of nanosized ceramics (e.g. SiC, WC, Al2O3, TiO2) has led to a 
much greater increase in the strength of aluminum and magnesium base composites than was achieved at much 
higher loading levels of micron- sized additions. [ 58] Such potential improvements have great implications for 
the automotive and aerospace, and  the defence industries due to the drastic weight savings and exceptional 
properties that can be achieved. Potential aerospace applications may include ventral fins for aircrafts, as well as 
fan exit guide vanes for commercial airline jet engines. Both components require high stiffness and strength, low 
weight as well as resistance to erosion  from rain, airborne particulates and hail. Components used in the 
automotive industry where bulk nanocomposites would likely be valuable include brake system components, which 
require high wear resistance, and thermal conductivity , intake and exhaust valves, which require high creep 
resistance and resistance to sliding wear, as well as piston liners, which require high wear resistance, good 
thermal conductivity and low coefficient of thermal expansion. [ 59] In addition, exceptionally high thermal 
conductivities, possible in selected nanocomposites, will find applications in thermal management applications in 
electronics. MMnCs can be designed to exhibit high thermal conductivity, low density, and matching coefficient 
of thermal expansion with ceramic substrates and semiconductors, making them ideal candidates for such 
applications. [
60] 
 
Advances in simulation, modelling and monitoring for nano-enabled lightweight metals. 
Understanding behavior of NPs in metal matrixes under production conditions is key to avoid inhomogeneous 
dispersion of reinforcement in the matrix and particle agglomeration. The casting process models will be coupled 
to the NPs models, such as dispersed multiphase model and Lagrange particle based models, to investigate, 
nanoparticles behavior in different castings processes. This will offer interesting insights of the dynamics of NPs, 
in liquid state, in mushy state during high, low and normal pressure casting conditions. Hence, specific strategies 
will be derived for each casting processes to avoid these defects.  Discrete element based modelling will be used on 
representative number of particles with shape, size and different types, to understand inter-particle behavior under 
different flow conditions leading to agglomeration.  In addition to the above mentioned, STAR -cast being a fully 
coupled and highly precise multi-fluid solver (HRIC) with the capability to handle highly compressible gas phase 
(~1000 Bar in HPDC), will provide interesting insights into air entrainment defects and complex dynamics of fluid 
flow involving NPs. The melt pool generation study will be used also as a starting point for the determination of 
nanoparticle distribution in the metal matrix, using a simplification of the casting simulation model described above, 
in order to investigate the issues related to inhomogeneous dispersion of reinforcement in the matrix for AM.  
On the other hand, the challenge to progress beyond the state of the art in monitoring will be to effectively implement 
technologies for inline process monitoring. This will require the design of compact, high numerical aperture optics 
to capture the maximum number of orders possible. Similar optical systems have been used to apply sub-wavelength 
optical diffraction metrology [
61,62] to characterise structures as small as 50nm in periodic patterns . Variations of 
the basic system may be developed, having adjusted light sources and optics to the resolution and spot size needed, 
and for compatibility with flat surfaces and non flat surfaces. These will be integrated in the related production lines 
to provide dimensional information on the structures in real time. Resulting data can be used to feed the processing 
models where appropriate. 
 
Innovation potential of LightMe for SMEs and Industry in the field of lightweight MMCs 
LightMe Ecosystem main innovation lays on the creation of a safe and neutral environment for start-ups, SMEs 
and industry to access facilities and manufacturing services for small series production if lightweight MMCs 
and thus, project with accuracy the cost and performance of such processes in the industrial scale. The test 
bed in this sense will provide ultimately also an estimate of what could be the projection of the manufacturing cost 
at full scale. Certainly,  the potential clients of the Ecosystem needs to know if their materials/products concepts

Innovation potential of LightMe Ecosystem in the level of operation 
LightMe is a one -stop- shop offering all the services needed to make commercial applications, based on open 
technological infrastructures, crucial to the technology maturation. It has been decided that the Ecosystem will be 
represented by a Non-for-Profit Organization acting as the Single Entry Point. The NPO will be established in 
month 20 of the project and will have the mandate to represent the ecosystem, closing agreements and signing 
contracts with the potential customers, being in accordance with national and EC regulations . Th us, the 
administrative burden for the customers will be minimum as they will come in contact only with the NPO structure.  
The main services that will boost the innovation capacity of the ecosystem are (A) technological services: providing 
access to expert ise, technology, and infrastructures, including manufacturing and product development. This 
includes for instance: collaborative RD&I, technical support on scale- up, commercial infrastructure, testing and 
validation, etc., (B) ecosystem services: developing and driving open innovation ecosystems with strong 
cooperation between research and industry and good connections between users and suppliers of innovations across 
the value -chain. This includes for instance: dissemination of information, innovation strategy development, 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 32 of 70] 
 
brokerage, inter- collaboration, etc. and (C) business-oriented services: supporting businesses to commercially 
apply these innovations and transform their business, including access to financing and investors. This includes for 
instance: incubator/accelerator support, access to finance, business/market intelligence, etc. Innovation management 
in the open innovation environment will enhance information sharing and diffusion of expertise for all actors 
involved to increase the chances of success, lower risks, and reduce costs. To achieve these objectives and ensure 
technology uptake, both technological and non- technological services are crucially compulsory

2. Impact 
The target of the LightMe proposal is to set up and operate a fully sustainable ecosystem  related to the 
upscaling of materials and products of lightweight metal matrix composites. The Ecosystem will be represented by 
a Non Profit Organization (NPO) that will be founded in Month 20 of the project and will act as the Single Entry 
Point. The NPO will have the mandate by the members of the Ecosystem to sign contracts . Via an amendment the 
NPO will be proposed to be a partner of the consortium. The core partners of the ecosystem have divided the 
development on the ecosystem in two pillars: Excellence and Sustainability. While in the section 1 the Excellence 
of the Ecosystem has been described, in this section the Sustainability of the LightMe Ecosystem will be 
demonstrated.
2.1 Expected impacts  
Open and upgraded facilities at the EU level … easily accessible to users across different regions of Europe;  
LightMe ecosystem will provide open access to industrial partners, including SMEs to PL related to casting, AM 
and SPS as well as to advance characterization techniques, modelling & simulation software, environmental 
assessment and consultancy on standardization and regulatory aspects (including nanosafety) for upscaling 
concepts related to lightweight metal matrix nanocomposites. The pilot lines are situated in 5 European countries 
(Austria, UK, Spain, Italy and Poland) during the first phase of the project the core partners of the ecosystem will 
proceed in all necessary modification and upgrades in order to be able to efficiently integrate a wide range of 
nanoparticles and to control and monitor the corresponding processes. The application for access will be done 
through a special designed web-platform (SEP) that will be supported by a group of experts as des cribed in the 
business plan above providing fast and reliable assessment to clients and setting up dedicated workflows. 
Attract a significant number of new SME users, … or in applications using them;  
SMEs play a fundamental role in investment and innovation in Europe. Despite macroeconomic challenges such 
as weak domestic demand, difficult access to finance and lingering economic uncertainty, they continue to be an 
essential part of the productive sector. Besides globalisation, SMEs face a number of other  challenges such as 
increasing digitalisation, rising energy prices and competition from non-
European, low labor cost countries, 
which require sensible investment and innovation strategies. LightMe  ecosystem will cover this need offering 
an open access innovation environment, in which SME will be able to proceed in technological innovation in a 
fast and low cost way. These decrease cost of innovation, compared to other existing alternatives (e.g. in-house 
research, customer-seller collaboration with individual RTOs) lays on the synergies that are developed inside the 
ecosystem, knowledge and good practice experience, as well as higher chances of commercialization and 
adoption of new products by the market due to the presence of important players from releva nt fields (large 
automotive and aerospace industries). These advantages makes LightMe  ecosystem extremely attractive for 
SMEs that are ready to innovate. The initial business plan below, shows the expected impact on European 
industry. 
At least 15% improved industrial process parameters and 20% faster verification of materials performance for 
highly promising applications; 
Currently the daily production optimization is manually performed based on the experience of the human 
operators controlling the production process. This is a highly complex task, where a large number of controllable 
parameters all affect the production in some way and must be adjusted to find the best combination. The process 
control systems to be developed within LightMe  will overcome this issue, by developing a data driven models 
based approach, which can largely improve the process efficiency, allowing to find complex, non-linear patterns 
in data, and transform them into models, which can be applied to fine- tune the process parameters, improving 
them by at least 20%, while strongly improving the quality of products [
63,64]. This will have a very strong impact 
on the customers that will access the LightMe ecosystem, as they will be able to strongly improve the quality of 
their products through optimized production processes. 
In more details the above targets will be achieve: 
In terms of the casting pilot lines (LPDC, HPDC, GSC) the following modification and additions will be carried 
our leading to an improver industrial process parameters. 
• Installment of ultrasound for large volume application 
• Development and optimization of tips for the sonotrode 
• Investigations of ceramic and Niobium tips 
• Comparative assessment 
• Comparison of the competitiveness of life time of both materials 
 
63 T. Hill, Exec. Director Analytics, “Machine Learning Techniques in Manufacturing, Applications & Caveats”, DELL, 2016. 
64 T. Wuest et al., “Machine learning in manufacturing: advantages, challenges, and applications”, Production & Manufacturing Rese arch, 
pagg. 23-45, Vol. 4, Issue 1, 2016. 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 34 of 70] 
 
• System for relative movement of the US equipment  
• Combination of rotary degassing and US treatment  
 
In terms of WLAM pilot line, the deployed approach will be based on a knowledge DB and procedure to populate 
it. All MMnCs’ process development tests will be based on a standardized DoE for process window development 
and the validation of the process parameters by ISO standardized test artefacts. All the test results will be stored 
in a DB which will serve for incremental process development for new materials, based on previous developments 
stored in the DB. This will ensure that the adoption of new MMnC for WLAM will take most of the previous 
developments (not only good but also bad tests) and reduce the process development time and verification of 
material performance for each material up to two weeks (from the previous 10 -12 weeks). The improvement of 
the industrial process parameters, on the other hand will be ensured by the adoption of te inline monitoring and 
control system and, in the case of WLAM, a cybersecured digital thread in which the material development tests 
are used for training of the deep learning models which will increase even more the fidelity of the process 
window. 
Overall for the two main categories of Pilot Lines (casting, additive manufacturing and SPS-KOBO) we have: 
Casting methods 
The Low Pressure Die Casting, High Pressure Die Casting and the Green Sand Casting pilot lines have some 
common features, all dealing with the most common casting techniques and their key process parameters. In 
particular, the performance improving will be achieved by the study of working temperature during die casting, 
working pressure, cooling time and cooling element (e.g., temperature and circulating speed, in case of a cooling 
fluid is used). Moreover, the results to be achieved are correlated with the good distribution of NPs within the 
casting alloys, the presence of deleterious reaction products and the reduction of waste at the end of the process, 
the low porosity grade and the absence of particle agglomeration. Input and output parameters will be correlated 
to each other within the data -
driven model to be built, in order to fully understand the values for the process 
parameters which optimize the material performances. 
Additive Manufacturing and SPS 
Metal Wire Additive Manufacturing, Borealis and Sp ark Plasma Sintering deal with different production 
methods, mainly based on the phase change of metals. In particular, here the key process parameters to be 
monitored and closed-loop controlled are the laser power and temperature, the chamber temperature, the moving 
speed of the AM end effector, the part orientation (form the AM PL), the sintering pressure (for the SPS), the 
external die temperature (for the SPS). 
For both the categories of Pilot Lines, the real time measurement of the input and output data to update the model 
will be ensured by the proper choice and installation of sensors (e.g., thermocouples, pressure meters, encoders), 
data storage, analysis and monitoring systems, and the update of the data -driven model will be aimed at setting 
the process key parameters to reach the performance improvement by the aimed percentage. 
 
At least 20% improvement in industrial productivity, reliability, environmental performance, durability, and 
reduction of life-cycle costs of these materials; 
Optimization of the production process will be performed via a machine learning based control approach, 
developing models to link the key process parameters with the final properties, durability and environmental 
performance of the new materials, thus allowing the identification of the best combination of process parameters 
able to optimize the characteristics of the materials. Data driven models  based control, combined with fast 
characterization methods, will allow better error tracking, increase production rate and equipment lifetime, reduce 
scrap, production and life-cycle costs. Machine learning has in fact already demonstrated to be able to increase 
production capacity by 20%, while lowering material consumption rates by 4% and downtime by 20% [
65]. The 
potential impact on the customers of LightMe  will be huge, as they will have access to an ecosystem able to 
maximize the performances of their products, while ensuring high industrial productivity. 
At least 15% indirect reduction in energy consumption across sectors using lighter materials in their products 
and processes 
Advanced materials are essential for boosting the fuel economy of modern automobiles while maintaining safety 
and performance. A 10% reduction in vehicle weight can result in a 6%- 8% fuel economy improvement . 
[66] Taking as example the automotive industry, the strength of Al sheet panels is approximately same as that of 
steel body panel, while its density is the 1/3 of steel. Its lower stiffness can be improved with the integration of 
NPs and thus, main steel parts of cars can by replaced by Al MMnCs. Mg is 33% lighter than Al and 75% lighter 
than steel. Taking into account the overall mass of an average car, use extended use of Al and Mg nanocomposites 
 
65 Forbes, “10 Ways Machine Learning Is Revolutionizing Manufacturing”, 2016. 
66 S. Wenlong et al “Analysis of Energy Saving of Vehicles Using Light Weight Materials”, Procedia, 88 (2016) 880 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 35 of 70] 
 
can lead to a reduction of ~30% in the mass and consequently to ~20% of energy consumption. Similarly, other 
important sectors of transportation (aviation and rails) can have significant positive environmental impact.  
 
Other impacts in European Industry, Economy and Society 
Environmental impact 
A major positive environmental impact has been already analysed in the expected impacts and is related with the 
reduction of energy consumption in the transportation sector due to the use of lightweight materials in cars, 
airplanes and other systems. Howev er, it is expected that also other positive environmental impacts will resulted 
from the activities undertaken by the LightMe project. More specifically: 
- Increase of yields in manufacturing processes. During the LightMe project, and especially in the first phase 
of it, process monitoring and process control systems will be integrated in the PL (Table 1.3 of section 1).  
- Materials saving. Optimized closed loop control (for all PL) and optimization of powder management and 
recycling systems (e.g. for the Borealis PL  [ 67]) will lead to decrease of fault batches and will enable the 
recovery of unused material. 
- Shift to more sustainable tools in the production lines . GSC PL will operate with new organica lly and/or 
inorganically environmental friendly bonding system (e.g. vegetable polyurethane resin) while SPS-KOBO PL 
will develop new die tools made of graphite and ceramic materials that will have as result the increase of dies 
life. Such innovation will lead to greener production methods. 
Occupational Health Impact 
Occupational Health and Safety is of crucial importance for the LightMe . Having identified possible occupation 
risks, the LightMe partners have already projected the necessary contingency plans for eliminating this risk. A series 
of measurements will be taken (e.g. use of cover gases for prevention of deleterious reactions products in the casting 
and AM lines) while ISQ will proceed in a thorough risk assessment of the Pilot Lines during the first stage of the 
project providing recommendations and H&S measurements, including aspects related to the handling of NP.  
Socio-Economic impact – Jobs creation 
Ecosystems need appropriate staffing to become sustainable. The process of opening up and further developing 
access to existing and new industrial infrastructures requires careful management, investment s and high expertise 
stuff. Integrated successful Ecosystem activities will lead to the creation of job vacancies of high level technical, 
scientific, managerial, organisational and marketing personnel in the members of the Ecosystem and the NPO. On 
the other hand, successful outcome of the test cases accessing the Ecosystem services will lead to a significant 
growth of the corresponding companies  (including SMEs) as they will bring to the market novel and sustainable 
products and materials. Based on the preliminary business plans carried out for the Ecosystem and the selected test 
cases it is evident that an important revenue will be created, leading to the creation of new high expertise jobs. More 
specifically it is projected that ~260 jobs will be created for the members of the Ecosystem 5 years after project’s 
finalization and more than ~140 new jobs for the partners accessing the Ecosystem.  Extrapolating this to the new 
client cases that will access to Ecosystem, it is expected that the LightMe ecosystem will result in more than 900 
new jobs in the wider field of lightweight MMC (materials providers, end users, research etc) in Europe.    
 
Barriers to achieve the impact of LightMe project 
It is evident that although the last two decades a high number of research projects has been dedicated in the 
development of new lightweight MMcC (e.g. according to Scopus, more than 1000 publications concern this field 
in the last 5 years) , only a very limited number of such cases has been finally commercialized and reached the 
market. There are many reasons that these concepts have not been adopted by the market and this phenomenon is 
usually described as ‘valley of death ’. Table 2.2 shows the plan of the LightMe  ecosystem for overcoming the 
upscaling and market adoption barriers though its services that will be provided to SMEs and Large Industry. 
 
Table 2.2: Mitigation plans of LightMe for overcoming barriers for upscaling of materials concept 
Barrier 1: Lack of available infrastructures 
Pilot Lines are essential for upscaling materials concepts. Through them, laboratory results can be transferred to 
pre-industrial level by developing robust production technologies. However, such lines are not always available 
to companies since their acqu isition cost is high, needs extra expertise in monitoring and control of lines, and 
SMEs are not eager to proceed in such investments unless they can decrease the risk. On the other hand, large 
industries, are not eager to stop their production lines to ca rry out tests for upscaling of new materials and 
products. LightMe ecosystem will provide a variety of flexible upscaling processes (e.g. casting techniques, 
additive manufacturing, sintering) for testing, monitoring and process optimization of production of the new 
materials 
Barrier 2: Need of expertise in characterization and evaluation of results 
 
67 http://www.borealisproject.eu/wp-content/uploads/2015/05/Borealis_brochure.pdf  
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 36 of 70] 
 
Characterization of materials and evaluation of the corresponding results is essential for the development and 
upscaling of new products. However, it is a common remark that this expertise exists mainly in universities and 
research centers. Access to such characterization facilities might be proven futile if it is not a part of a scheduled 
innovative plan. LightMe experts will provide technological, scientific and manufacturing expertise; advance, 
accurate and fast characterization methods for the novel developed materials, combined with advanced modelling 
techniques linking the crucial parameters of production steps with the final properties, lifetime and environmental 
impact of the new materials.  
Barrier 3: Industry needs standardized and validated solutions  
A lot of highly promising innovative ideas often remain in the laboratory as they are not linked with standards 
and regulatory frameworks. Especially, when it comes to materials containing NPs issues such as nanosafety are 
becoming a major barrier as the regulatory framework has not been yet assimilated by the industry. Indeed, end 
users, especially in the fields of aerospace and automotive industry will ignore products that are not harmonized 
with the latest standards. LightMe ecosystem will provide all the necessary services and activities related to 
standardization, compliance with existing regulatory framework and safety/nanosafety/standardization aspects of 
the materials to be upscaled. 
Barrier 4: High perceived risk for investors 
Even the most promising ideas and concepts will probably need extra funding until they come to the market. 
Most often, SMEs cannot afford to invest on their own additional  funds, while investors are reluctant to invest 
without securing the previous mentioned aspects (e.g. compliance with standards of the new materials, lifetime, 
performance). Inside the LightMe ecosystem proper conditions for bridging investors with SMEs  
will be 
provided. Thus, activities, such as translation of knowledge of discoveries developed usually in the academic 
community, in a context that is relevant to the industry investors will take place. Already 5 investing groups have 
express interest in the LightMe (Annex I) 
 
Public acceptance 
Enterprises are aware of their customers’ scepticism about adoption of new technologies and more specifically 
nanotechnologies. Main concerns of customers are on the nature of the materials, their functionality and 
applicability, their performance, their sustainability and naturally, on their cost. LightMe Ecosystem will work on 
the direction of public acceptance focusing on activities that they will lift nano- safety concerns, prove their 
functionality and appliance trough demonstration activities, certify their high performance and enhanced properties 
through standard testing results, explain the high sustainability achieved for both materials and products through 
LCA, contrast their high performance and multifunctionality to their initial production cost, etc. Planned 
dissemination and communication activities (see next paragraphs) will be followed to achieve the above scope. 
Industry acceptance – Investment interest 
Industry is constantly seeking more sustainable methods in the production of materials with enhanced properties 
or multifunctionality in order to widely satisfy the demands of end users. Multiple actions are expected to raise the 
investment interest of the industry: dissemination of the standard testing results; feasibility studies on the techno – 
economic aspects of the materials production and usage.
2.2 Measures to maximize impacts  
LightMe project will address all issues related to exploitation, business development, innovation management, 
management of IP, data management as well as dissemination and communication activities. The dissemination and 
exploitation of the project’s results as well as the management of knowledge and intellectual property are considered 
as critical issues for the success of the project. A Dissemination and Exploitation plan, including a business strategy, 
plan and model, has been already developed and will be constantly updated so that it encompasses all the progress 
that is made during the project. Finally, communication activities strategy has already been projected with input 
from all partners and will be updated during the project. Further analysis is provided in the following subsections. 
 
2.2.1 Plan for the Dissemination and Exploitation of the project results 
A. Dissemination activities 
The dissemination activities will begin with the initiation  of the project at month 1. The dissemination plan is 
designed to reach the largest audience possible and to inform EU stakeholders about the LightMe  project’s 
objectives and results. Dissemination activities aim at paving the way towards the future market penetration of 
LightMe solution and to ensure the successful exploitation of the project outputs (see 2.2.1B paragraph). Moreover, 
they will promote the project’s approach and to encourage interested stakeholders to adopt the solution developed. 
The major aim is to ensure that the project’s outcomes are widely disseminated to the appropriate target groups, at 
appropriate times (respecting the proposed project timeline), via appropriate methods (mean of information 
disclosure, intensity, etc.). For a successful dissemination all LightMe beneficiaries will cooperate in order to create 
higher added values at the market. With such an approach, LightMe PEDR (Plan for Exploitation & Dissemination 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 37 of 70] 
 
of Results) will foster cross -border and cross-sectorial cooperation between the members of the consortium  with 
the final goal to attract new customers to the LightMe ecosystem. All along project duration tactical, strategic and 
operative elements of promotion, exploitation of results and awareness raising will be actively employed and will 
ensure capturing of a large audience, in an appropriate manner and hence ensure long- term sustainability of the 
project results and the established NPO. For an effective public outreach both standard dissemination activities, 
dedicated to public information, and more targeted engagement activities, where dialogue (communication) and 
alliances is created, dynamically co-exist. A draft Communication & Dissemination Roadmap has already been 
developed (Figure 2.1) and will be updated frequently during the implementation of the project. Based on the 
dissemination road map adequate indicators (Dissemination KPIs) to measure the impact of the dissemination 
carried out are also shown (see Table 2.1).

players representing LightMe value chain that can take advantage of their network of contacts to raise awareness.

of the ecosystem: 1) European Start-ups, SME, and Midcap communities: Companies (tech and non-tech) interested 
in understanding the potential of lightweight metals. 2) Regional innovation networks and accelerators: Existing 
innovation hubs interested in expanding existing local support to European cross -border support. 3) Design 
experiment stakeholders: Owners of products and services, platform providers, inventors, R&D entities. 4) LightMe 
cross border community: Participants in other projects in the call. 5) Policy makers: Entities in charge of funding 
programmes. 6) Broader innovation community: interested in the best practices for the advance of the EU sector. 7) 
Investor: VC, Angels, Crowd funding platforms, Bank looking for innovative companies interested in embedding 
new innovative components in their products and services.  8) End users in the fields of automotive, aerospace and 
transportation sector and other associated sectors were technologies can be applied, 9) High technology SMEs 
interested in upscaling new materials and starting new business models.

designed and will be updated on a regular basis. The plan will identify information about events important for the

among three main target audiences: stakeholders/end users, research experts and the wider public. For a maximum

Data management Plan 
The Data Management Plan (DMP) will be developed already from the first months of the project implementation 
by the consortium. The DMP will be updated at least by the mid-t erm and final review to fine- tune it to the data 
generated and the uses identified by the consortium since not all data or potential uses are clear from the start. New 
versions of the DMP will be created whenever important changes to the project occur due to inclusion of new data 
sets, changes in consortium policies or external factors. A description of the data that will be generated or collected 
will be given, as well as information about its origin, nature and scale and to whom it could be useful. The extension 
and depth of the information given depends on the grant and consortium agreement. The methodology and standards, 
whether and how this data will be shared and/or made open, and how it will be curated and preserved will be decided 
by the consortium during project implementation.  
The DMP will follow the below basic steps: 
 Data set reference and name: identifier for the produced data 
 Data set description: description, nature, scale, information about integration and reuse etc. 
 Standards and metadata: reference to the standards that will be used and how the metadata will be created 
 Data sharing: access procedures, software or other tools needed for access, repository, reasons for confidential 
data Archiving and preservation: procedures for the long-term preservation of the data, estimated end volume 
B. Exploitation activities 
The most important exploitable result of the project is the LightMe Ecosystem itself. Thus, the consortium has 
worked and developed a preliminary exploitation plan for the Ecosystem, based on a draft business plan. In the next 
paragraphs, the business plan of the LightMe ecosystem is presented along with the exploitation of the other 
individuals results of the project. 
 
Exploitation plan for the LightMe Ecosystem & Business Plan 
As the Ecosystem will be represented by the NPO the following business plan, concerns this legal entity. 
1. Value proposition and role of the LightMe Ecosystem 
LightMe Ecosystem value proposition is the operation of a new, open innovation ecosystem targeting in the 
upscaling of lightweight metal and metal alloy composites materials and products . This will be achieved via 
the collaboration of high expertise groups across Europe in the fields of lightweight metal processing and 
manufacturing, monitoring, testing, characterization, modelling, environmental assessment, standardization, 
nanosafety, innovation management and training. The detailed presentation of the ecosystem services has been in 
details described in section 1 (paragraph 1.3.) LightMe Ecosystem will provide state of the art services to SMEs, 
midcaps, large industries and academia  interested in developing new applications and products for the 
transportation sector and other fields in which lightweight metal products find applicatio ns, by means of 
improving metal alloys' properties and providing sustainable production processes. Moreover, having the legal 
status of NPO will act as a Pan-European association, serving the interests of its members regarding the field of 
lightweight metals and alloy composites. 
The following figure presents the CANVAS business model that have been scheduled. 
 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 40 of 70] 
 
 
Figure 2.2: LightMe CANVAS business model 
 
2. Management and organization of Ecosystem 
The members of the LightMe ecosystem have already decided that the most efficient way for the proper 
representation and operation of the Ecosystem is to establish a non-for profit organization (NPO). The NPO will 
undertake the whole administrative, financial and legal issues of the Ecosystem (e.g. marketing, access to additional 
funding, contracts with customers, secretarial and administrative tasks, etc) and will be the Single Entry Point 
“SEP” of the Ecosystem. As mentioned, t he NPO will be founded at Month 20 of the project . The proposed 
structure of the NPO is organized as follows: 
 The Board, consisting of 17 members (one person from each organization - PoliMI, ACCESS, AIMEN, Axia, 
EWF, INOP, IRES, IRIS, ISQ, OGI , RDC, INCOTEC, Stam, TimeL, UBRUN, ICCRAM, Iris Tech) that will 
be the supreme authority of the NPO and will be responsible for the preparation of all strategy and policy matters 
of the NPO. The Board will be chaired by the president (elected by the board), that will have a 3 years’ service 
having the right to re-elect for another term.  
 The Executive Manager (EM), will run the NPO and will be responsible to the Board for the execution of its 
decisions and the financial issues of the organization. 
 Secretariat Office, that will be staffed with employees of the NPO. 
 Working Groups (WG). The WG will be linked with the six building blocks of the Ecosystem. Initially the 
WG will be staffed by experts of the members of the ecosystem based on t arget and mission of each working 
group. The responsibilities of the WG will be: 
o To provide an initial assessment of the feasibility of the customers’ test cases for accessing the ecosystem 
and proceed  
o To develop the necessary workflows for each test case. 
o To proceed in clustering activities with similar open innovation test beds and other pan-European initiatives 
for creation of synergies.  
 
With the progress of time the WG will include high 
expertise employees hired by the NPO. The target is that 
the fourth year after the establishment of the NPO 
(second year after the project finalization) the WG will 
be exclusively staffed by employees of the NPO, while a 
close collaboration with the experts of the members will be 
maintained. 
 
3. Operational Plan  

[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 41 of 70] 
 
The major aspects governing the operation of the NPO and all individual relationships with the members of the 
LightMe ecosystem as well as the clients are presented below and will be finalized within WP2. 
Agreement between NPO and LightMe ecosystem members. 
The NPO will act as the SEP between potential end users and the LightMe Ecosystem, in order to facilitate the 
negotiation of the services and accelerate the adoption of the LightMe technologies to the market. Thus, it is essential 
the NPO to have already an established joint agreement and collaboration protocols with the members of the 
Ecosystem. First of all,  the LightMe members – pilot owners, technology partners (e.g. predictive modelling, 
process monitoring, characterization) and other service providers (e.g. standardization, innovation management, 
LCA, training etc.) will sign a Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) and a Dealer Agreement  (DA) with the 
NPO in order to fix the terms of collaboration. The Dealer Agreement will form the contractual framework for 
the provision of the LightMe services via the Ecosystem. The Dealer Agreement will provide the additional 
details of each Pilot Line and the services offered by the LightMe Ecosystem. Either Party to this Agreement may 
– with the mutual agreement of the respective other party – amend or add information to the pilot/services covered 
by the Dealer Agreement and also add new Pilot/services sheets. New pilot/services will be welcome, provided that 
the terms and conditions set forth in each new Pilot/service sheet do not contradict those of the Agreement. The 
NPO will become the SEP upon the Dealer Agreement coming into force. The NPO will commercialize the services 
offered by the LightMe Ecosystem in accordance with the terms and conditions of the Agreement. 
Agreement between NPO and customers of LightMe ecosystem. 
Access to the LightMe Pilot/services by the end users will be based on the End-user Terms of Use (ETU), which 
the NPO will conclude with each individual customer. The Term of Uses will include: 
 The NPO provides the access to Pilots and services to properly registered users via an online platform within the 
scope of a technology services solution. 
 The services are provided to the User against payment of a fee, agreed with the actual service provider members 
of the LightMe Ecosystem, for the duration of its use (“pay- per-use” business model). Regulations governing 
remuneration will be detailed during the project. 
 The access to Pilots and services available on the Ecosystem is usually third -party service to which the NPO 
merely provides access. The use of Pilot/services may be subject to deviating or additional regulations (e.g. due 
to national regulations), which the NPO will point out to the User prior to use. 
 The NPO reserves the right to improve, adapt or modify the online platform in terms of content and/or structure. 
For example, the NPO may modify or discontinue some services, make available new ones, and modify or extend 
the user interface of the online platform. In doing so, the NPO will consider the User’s legitimate interests. 
 The NPO will also offer a customer support service thought the web platform . Also options for “after  sales” 
services will be projected on the End-User Terms of Use agreement. 
The NPO shall ensure that all end users intending to have access on the Pilot/services accept the End-user Terms of 
Use. For the valid lifetime of this Agreement, the NPO shall make appropriate updated versions of Pilot Lines 
technologies available from time to time, when the usage rights change, or new jurisdictions require an update. The 
Customer may only reject the use of updated versions, where legitimate interests justify this. 
 
Operational procedures for accessing the Ecosystem 
Clients will apply for access to the Ecosystem through the dedicated web platform operated by the NPO who acts 
as the SEP. Awareness of potential customers concerning the services of the Ecosystem will be done through various 
channels, while access to the Ecosystem in order to understand the potentiality of the pilot lines and other services 
will be free of charge for the users/customers. The procedure for accessing the ecosystem will be the following: 
 The customer/end user make an application in a non -confidential form via the web -platform of the SEP. The 
application concerns the completion of a questionnaire consists of closed and open type questions.  
 The application is assessed by the SEP and the customer is contacted. An NDA is signed between the SEP and 
the customer and more conventional details of the concept are provided as well as of the required services.  
 The SEP in collaboration with the WG are setting up an offer  including the technical workflow based on the 
needs of the customer, a detailed cost estimation of the services described in the workflow and the handling of 
new IPRs. 
 Upon the approval of the offer by the client, a contract agreement between the NPO and the customer is signed, 
while the agreement between NPO and members of the ecosystem is activated and thus the ecosystem is working 
on the project based on the contractual obligations of its members.  
Finally, it is important to refer on the decision-making procedures of the Ecosystem that will be defined during 
the first period of the project and will include the following main aspects: 
 Evaluation of test cases and translation of the customers’ needs to be based on characterization workflows. This 
will be carried out by the WG in collaboration with the potential customers and the group managers. 
 Pricing of ecosystem services. The members of LightMe  are committed to provide their services at fair prices 
and thus, competitive offers will be given to the customers. It is expected that due to the synergies that will be 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 42 of 70] 
 
developed in the ecosystem leading to a one stop shop , the total revenues that will be created will be higher 
compared to the sum of the revenues that each partner can create on its own (economy of scales). 
 Internal conflict mechanism resolutions will be developed for possible conflicts inside the ecosystem. 
 Intellectual property issues and confidentiality aspects will be arranged between the LightMe and the clients 
NPO acting as Association in the field of Lightweight MMC and advance materials 
Under this function the NPO will have the right to register associated members across Europe upon annual fees. 
The associated members can be SME, start ups, large enterprises, research institutes, other stakeholders and 
investors. Thus, around the Ecosystem a community of stakeholders will be created. The members of this association 
will enjoy privileges such as reduced fees or free access for conferences, workshops and training events, free access 
to the Association Journals, updates and introduction in new technologies, liaison and visits to the facilities of the 
members of the Ecosystem. The target of this community is to bring in contact stakeholders across value chains and 
provide a safe environment for open innovation practices.  
 
4. Market segmentation, size & needs 
One of the main factors that affect the vehicle energy consumption is the weight. Lighter vehicles consume less 
fuel, emit less harmful gases and provide a better performance. Lightweight materials have become increa singly 
critical for producing components for aircrafts, cars, trains, ships, and defence equipment. Especially, lightweight 
metal and alloys possess high strength-to-weight ratios and low density. [
68] 
Common applications are met in the automotive, aerospace, manufacturing, railway and other large niche 
or even everyday applications . For example, r ising awareness about fuel emissions has led to automobile 
manufacturers turning to products that can reduce the weight of vehicles. In the case of cars, for instance, a 10% 
reduction in vehicle weight is estimated to result in a 6 to 8 % fuel economy improvement  [ 69]. The use of 
lightweight materials such as magnesium (Mg) alloys, aluminum (Al) alloys, carbon fiber instead of traditional steel 
components, can reduce the weight of the vehicle by up to 50 %, having a direct impact on the reduction of the fuel 
consumption. 
LightMe Ecosystem will focus in the production of new lightweight metals in the Aeronautic and automotive 
sectors, which are the following: aluminum, magnesium, and titanium alloys.  
 
Market and environmental benefits of lightweight metals and alloys 
The global lightweight materials market size is expected to reach 225.3 billion € by 2024 [
70], exhibiting a CAGR 
of 8.9% during the forecast period. This growth is consequence of the increasing demand for lightweight materials 
in transport and energy sector industries such as automotive, aerospace and wind energy. In 2015, the automotive 
segment dominated the overall market in terms of revenue, with an 86% share. Rising awareness about fuel 
emissions has led to manufacturers using lighter components in vehicle design to improve mileage. Moreover, rising 
material innovation in aviation is expected to improve demand for lightweight materials. In the automotive sector, 
the lightweight materials market represented €126.18 bn in 2015 and it is expected to reach €255.17 bn by the end 
of 2024, with a CAGR of 8.36% during the forecast period [
71]. The li ghtweight metals that will experiment the 
major growth, leaving aside the high strength steel are the aluminium, titanium and magnesium.

market share by application for 2016 
 
More analytical data market, concerning the metal of interest are presented below:

Aluminium: Transport sector consumes almost 40% of the Al  production in Europe . The global Al  market was 
value at 133,564 million euro in 2015 and is expected to reach 167,277 million euro by 2022, registering a CARG 
of 3.3% from 2016 to 2020. The annual turnover of the European Al  industry accounts for 38 billion EUR, so the 
share of the transport section can be estimated at 14,82 bn €. Aluminium makes up 75-80% of a modern aircraft and 
it is the second most used material in vehicles, only behind the steel. Currently, the average Al content per vehicle 
produced is around 150.6 kg/vehicle, and it is foreseen to reach nearly 200 kg per vehicle by 2025 [73].  
Magnesium: the magnesium alloys  market is estimated at 1.30 billion euro in 2018 and is projected to reach 
USD2.37 billion by 2023 with a forecast to grow at a CAGR of 10.1% from 2015 to 2020 [74]. The metal magnesium 
market is expected to grow substantially owing to its use in the aerospace industry pertaining to the rising need for 
fuel efficiency and reducing weight of an aircraft. Moreover, increasing demand from automotive industry is 
expected to fuel the market owing to the rapid growth in the automotive sector mainly in China, India and Mexico. 
Titanium: Ti metal market size to maintain the average annual growth rate of 2.82% from 11500 million euro in 
2014 to 1250 million euro in 2017. The analysts believe that by 2022, the market size of the Ti  metal will reach 
1350 million euro [75]. Aerospace Ti market is forecast to grow at a CARG of 3.3% by value from 2015 to 2020. 
Market overview based on application 
Automotive: The global automotive metal market size was worth ~72 billion euro in 2016. [
76] Growing demand 
for vehicles coupled with abundant raw material availability are the key factors for the growth globally. The sector 
has been witnessing significant development in terms of materials as well as technologies used for manufacturing 
of vehicle components. Stringent fuel efficiency regulations  have facilitated R&D to develop lightweight & cost-
effective materials for the automotive sector. Moreover, new technologies including 3D printing are being utilized 
for the manufacturing of large metal parts. Al and Mg are the fastest growing materials in the automotive industry. 
Lightweight of these products has led to increase in their utilization in the manufacturing of car components, body 
structure, power train etc. In addition, rising focus of consumers towards car racing and sports cars is likely to have 
a positive impact on the market growth over the next eight years. It is estimated that the automotive industry supports 
more than 13 million sector-related jobs in Europe and increasingly, these are highly skilled jobs. This sector also 
makes a major contribution to EU’s GDP, and exports far more than it imports. For these reasons the Automotive 
sector is considered central to Europe’s employment and prosperity. In particular the extensive diffusion on US, 
China and India market represent an important opportunity of growth for the European automotive industries. [
77] 
Aerospace: The increasing Demand for Lightweight and More Efficient Aircraft is driving innovation which 
connects scientific, social and environmental advances. Though the aerospace metal materials market is growing at 
a significant rate, few factors hinder the growth of the market globally. The global aerospace materials market is 
projected to reach 26 Billion euro by 2022, at a CAGR of 6.9% from 2017 to 2022. [ 78] Increased passenger 
transportation is projected to enhance the aircraft production industry, which will further drive the demand for 
aerospace materials. The high demand for lightweight aerospace materials is primarily due competitiveness towards 
the presence of top key players for aircraft manufacturing such as Boeing, Lockheed Martin, and others in the 
region. Globally, avionics and engine together account for approximately 39% of the market are expected to support 
the aerospace and defence industry going forward. Geographical analysis shows that the highest Annual Growth 
Rate is anticipated from Asia-Pacific region during whereby Europe and North America follows.  
Incorporation of lightweight materials in the manufacturing of parts for rail, shipping, and energy production is 
rapidly picking up. Rail wagon production is expected to increase with a 2.5- 3% CAGR over the next ten years, 
while manufacturing very high-speed trains rolling stock segments have the highest growth rate of 6.2% CAGR
79. 
The potential market share for metal lightweight materials and especially aluminum-based composites is immense. 
For example, the global market for rail industry connectors is expected to grow with an 8.0% CAGR, reaching an 
annual volume of $828.8 million [
80]. Similarly, aluminum composites are expected to replace steel in the building 
of tankers, big ships, yachts, motor boats, as well as underwater craft [81]. In wind energy production, approximately 
one fourth of the materials used are lightweight.

6. Sustainability of the Ecosystem & Financial projections 
In the next paragraphs the actions that will be undertaken by the LightMe ecosystem in order to demonstrate its 
sustainable are described.  
Towards the sustainability of the Ecosystem 
The best technology is worthless, if there is no means to make it accessible to the stakeholders. The members of the 
LightMe Ecosystem have already accumulated experience in this regard and have a strong position to guarantee the 
sustainability and the commercialization of the results and services of LightMe. A s aforementioned a Non-profit 
Organization, will be created during the LightMe project in order to establish commercial and legal procedures that 
will facilitate the creation of strategic alliances and the definition of common practices toward serving the 
stakeholders. A common commercial model for the Ecosystem will be adopted, aiming to strengthen the inclusion 
of further technology providers and the exponential growth of the end-users.  
The single entry point concept will assist in consolidating the technology, connecti ng people and facilitating 
collaboration. Indeed, the result of the Lightme project will be complemented with an Ecosystem, enabling end-
users to access the technologies and the manifold services from one single place. On the one hand, the Ecosystem 
will s treamline the access of new composite lightweight metals solutions to end -users. On the other hand, 
technology providers will be able to join the Ecosystem and offer their solutions, while profiting from a large 
community. The Ecosystem aims to be open and to promote the collaboration among the stakeholders, in order to 
connect people and businesses with one another, beyond the borders of single European countries focusing on 
European SMEs without being limited to be used by European companies only. The following table presents the 
 
82  https://ec.europa.eu/growth/industry/policy/key-enabling-technologies/european-strategy_en 
83  https://publications.europa.eu/en/publication-detail/-/publication/be32dfc7-1499-4328-b54f-a9f024805f59/language-en 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 45 of 70] 
 
added value offer of the LightMe Ecosystem in terms of materials processing, sectors addressed, services provided 
and revenue models: 
 
 
 
The LightMe Ecosystem has already recognized specific barriers that might prevent potential customers to access 
the services. Thus, proper measurement is projected in order to overcome these barriers. Besides the upscaling 
barriers already described in Table 2. the LightMe ecosystem has taken into account the following actions and 
procedures, targeting in the facilitation of access of customers (and especially SMEs) in the ecosystem.  
a. Access to finance: 
The members of LightMe have alrea dy recognized that access to the services of the ecosystem might have a cost 
that is above the capacity of potential customers despite the fact that the services will be provided at fair prices. This 
might be more evident in the case of SMEs and start-ups. Thus, the LightMe ecosystem, through the NPO that will 
act as the SEP and will undertake specific actions, targeting in facilitating the access to additional finance, including 
private and public funding, of such cases. Such cases will be posted in a dedicated page of the Ecosystem’s web 
platform, providing non-sensitive information in order to become visible in investing groups so that can come in 
direct contact with them. The Ecosystem will work on the following directions:   
1. The LightMe ecosystem has al ready contacted private funds  (Venture Capital Funds, Business Angels etc) 
that have expressed interest in the field of lightweight metals and alloys and are eager to proceed in private 
investments. The LightMe ecosystem will provide a safe and neutral environment for private investments. Five 
investing groups ( e.g. Wonder Talent Investor from Italy, Clave Mayor and Galician Agency for Innovation 
from Spain etc) have  provided letter of intent (Annex 1), supporting the activities of the LightMe Ecosystem. 
2. The LightMe ecosystem has recognized the most successful European crowdfunding platforms concerning 
innovative idea derived from SMEs and startups (e.g. Crowdcube, Seedrs, Kiss kiss bank bank, Companisto) 
as well as worldwide platforms (e.g. Indiegogo, RocketHub, Fundable, Ulele). During the project, these 
platforms will be contacted in order to establish collaboration with the Ecosystem. The target is to undertake 
the showcasing of the concepts need additional funding following the “all-or-nothing” funding model.  
3. The LightMe ecosystem will establish collaborations with bank firms  established in Europe, targeting to 
facilitate the acquisition of low interest loans by the partners.  
4. The Innovation Management Group will provide consultancy services to the potential customers via the SEP 
for applying bids through national or European funding mechanisms . Of particular importance could be 
considered funding schemes such us the SME instrument, FTI and regional projects dedicated in innovation.  
5. Finally, LightMe ecosystem will act as a bridge between upstream and downstream industry. Large enterprise 
and end users can provide direct funding to SMEs and start up for accessing the ecosystem  
In all above cases, the potential customers can take advantage of the services provided by the ecosystem concerning 
development of dedicated business plan, market analysis, showcasing videos etc.  
 
b. Pricing Policy: 
The pricing policy of LightMe has been based on two main aspects: (a) the ecosystem to become attractive to the 
potential customers and (b) to lead to a sustainable organization. Aspects like market prices for research services, 

[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 46 of 70] 
 
the goal of Ecosystem revenue and flexibility has been taking into account. The core partners of the Ecosystem have 
already provided in a list for average cost of the services that will provide (Annex 2). Additionally, to the cost the 
partners have also committed in the availability of each service. This pricing list was the basis for calculating also 
the average cost of test cases, as presented in the next paragraph. It is expected that these prices will cover fixed and 
variable costs, while the operational cost of the NPO (rents, salaries, marketing expenses) are also taken into 
account. During the first phase of the project, the pricing policy will be finalizes based on the following roadmap: 
- Market penetration: Setting up prices that will be attractive and affordable for industry and SMEs 
- Market share acquisition: To secure an adequate share of the corresponding R&D&I markets that will provide 
sustainability to the ecosystem 
- Satisfactory Rate of Return: To ensure a sustainable cash flow and profit allowing the expansion of LightMe.  
Discounts and offer opportunities will be examined (e.g. associated members, awards for innovative concepts etc).  
 
c. Financial projections: 
The target market the LightMe Ecosystem are companies in the field of materials developers, end users of the 
automotive, aerospace, rail and marine industries, where decrease of weight leads to significant energy savings, and 
R&D entities eager to upscale concepts in the field. More specifically, the LightMe ecosystem will cover the part 
of research and innovation in the field of lightweight metal matrix composites and advance materials that currently 
is not addressed by similar ecosystems as analysed in paragraph 1.4 . It should be mentioned that the addressed 
markets (e.g. automotive, aerospace) present the highest expenditure of R&D activities [ 84]. For example , th e 
European automotive industry is responsible for the 44% of the worldwide R&D expenses of the sector reaching in 
total the 50 billion € [
85], while aeronautics industry in Europe spends ~14 billion € in R&D (12% of turnover) [86]. 
LigthMe Ecosystem concept is in full accordance with the R&D&I reality in the field of lightweight metals. As 
already depicted in the SWOT-PEST analysis, various factors (environmental, financial) pushes towards the use of 
lighter components, especially for the transport industry. This shift, has created a high interest from both SMEs and 
larger enterprise to adopt such concepts in their portfolio. Thus, LightMe ecosystem will attract the interest of such 
companies and other stakeholders. Already during the 2 months of the proposal preparation ~40 companies have 
expressed their interest in the ecosystem services and potential results while ~15 other stakeholders  
(associations, research institutes and universities) have also provided letter of inten ts (Annex I). The dedicated 
dissemination and exploitation activities that will be undertaken by the partners, will significantly increase the 
awareness of industry, investors and other stakeholders for the LightMe  concept . The consortium has set the 
following KPIs for the duration of the project concerning the awareness and express of interest  from possible 
customers of LightMe.

Based on the above KPIs, the Table 2.5 presents the financial projections for the LightMe ecosystem for a period 
of 5 years after the finalization of the project. The following assumptions/estimations have been taking into account 
for the set up of the table. The presented costs are based on the preliminary pricing policy of the Ecosystem and the 
experience of partners in pricing industrial projects in their entities 
- The average cost of a test case concerning SMEs is ~ 90.000 €. This cost concerns the access to the PLs and 
provision of the additional services and corresponds to a duration of 3-5 months.  
- The average cost for a test case concerning L.Es is ~150.000€ and corresponds to a duration of 6-9 months. 
- Patent/technology licensing average revenue is calculated to 120.000 € per year 
- Technology transfer services and agreements is calculated to 100.000 € per year 
- Membership fees per year is set at 2.000€ 
- An average revenue per organized event is set at 20.000€. It should be mentioned that although the events 
organized by the Ecosystem will not have a significant contribution in the overall revenues, they are considered 
as of high importance due to their significant role in the dissemination and networking activities. 
- It should be mentioned that the calculated revenues for the SMEs and LEs as depicted in the first 2 lines of the 
Table 2.5 concerns the whole services of the LightMe Ecosystem. Already in Table 1.6 the initial interest for 
the various services of the Ecosystem has been shown, based on the answers of the companies that have 
provided LoI. It is evident that the majority of the companies (81%) are interested to access the Ecosystem in 
order to use the open pilot lines for upscaling new materials and products. However, there are also companies 
that are interested only to the other services of the Ecosystem (e.g. characterizations, process simulation, 
consultancy in standards, regulations, nanosafety and innovation managements). Concerning the analysis for 
the interest of the potential client for the various PLs it is shown that both casting methods as well as additive 
manufacturing and SPS concerns close to 90% of the potential client. On the other hand, half of the potential 
clients are interested not only to the services of the Ecosystem but they expect to establish new collaborations 
inside the Ecosystem with other stakeholders.  
- Finally, in Annex II all partners have provided a first proposition concerning the pricing of their services. 
 
Table 2.5: LightMe Ecosystem financial projections 
 
The initial investment of the set up of the Ecosystem corresponds to the budget of the LightMe project (13 million 
€). Additional investments for the first 5 years of the operation of the Ecosystem are expected to be in the range of 
~2 million € (further upgrades on PL including also maintenance costs). Thus, the total investment is ~15 million  
€.  
The LightMe ecosystem targets to meet the requirement set by the EC for creating revenues being 4 times the 
funding provided to the project by the EC.  
Taking into account a new job for every 200.000€ of additional revenue it is expected that ~260 new jobs will be 
created within the Ecosystem, including also the NPO. However, the impact on jobs creation will be much higher 
by including also the new jobs positions concerning the clients of the Ecosystem. With a moderate estimation of 
creation of 3 new jobs for each of the clients entering the Ecosystem (due to their business growth attributed in 
novel and competitive products they will develop) a total of ~900 new jobs will be created.
