IPR and knowledge management 
Consortium Agreement: A Consortium Agreement (CA) will be agreed and signed prior to project commencement 
in order to define the important points necessary to obtain the best possible management (financial conditions, IPR, 
planning). The DESCA H2020 template will be used as reference. Prior to the CA definition, the main guidelines 
for IPR management will be defined. Being one of the keys for the project success, background knowledge of each 
of the partners that may be used to achieve the project objectives will be identified and measures will be taken in 
order to deal with the use of Intellectual Property. Moreover, the consortium agreement will include any key steps 
that need to be taken for the best management and exploitation of the project. 
The IPR strategy of the project is an important part of the project exploitation plan. During the project meetings the 
internal results will be reviewed with the goal of identifying important ideas and defining an individual strategy for 
the positioning of these ideas in the standardization and commercialization processes. The IPR policy underlies the 
intention of the consortium to assure optimal IPR management for the development as well as for the professional 
exploitation of results. The following principles may regulate the aforementioned issues: 
Management of knowledge and Intellectual Property: All project’s participants have to co -operate in order to 
reach the most efficient process of knowledge management. The know -how exchanged between the partners may 
include, in certain cases, background knowledge. The partners are in agreement on the principles for the 
management of intellectual property. Access rights to background knowledge (pre-existing) needed to carry out the 
project will be granted royalty -free by the owning participant. Where a participant’s background IP is needed for 
post-project exploitation of the “results” (known as foreground) the participant may choose to charge a license fee 
under fair and reasonable terms. Finally, all knowledge will be managed in accordance with the EU Contract and a 
consortium agreement that will be timely prepared and signed by all consortium members. 
Patents and Knowledge Sharing: If considered appropriate the “results” IPR on new prototypes developed will 
be patented in Europe and any other regions of the world. 
Rules for governing access rights for the jointly executed research: Partners working together on common 
objectives of the project will enjoy access rights to: 
• The knowledge arising from work carried out under the joint programme of activities 
• The pre-existing know-how of the other participants when it is necessary for the project implementation. 
Except where other conditions are set in the CA, access rights to generated knowledge and pre-existing know-how 
shall be granted on a royalty- free basis for the development of the project. Access rights for profit -
making/commercial use of the knowledge generated within the network will be detailed in the CA. 
Background IPR: The Background knowledge of the partners, as stated before will be declared prior to the writing 
of the CA.  Background IPR will remain the property of the Originator partner. However, where needed, during the 
period of the project, all “background” knowledge of the partners is going to be available for use by any other 
partner of the consortium. Access rights will be granted, royalty-free by the owning partner. 
[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 50 of 70] 
 
In terms of post-project exploitation, access will be once again granted by the owning partner, either royalty-free 
or by charging a license fee under reasonable terms, promoting in that way the collaboration among nations and 
the advancements of the research and innovation. For better protection of the knowledge shared, a Non-Disclosure 
Agreement could be signed between the involving partners 
 
2.2.2  Communication of Project outputs 
LightMe project is expected to also communicate success stories of the ecosystem to the wider public. A broader 
general public will be reached by top level messages that reflect the project’s and particular segments of society 
where isolated actions would not be as effective as through a corporate LightMe. The campaign will use multiple 
channels to deliver a clear and consistent message to a variety of audiences in a way that they can be understood by 
non-specialists and it will have to actively engage with citizens, seeking their views and promoting a permanent 
dialogue. As aforementioned communication activities are of high importance in order to reach a wide audience, 
through which citizens will be shown concrete examples. Thus, an integrated communication campaign that 
demonstrates to non-specialized audiences of the project’s outcomes will be implemented. LightMe will implement 
a detailed communication plan, as part of the LightMe Dissemination Plan, aiming at explaining the project rationale 
and objectives. To this scope, the consortium has developed an initial communication strategy plan including Key 
Performance Indicators (KPI) (Table 2.8). During the project implementation, it will be further enriched to include 
ways of promoting the project ideas and the ecosystem before its end, as well as after the project ends since an NPO 
will proceed its operation. Partners will start by identifying the objectives of the communication campaign, which 
will differ according to each partner’s role in the project (core partners of the ecosystem, transversal roles, ecosystem 
clients): Designing the project graphical identity, to ensure consistency throughout the project duration, producing 
project documentation, which will stress the actual benefits of the solutions, along with incentives for involving 
different stakeholder groups. Organising project events, to raise awareness among a targeted public, analyse project 
activities, establish personalised interactions and provide project partners with useful inputs from target stakeholders 
to further improve the LightMe solutions. Contributing to external events, to raise key stakeholders’ awareness and 
facilitate knowledge sharing, thus increasing the project impact. Targeted events include events organised by the 
EU Commission’s Unit supervising the project, other EC Conferences and thematic clustering meetings, annual 
events organised under the aegis of the EC, and key events in the domain of circular economy. Similar to the 
dissemination key message on which the campaign will be based on will be used in order to attract the public. 
During the progress of the project also the Evaluation and redesign will be considered. The communication strategy 
will be evaluated in order to identify the strong and weak points and to revise and redesign if necessary the planned 
actions for achieving the best results. Therefore, during each project meeting each 6 months there will be a dedicated 
section to review the existing communication strategy, evaluate the succeeded results and identify threats or 
opportunities.

3. Implementation
3.1 Work plan — Work packages, deliverables  
 
The partners have already discussed and agreed about the management structure and the necessary procedures for 
the successful implementation of the LightMe project. In line with the technological/marked/innovation objectives 
that LightMe has to achieve in this 48 months programme the work to be accomplished has been structured in 14 
Work packages (Figure 3.1), each of which has been sub-divided into a number of tasks, which are in details listed 
in Figure 3.2 (Gant Chart) . Each of the work packages will be led and managed by a project partner who  is the 
expert in the relevant field. The whole development is targeting on demonstrating the technology in operational 
environment and supported by targeted research activities. The objectives are planned to be in complete alliance 
with the issues raised by the topic NMBP -01-2018 and will be implemented in a reasonable, scalable and cost -
effective manner, justified by integrated production methods. The structuring of the WPs has a dual scope. On one 
hand to set up and optimize the operational procedures of  the Ecosystem (WP2) and the necessary tools (WP3), 
starting from Pilot Lines and going to all supporting tools. On the other hand, to implement the upscaling of 8 
selected test cases in the filed of lightweight materials (WP4-11) as well as of 10-15 additional test cases during the 
open call (WP12). Finally, clustering and training activities (WP13) will be undertaken together with extensive 
dissemination and communication activities, targeting in the awareness of various stakeholders and thus, the 
successful exploitation of the LightMe results and in the sustainability of the Ecosystem (WP14) 
Appropriate synergies and collaboration are scheduled between the WPs. Feedback will be provided from the test 
cases WPs in order to continuously optimize the Ecosystem operations and tools. Due to the high total number of 
the WPs appropriate measurements have been taken in order to ensure the proper management and monitoring of 
the progress of the project, as in detailed described in paragraph 3.2. Figure 3.1 depicts the interconnections between 
the work packages and tasks of the LightMe project. 
 
 
Figure 3.1: LightMe Pert Diagram 
 
Figure 3.2. provides the Gantt chart of the project. The project will have a duration of 48 months and is split in three 
phases. The first phase (M1-20) concerns the set up of the Ecosystem (structure, infrastructure and processes). The 
second stage (M21-48) concerns the implementation of the test cases, including the open call and the validation of 
the ecosystem through them. Finally, in parallel to the 2 phases, the third phase, related to the extroversion and 
exploitation activities will be implemented (M1-48). 
 
 

[H2020-814552 LightMe – Part B]    [ 53 of 70] 
 
Figure 3.2: Gantt chart of LightMe project 

[DT-NMBP-01-2018]  
[LightMe]    [ 54 of 10]
3.2 Management structure, milestones and procedures 
3.2.1 Organizational Structure 
The management structure and procedures need to be clear and well-defined in order to implement successfully 
a project of this scale and dimensions. Both the core member of the Ecosystem as well as the members 
representing the eight test case are very experienced in collaborative R&D activities,  and cope with the overall 
management and implementation of the project. LightMe management is structured in four levels (Figure 3.3): 
1. Strategic Level: Composed by Project 
Steering Committee (PSC)  
2. Executive Level: Project Manager (PM) 
and coordination team of PoliMi 
3. Technical Management Level: consist 
of Ecosystem Technical Manager (ETM), 
Validation Technical Manager (VTM) and 
the Dissemination Exploitation 
Communication (DEC) committee. 
4. Implementation Level: WP leaders 
(WPL) supported by task leaders.  
The various management levels, roles and 
responsibilities are briefly explained 
below: 
  
Figure 3.3: LightMe Management Structure 
Level 1 (LightMe Strategic Level) 
The project will be strategically directed by the (PSC) which will be the ultimate decision- making body of the 
consortium, consists of one Delegate per Partner and chaired by the coordinator. Every PSC member will have 1 
vote and decisions will be made by majority voting. It has been determined that all PSC Members have been 
empowered to make decisions on behalf of their organization. This means that the majority of the members will 
be Executives, which will avoid unnecessary delays in the decision- making process. It will have the overall 
responsibility of all technical, financial, legal, administrative, ethics and dissemination and exploitation issue of 
the project, and will be also responsible for conflicts resolution. The Committee will be regularly informed by 
the PM about the progress of the project, achievement of milestones and critical stop/go decision points in 
accordance with the risk mitigation and contingency plan.  
 
Level 2 (LightMe Executive Level) 
The Project Manager (PC), Prof. Luca Magagnin, has a long experience in Project Coordination of R&D&I 
projects and will serve as the chairman for the PSC . He will be responsible for the coordination of project 
activities. The PM and his team coordinates and manages those items that affect the contractual terms with the 
EC, which will be fixed at the outset of the p roject, as well as the technical and scientific activities of the 
consortium. The mandate to the PC is outlined (but not limited to) the following:  
• Following administrative and financial issues of the project opposite to the EC and the consortium.  
• Communication with the EC.  
Accomplishment of project activities & targets within time schedule & budget constraints.  
• Overall project planning and scheduling.  
• Coordination of partners and organization of project meetings.  
• Internal (among the consortium partners) and external (to the EC) reporting, documentation and financial 
management (all of them through the Project Management Office).  
• Representation of the project and partnership to external stakeholders and initiatives.  
• Carry out the amendment by month 24 to include the NPO in the consortium.  
The management structure is the guarantee to the proper implementation of activities: it ensures that the project 
operates at the highest standards in both organisational and financial terms. The previous tasks, responsibilities 
and competencies permit an efficient, synergy-boosting and transparent platform for all Partners to concentrate 
on their different tasks needed to achieve the planned objectives of this present research project.  
 
Level 3 (LightMe Phases Management Level) 
The LightMe technical management level has been structured in order to handle decisions concerning any 
important operational issue that are related to the technical issues of the ecosystem setup, its validation as well 
as dissemination - communication and exploitation issues. Due to the complexity of the LightMe project a high 
number of Work Packages has outlined, 14 in total. In order to have an efficient implementation of the project 
the consortium has decided to set at this level three technical management positions:  

[DT-NMBP-01-2018]  
[LightMe]    [ 55 of 10] 
A) Ecosystem Technical Manager: Dr. Robert Lando from STAM has been selected to undertake the role of 
ETM.  The ETM will be responsible for the smooth execution of WP2 (PoliMi) and WP3 (UBrun). Dr Lando has 
a long experience in coordinating EC projects. He has been responsible for coordinating a significant number of 
pilot lines in relevant European Projects, while he has also the experience of setting up and operating Digital 
Innovation Hubs (e.g. Fortissimo). His role as ETM will facilitate the set up of the ecosystem concerning both 
tangible (e.g. pilot lines, infrastructures, testing equipment) as well as non- tangible (e.g. procedures, protocols 
etc) issues that are the main objectives of the WP2 and 3.  
B) Validation Technical Manager: Dr. Pilar Rey from AIMEN has a MSc in Chemistry (Inorganic Materials) 
and a  PhD in Chemistry (Science and Engineering of Materials). She is an expert in Material Sciences and 
Technology with more than 10 years of experience in R&D Projects related to advanced materials. Dr. Rey has 
been involved during more than six years in R&D initiatives in the field of characterization and production of 
coatings, based on non-conventional processing of advanced ceramic materials. Currently, Dr. Rey is working at 
the Advanced Manufacturing Processes department in the Technology Centre AIMEN. Dr. Rey has been dealing 
with several projects related to all stages of the pulvimetallurgy process including mechanical alloying, extrusion 
and joining of aluminium profiles by Friction Stir Welding and also powder deposition by laser cladding and 
additive manufacturing. She has more than 12 years working in manufacturing and testing of several materials 
and she has specialized in last years in working with light alloys (Al, Mg, Ti),  AlMMCs by Friction Stir Welding 
and Friction Stir Processing and fabricati ng and testing composite materials with different matrices specially 
ceramic reinforced metals. She will follow and guide in collaboration with the work package leaders the WPs 4-
12.  
 
C) DEC-committee: The DEC-committee will consist of three persons: 
i. The Innovation & Exploitation Manager (IEM) will be Dr. Alexandros Zoikis Karathanasis from Axia.  
ii. The IPR manager will be Mr. Hans Gaux from TimeL. 
iii. The Dissemination & Communication Manager (DCM) will be Mr. Eurico Assunção from EWF 
The DEC committee will be chaired by the IEM and will be responsible for the activities undertaken in WP13 
and WP14. This position is quite important as Innovation Management requires a unique set of skills, t he 
innovation potential of LightMe that builds on the SEP with multiple access modes tailored to industry and on 
the DEC to manage all innovative commercial contracts and IPR.

The IPR follows CA recommendations for the Consortium (background and foreground IP). IP management will 
target: a) to timely promote valuable open data (protocols and procedur es to accelerate innovation); b) attract 
industry and SME to direct/collaborative access and C) protect sensitive data of any clients of the ecosystem. The 
detailed internal IP management will be outlined in the CA. Background IP (publications, patents, owned prior 
to CA and relevant to the project) shall be available to the Consortium. Protected IP by a Partner shall not restrict 
[DT-NMBP-01-2018]  
[LightMe]    [ 56 of 10] 
other Partners from scientific work on issues regulated by that patent. Prior knowledge not regulated by patents 
and not published at the time of CA, could be shared by the Partners under a reciprocal NDA (non disclosure 
agreement). Foreground IPR (generated after CA) will belong to the Partner that created the IP or shared among 
Partners proportionally to contributions. All Partners will have access on a royalty-free, non-exclusive and non-
transferable basis to the respective IP for the performance of the project tasks only. Any other use shall require a 
royalty-bearing, non- exclusive and non- transferable license subject to a separ ate licensing agreement. This 
management level will be supplemented by innovation and marketing experts from the partners’ organizations 
and especially the industrial ones. IPR exploitation will be processed by means of standardized fact -sheets 
operated by ICT tools. Finally, the DCM will be responsible for the extroversion activities of the consortium and 
the Ecosystem including clustering and training activities. 
 
Level 4 (LightMe Implementation Level) 
Each WP leader will be responsible for: (a) resolving day-to-day administrative, technical and resource problems 
within his/her WP , (b) disseminating information relating to all aspects of the work to the other WP leaders 
ensuring smooth coordination of work package activities and (c) reporting to the upper levels of project 
management. The selected management structure offers a good balance of the various elements that affect 
management design and operation during the project and post project (i.e. simplicity, flexibility, effectiveness, 
etc.). At the same time, it allows for increased flexibility and effectiveness, as it favours the appointment of 
multiple roles to each partner. WPL organizes the production and internal review of the WP deliverables. Each 
WP group will provide a written technical progress report each 6 months to the PM , based on the reports 
submitted by the concerned personnel involved. The individual WP Groups will meet as necessary, convened by 
each WPL, but at least 4 times during the course of the WP. These meetings will concern the progress of the work 
being done in the WP and deal with any problems that have arisen. The members of the WP Groups for each WP 
will be one representative from each organization participating in the WP. Each of the WP Members will be 
responsible for attending the project and WP meetings to which they are convened, for providing individual 
quarterly internal technical reports to the WPL, and for ensuring the quality of the work they do within the WP.  
 
3.2.2 Management activities of the project 
Project Management Tools for planning, monitoring and reporting: LightMe will use on -line Project 
Management Tools (Trello, Dropbox, Google docs, etc.) that facilitate project planning, monitoring, and 
information collection and reporting thus, ensuring that project information is always up- to-date, and can be 
reported in a timely and consistent manner. The respective tools will also feed the Periodic Reporting to the EC. 
Project information flow will be channelled through: (i) ma instream electronic communication (e.g. emails, 
phone, Skype, internal web-site, etc.); (ii) bi-annually scheduled, and if necessary, ad-hoc GA meetings; (iii) ad-
hoc virtual or physical technical meetings; (iv) internal semester progress reporting (from p artners to PC); (iv) 
project co-creation workshops and events; and (v) preparation context for the official reporting to the EC.  
Consortium meetings: eight (8) consortium meetings are scheduled  every six months . These meetings will 
constitute major milestones for planning, exchanging information among partners, assessing project progress and 
success (financial and technical) and for taking major decisions about project execution. (A) 1st Kick-off Meeting 
(M1): to detail project planning, work allocation and initiate project activities, (B) 2 nd – 7th Meeting (every six 
months): progress review and planning for next period, (C) Final ( 8th) Meeting (close to the end of the project): 
Preparations for the final event and project review. For reasons of cost -efficiency, consortium meetings will 
coincide, when possible, with the project planned events (workshops, stakeholder events, info days, etc.) or 
review meetings. Minutes of all meetings will be kept and circulated to all partners, followed by Action Lists. 
The Partners will have a week upon receipt of the minutes to comment on them, otherwise they will be considered 
as approved and form part of the project implementation plan.  
Financial management and procedures: The Financial Tools used on the project will comprise a set of linked 
spreadsheets which present only the essential information for partner and Coordinator inputs, specifically to 
reduce the financial administrative complexity for all project members. The primary financial information will 
be extracted from the agreed EC contract following successful contact negotiations. Periodic entries are essential, 
and Project Manager will ensure that (a) annually, the personnel costs and overheads must be updated and (b) 
monthly the partners must enter their hours and expenses on a simple form.  
LightMe 
 
3.2.3 Decision-making & conflict resolution procedures 
In terms of decision making  mechanisms, when strategic decisions need to be taken, such as action to solve 
conflicts, action to mitigate critical risks to project implementation, action to manage changes in the work plan, 
decisions in relation to IPR and exploitation, etc., it will be the responsibility of the PM to seek consensus with 
the PSC, whereby each partner will be assigned one vote. Decisions will be taken by simple majority. In the event 
of a tie situation, the PM will have a double vote. Each representative of the PSC will  be responsible for 
[DT-NMBP-01-2018]  
[LightMe]    [ 57 of 10] 
mobilising and coordinating the active and coherent participation of the other personnel from their organisation 
who are involved in the project team, and they will also ensure that reporting and cost statements from their 
organisation are submitted on time and correctly. In the case of conflicts LightMe has already set up a conflict 
resolution mechanism that will be followed during the LightMe project (Figure 3.4).  
 
Figure 3.4: LightMe Conflict resolution mechanism 
Should any conflict arise requiring a decision the target is to solve the conflict in the lowest possible level (Task 
leader < WPL < TM < PM<PSC). This procedure will be also included and described in the details in the (CA). 
If a dis pute persists even after the meeting of PSC, then the partners will seek the advice of an independent 
external arbitration chamber. 
 
3.2.4 Milestones for validation of the ecosystem 
LightMe project is ambitious with a lot of partners involved. The Project Milestones will be used as a valuable 
tool for evaluating critical performance and determining whether or not the project is on schedule.  Successful 
achievement of the targets specified in the milestones will ensure a smooth project implementation. Milest one 
reviews will be held at each meeting of the PSC six monthly and a critical review of the outlook for effective 
exploitation of results will be monitored by the partners. The Project Milestones will be used as a valuable tool 
for evaluating critical performance and determining the progress of the project. 
 
3.2.5 Critical risks and sustainability 
Risks can be categorized  as follows; technology related risks, market related risks and transversal risks 
(environment related risks and organisation related risks). Given the dynamic nature of any project of this size 
and complexity, it is quite important, even from proposal development stage, that the consortium have a well -
defined risk management process and specific procedures to reassure early identification, adequate handling and 
proper mitigation of potential risks. In addition, another very important step is the pre-identification (well-before 
project start date) of the several types of risks that may potentially appear during project implementation as well 
as the means to proactively handle and successfully address them so as to minimize potential uncertainties as 
much as possible. Below this figure the phases and management approaches employed by the LightMe ecosystem 
to control project risk are explained in more detail. Regarding the monitoring of risks identified, as well as 
updates, this will take place on an ad- hoc basis (when a new risk is identified) or once every six months. For 
every new major risk identified the PSC will prepare a contingency plan to reassure the quality of project results 
and deliverables and the on-time execution of the project activities. All contingency plans will be incorporated 
to the overall organizational work plan of the project and will be further accompanied with partners’ 
responsibilities to handle them. Finally, risks will be assessed separately and will be reported at least on semester 
basis in the project reports. The table below summarizes an indicative list of the risks identified by LightMe 
consortium at proposal-stage level and their related contingency plans in brief.
3.3 Consortium as a whole hole 
LightMe introduces a network of different open access Pilot Lines (PLs), which have been selected due to the 
fact that they are representing a wide spectrum of production methods for processing lightweight metals as well 
as on the fact of their geographical distribution (UK, AT, ES, IT, PL) that shows a trans -national collaboration. 

[DT-NMBP-01-2018]  
[LightMe]    [ 58 of 10] 
The owners of the pilot lines will collaborate closely with the other members of the Ecosystem. Already in section 
1 the complementarity of the core ecosystem partners and the synergies that will be developed between the in 
order to offer fast and affordable upscaling services has been demonstrated. It should be mentioned that the core 
consortium consists of well recognized Universities (PoliMi, Ubrun) and Research Institutes (AIMEN, OGI, 
INOP, ISQ, ACCESS) with long record concerning the development of new knowledge and technology transfer 
as well as of innovative SMEs, with high expertise in their corresponding fields of modelling process control and 
monitoring (Iris Tech, Iris, Stam), environmental impact assessment (ICCRAM ). Moreover, SMEs with non-
technical roles will play a crucial role in the progress of the project due to the expertise they are bringing in the 
consortium like data management (IRED), innovation management (Axia), marketing and funding (INCOTEC), 
legal and advocacy consultancy (TimeL) and IT experts (RDC). The presence of EWF (Association) will provide 
also important expertise in standardization/regulatory issues as well as training aspects. Overall, the core 
ecosystem partners have all the necessary experience and expertise in order to consist a sustainable and innovative 
ecosystem. 
On the other hand, the consortium includes also 8 industrial partners (6 SMEs and 2 Large industrial partners) 
that have been selected in order to assist in the set up and evolution of the LightMe  Ecosystem through the 
implementation of their test cases. The selection of the 8 partners have been based on their experience in carrying 
out research project, the TRL of the test cases they introduce in the Ecosystem and on the markets they represent. 
Actually, the validators of the Ecosystem, form a supply chain span from novel materials producers (MBN, 
Mgcom) to downstream industry like automotive companies (Hidria, DIAD, JVST), aerospace companies (Cosk) 
and technology qualification companies for aerospace industry (AML) and finally to companies providing 
vertical integrated production lines (Kampakas).   
All 25 partners will collaborate between them in order to successfully deliver and achieve the LightMe objectives.

role/expertise in the project is depicted.

4.1.1 POLITECNICO DI MILANO 
 
Participant No 1 
 
Short name PoliMi 
Country Italy 
Organization type RTD 
webpage http://www.polimi.it 
Description of the legal entity 
Politecnico di Milano is a scientific -technological university which trains engineers, architects and industrial 
designers. The University has always focused on the quality and innovation of its teaching and research developing 
a fruitful relationship with  business and productive world by means of experimental research and technological 
transfer. Politecnico di Milano is 1st in Italy, 28th in Europe and 230th in the world according to QS Rankings 2013; 
in the top 50 universities in the world in manufacturing engineering areas. 37,900 enrolled students, with 3732 
Foreign students; and 1346 teaching staff. The PoliMi unit will be hosted at the Department of Chemistry, Materials 
and Chemical Engineering (CMIC) "Giulio Natta" of the Politecnico di Milano. The De partment 
(www.chem.polimi.it) was established in 2001, through unification of three pre -existing chemistry -oriented 
departments. One of these was the scientific home of the Chemistry Nobel Prize winner Giulio Natta (shared with 
K. Ziegler in 1963, for ster eospecific polymerization). Personnel of the Department, composed by about 120 
permanent researchers plus a large numbers of post -doc researchers, PhD students and other collaborators, 
participates in many study programs, and in particular to the Bachelor, Master and Ph.D. programs in Chemical 
Engineering and in Materials Engineering. The mission of CMIC Department is to promote and to support the central 
role of chemistry, chemical engineering and materials science and engineering throughout the whole spectra of new 
technologies by offering advanced expertise. This is attested by the contributions to basic science (scientific papers 
published in a wide range of high impact factor international journals), by the international patents and by the 
contracts wit h small, medium and large (often multinational) companies covering a broad distribution of 
merceological sectors. Research projects and activities, covering a wide range of fields within pure and applied 
chemistry, chemical engineering, materials science and technology, are funded by national programs (PRIN, FIRB), 
European projects, private foundations, contracts with large as well as local small-medium enterprises.  
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
PoliMi will be the coordinator of the LightMe project leading WP1. More specifically Prof. Magagnin will be the 
project manager and responsible for the coordination activities and the relationship with the European Commission. 
He will be responsible for the relationship with the European Commission and will be responsible for the overall 
administrative, financial, legal and ethical management of the consortium T1.1. In the Ecosystem PoliMi will be 
member of the Building Block 3 that is related to the Testing and environmental assessment services as well as in 
Building Block 5: H/S, nanosafety, regulation & standardization services collaborating with ISQ and EWF. In WP 
2 they will lead T2.2 establishing internal operation procedures of the Ecosystem as well as T2.4 that concerns the 
fine tuning of the Ecosystem structure and procedures. In T3.6 they will work on the fine tuning of the Ecosystem 
tools. PoliMi thus will have a leading role and has already considered all necessary aspects for the creation of the 
LightMe NGO. They will also hav
e an involvement in the implementation and validation of Al automotive 
components for JVST produced via SPS KOBO creating work flows in T7.1. In WP8 they will setup work flows in 
T8.1 that for the test case of Kampakas of door knobs produced via LPDC & GSC. It is worth mentioning that PoliMi 
has collaborated with Kamp in the FP7 SelfClean project and thus will have a good basis for further advancing 
results. In WP12 that addresses aspects surrounded by the open call they will lead all tasks T12.1 -4. In T13.1 they 
will lead Clustering with EC ecosystems they have done already a huge effort in involving companies around PoliMi 
and in collaboration with all partners they will expand this network to the international level. Finally, in WP14, they 
will contribute as all partner in the dissemination/exploitation and knowledge management including the task related 
to attraction of additional funding.

Description of any significant infrastructure and/or any major items of technical equipment 
Facilities hosted in the Department: from the chemical point of view, PoliMi has free access to state -of-the-art 
equipment, in the experimental material science Section, nanoparticles synthesis, deposition and material 
characterization facilities are available. In particular, glove box for controlled atmosphere reaction, small scale lab 
reactor for controlled pressure and temperature synthesis, chemical hoods, ovens for controlled coating densification 
will be used in the synthesis of hybrid sol -gel coatings. The laboratory activity relies on a wide range of analytical 
tools, characterization techniques and equipment for electrolytic, physical and chemical vapour 
deposition.Measuring instruments and equipment for material/process characterisation include the following: X-ray 
Fluorescence Spectroscopy (XRF), as well other basic instrumental chemical analysis techniques; Atomic Force 
Microscopy (AFM) equipped with Kelvin Probe; ellipsometry; non- contact surface roughness; micro -indentation 
testing instrument; fretting, wear and tribo-corrosion testing systems with different contact geometry; polarography 
and voltammetry; electrochemical impedance spectroscopy analyser and high speed waveform generator; quartz 
crystal microbalance; in-situ electrodeposits internal stress measurements; electrodeposition facilities (high current 
/ high voltage power supply units, for both direct current and pulse plating). Environmental Scanning Electron 
Microscopy with Energy Dispersive Spectroscopy and Transmission Electron Microscopy, X -Ray diffrattometry, 
laser profilometry, Glow Discharge -Optical Emission Spectroscopy, Ellipsometer, ATR FTIR, Nanoscratch, and 
Nanoindenter are accessible for a complete chemico -physical and surface mechanical characterization of the 
deposited coatings.

4.1.2 ACCESS e.V. 
 
Participant No 2 
 
Short name ACCESS e.V. 
Country Germany 
Organization type RTD 
webpage http://www.access.rwth-
aachen.de/ 
Description of the legal entity 
Access is an independent research centre associated with the Technical University of Aachen (RWTH) in Germany. 
50 engineers and scientists are pooling a diversity of individual skills to merge both scientific and technological 
know-how in materials and processes with a special focus on metallic materials and casting processes. Excellence 
in science demonstrated in application is the leitmotiv! High end products for turbo machinery are outstanding 
examples for this approach. Scientific expertise and technological skills are transferred into best practice examples 
when needed. Scientific Expertise: Research into fundamentals of solidification and solid state phase transformations 
is essential. It enables us to accomplish a knowledge- based development of metallic materials for dedicated 
applications. We use state of the art experimental and analytical equipment, Thermo -Calc and our proprietary 
microstructure simulation software MICRESS® to comprehend the thermodynamics and kinetics of microstructure 
formation. Microgravity environment is used as a unique tool for specific solidification experiments to provide 
benchmark data for numerical modeling. Today’s exciting areas are aluminides, ferromagnetic shape memory alloys 
and solar silicon. Improving the properties of commercial steel grades, superalloys or aluminium alloys is 
challenging none the less. Technological Solutions: The technological solutions are embedded in our scientific 
expertise, being targeted to commercially competitive products. Our know-how covers entire production lines from 
the raw material to final parts on stock (FPS) and even extending towards life -cycle predictions. Access has 
successfully optimized special casting processes for a number of alloy families with a focus on light weight alloys 
for the aero engine and automotive market. The simulation tool STAR-Cast, a joint development between cd-adapco 
(now Siemens PLM) and Access, is a true compelling engineering simulation solution for a broad range of casting 
processes. High Quality Products: The Access TechCenter operates on a DIN EN 9100:2016 certified center,  
provides an ideal environment for process engineering and component manufacturing via casting. Our main task: 
reach technological readiness and provide a production capability according to industrial standards. Access 
guarantees the transfer of its developments into industrial production and is ready to support implementation at the 
customer’s site. Access has been approved and certified to provide prototype parts for the new generation of aero 
engines and car engines. Software Tools: As international experts in casting and metallurgy Access has been 
focussing on the simulation of mat erials processing and properties on different scales. STAR -Cast offers 
comprehensive modelling capabilities on the component and process level whereas MICRESS® is a universal tool 
for the simulation of the internal structure of materials on the microscale. 
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
Access will provide modelling and simulation support of the casting pilot lines thus are leading member of the 
Building Block 4 that deals with all aspects of Modelling & simulation services especially for casting where they 
will be in close collaboration with UBrun, INOP, Stam. In WP 2 they will contribute in the establishment of the  
internal operation procedures of the Ecosystem as well as fine tuning of the Ecosystem structure and procedures. In 
T3.6 they will work on the fine tuning of the Ecosystem tools. They have already provided letters of intent from their 
clients. The will also participate in WP6 collaborating with AML for the test cases produced in the pilots of LPDC. 
In WP8 they will model the LPDC and GSC casting process for the test case of Kampakas (doorknobs). In WP9 they 
will collaborate with Hidria for the steering pin ions that will produced at the pilots of HPDC and GSC. Closing in 
WP12 that addresses aspects surrounded by the open call they will contribute in clustering and training activities in 
the ecosystems, they have done already a huge effort in involving companies they are already collaborating SIEMES, 
FORD and other. Finally, in WP14, they will contribute as all partner in the dissemination/exploitation and 
knowledge management including the task related to attraction of additional funding. 
 
Description of personnel´s profile (representative ones) 
Georg J. Schmitz (Male): Dr. Georg J. Schmitz obtained his PhD in materials Science in 1991 from RWTH Aachen 
University in the area of microstructure control in high temperature superconductors. His research interests comprise 
microstructure formation in multicomponent alloys, modelling of solidificationphenomena, phase-field models and 
thermodynamics. Dr. Schmitz is the coordinator of the European “Integrated Computational Materials Engineering 
expert group - ICMEg”. He has been appointed as expert by several institutions and is active member of the TMS 
committee on Integrated Computational Materials Engineering “ICME” and of the European Materials Modelling 

[DT-NMBP-01-2018]  
[LightMe]    [ 69 of 10] 
Council EMMC. He is editor and reviewer fo r a number of journals and has published  more than 150 scientific 
articles and jointly with Dr. Prahl – edited a recent book on a platform concept for ICME.  
 
Santhanu Jana (Male):  Dr. Santhanu Jana has strong expertise of development and application of computational 
fluid dynamics to casting and other material processes. He holds a Bachelor in Chemical Engineering, Masters in 
Computational Engineering and PhD in Materials Engineeri ng from RWTH-Aachen, Germany. He has around 13 
peer-reviewed publications and was involved in development of commercial casting software STAR -Cast. His 
experiences includes application of modelling tools to develop various casting processes; including near  net shape 
casting of TiAl for low pressure turbine blades in next generation aero -engines. He is currently a work package 
leader of Horizon 2020 project EQUINOX, responsible for modelling of thermodynamics, flow and microstructure 
and experiments development of near net shape casting. Prior to his ongoing job at Access since 2008, he worked at 
Institute of Fluid dynamics, Erlangen from 2002 to 2007, on numerical modelling of crystal growth processes. 
Jürgen Jakumeit (Male) Dr. Jürgen Jakumeit has a strong background in computer simulation of physical processes. 
His PhD and habilitation at the University of Cologne were in the field of semiconductor device simulation. During 
his engagement at Fraunhofer institute SCAI, he led a group on the numerical optimization of industrial production 
processes. Since 2002 he is head of development of the casting process simulation at Access e.V in strong 
collaboration with CD-adapco, now Siemens PLM. In the field of casting simulation his focus is mould filling and 
related defects like gas enclosure, misruns, cold shuts and porosity. His interest extends to other metallurgical 
production processes like additive manufacturing.   
 
Markus Apel (Male):  Dr. Markus Apel is an expert in material microstructures, phase transformations and 
microstructure simulation with more than 50 authored and co-authored publications in this field listed in the web of 
science. 1996 he graduated with a PhD degree in physics from the University Göttingen, 1997 he start working at 
ACCESS. Since then, he participated in numerous public or industrial funded projects in the area of metallic material 
processing, e. g. in the FP5 project VESPISM or the FP7 project “Multiscale Modelling Platform: Smart design of 
nano-enabled products in green technologies”. He gained several DFG research grants in the area of solidification 
science. Since 2008 he is heading the microstructure simulation group at ACCESS which is developing MICRESS, 
the leading commercial phase field software package for microstructure simulations in technical materials and 
processes.  
 
Heiner Michels (Male):  Heiner Michels  joined ACCESS in 2016 and is currently leading one of ACCESS 
appliedresearch focus groups, concentrating on Iron Aluminide (FeAl) processing with the goal to qualify FeAl -
alloys for part production, mainly in the energy aerospace industry as a lightweight , cost-effective and sustainable 
material. The currently ongoing projects, in total 5, on this FeAl -platform addresses technological readiness level 
from 2 to 5. Before working at ACCESS; Heiner Michels was at MAGMA Gießereitechnologie GmbH, a leading 
deve
loper and provider for casting and solidification simulation software for the foundry industry. Prior to that, he 
spent 5 years at the RWTH Aachen Foundry Institute as a PhD student. Heiner is a RWTH Aachen graduated foundry 
engineer.

Description of any significant infrastructure and/or any major items of technical equipment 
Access e.V. offices are located Aachen, Germany. An overview of technical equipment available at Access: 
 
Computing facilities:  
Access e.V. has a two high performance computing clusters, first one consisting of 36 computing nodes with 976 
cores and the second one with 36 computing nodes with 432 cores. 
 
Analytical facilities: 
Access has an excellent Analytik  Department equipped with three modern Field Emission Scanning Electron 
Microscopes (ZEISS Leo 1550, ZEISS Ultra 55, Zeiss Crossbeam) equipped with Oxford EDS and EBSD Systems 
and stages for micromechanical testing, Computed Tomography (Nikon Metrology), different automated High-End 
Light nicroscopes (Zeiss Axiophot, Zeiss Imagre M1, Hirox KH-5400), optical 3D Steinbichler 3D Scanning System, 
instrumented Indentation and more. With this equipment and well trained personel Access is capable of performing 
all necessary material research requests inhouse and for external partners. EBSD based Phase or Grain Analysis, 
Image Analysis, Tomography based 3D Defect Scans or Handling of large volumetric Datasets are common tasks. 
 
Technical Center: 
In addition to ACCESS simulation and analytic infrastructure, a complete casting production line is operated at the 
DIN EN 9100:2016 certified TechCenter of ACCESS in Aachen. This includes mould/die layout and production, 
casting devices and machining centers. According to ACCESS material and market focus, most equipment is 
stemming from the investment casting process route (LINN SUPERCAST, LEICOMELT TP5, VA-Tech automated 
shell mould production center). However, numerous equipment can be used for a range of purposes, such as the Go 
Mill350 and Mikron MillE700U machining centers. Gravity die and sandcasting capable casting devices add to 
ACCESS casting infrastructure.

4.1.3 ASOCIACION DE INVESTIGACION METALURGICA DEL NOROESTE 
 
Participant No 3 
 
Short name AIMEN 
Country Spain 
Organization type RTO 
webpage www.aimen.es 
Description of the legal entity 
AIMEN is a Non -Profit association constituted by 100 companies, which supplies technological support to more 
than 400 companies dedicated to industrial or commercial activity related to metallurgy, automotive sector, civil 
construction, mechanics, shipbuilding, chemicals, foundry, machinery, ceramics, food, cement, wood and its by-
products, plastics, engineering, assembly and others. Located in the Northwest of Spain, AIMEN is a highly-
professionalized organization with more than 200 employees specialized i n Materials Science, Manufacturing 
Process Engineering, Control Engineering and Laser Processing. Its mission is to improve competitiveness and 
technology know-how of Manufacturing Industry. AIMEN is divided in two units: AIMEN Industrial Services, which 
dedicates to perform industrial services through direct contracts with companies (in 2016, more than 650 services to 
clients from 25 countries) and AIMEN R&D which dedicates to develop and execute publicly funded R&D projects 
at regional, national and European level. AIMEN R&D is divided in four research units: Advanced Materials 
(MAVA): material development and processing of polymer-matrix composite materials, multimaterials (hybrid and 
dissimilar materials), metal matrix composites (MMC), etc. Adv anced Manufacturing Processes: development of 
process and applications in manufacturing and joining technologies using different active principles: laser (cutting, 
welding, surface processing and functionalization, cladding, additive manufacturing (metallic powder and wire), 
friction stir (welding, processing), wire arc (welding, additive manufacturing), etc. Robotics and Control: 
collaborative robotics, flexible and smart systems, sensor integration, machine learning, artificial intelligence, etc. 
Environmental Technologies: water treatment, biowaste recovery, LCA, etc. Being a European Competence Center 
in Laser based processing, AIMEN has active presence in the main European and National technology platforms and 
initiatives such as Photonics21 (secretary of the Spanish branch), EFFRA, EuRobotics, EuMAT, ManuFUTURE, 
etc. AIMEN is the official training centre of the European Welding Federation (EWF) and takes part in other national 
and international expert panels, consulting committees, groups and societies like the International Institute of 
Welding (IIW), EARTO, the European Laser Institute (ELI), sectorial industry clusters (automotive, shipbuilding, 
metalworking), as well as in SECPhO (Southern European Cluster in Photonics and Optics). 
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
 
PILOT LINE FOR METAL WIRE ADDITIVE MANUFACTURING (MWAM) 
AIMEN will provide to the LightMe ecosystem its pilots facilities of Building block 1 “Pilot lines and fast 
prototyping units for wire AM (Laser Metal Deposition (LMD)) which will be used to process various metallic alloys 
including Ti, Al and Mg. AIMEN will set a prototype of an industrial facility for manufacturing of medium / large 
size components using WLAM principle capable of processing non- ferrous alloys and develop and test process 
parameters for processing of advanced composite materials provided by the SME partners. Thus they are one of the 
six members of the of the Building Block 3 that is related to the Testing and environmental assessment services. In 
WP2 like all core partners of the ecosystem will contribute in the setup. In T3.1 they will have a very impotent role 
and effort since this is the task during which they will prepare the upgrade and proceed with all appropriate 
modifications of Pilot Lines. In WP5 they will be in close collaboration with Mgcom in order to test the Mg 
composite wires. They will also participate in WP6 collaborating with AML for the test cases produced in the pilots 
of LPDC. In WP6 they will provide AML with components produced by AM for machining the main matrix will be 
Ti & Al for applications addressing the aerospac e sector. Closing they will be involved in WP10 Scale up and 
Validation of drag braces via MWAM and Borealis. In WP10 Al MMC drag brace for Cosk will be developed 
through AM. More specifically the metal deposition additive manufacturing processes will be developed for aircraft 
landing gear structural parts, MWWM AM processes will be utilized for producing a) Aircraft machined parts 
holding a great potential for justification by means of cost as a result of relatively low annual quantities. (between 
500 to 1
000 pcs. per product), b) lower drag braces. In WP12 they will work on open call they will contribute in 
training activities for the ecosystems. Finally, in WP14, they will contribute as all partner in the 
dissemination/exploitation and knowledge management including the task related to attraction of additional funding.

4.1.4 ADVANCED MANUFACTURING (SHEFFIELD)LIMITED   
 
Participant No 4 
 
Short name AML 
Country United Kingdom 
Organization type SME 
webpage http://www.amlsheffield.co.uk/ 
Description of the legal entity 
Advanced Manufacturing (Sheffield) Ltd (AML) is a manufacturing production company located in the United 
Kingdom specializing in the development of advanced manufacturing solutions, and production services for a 
number of blue chip clients, including Rolls -Royce, Boeing and Siemens. Originally a spin- out company from the 
award winning Advanced Manufacturing Research Centre (AMRC) at the University of Sheffield, AML has now 
firmly established itself as a supplier to a number of clients with an annual turnover in excess of £2m and employs 
around 30 full time staff. 
 
The opportunity to spin out AML arose from a market opportunity to commercialize the growing demand for 
advanced manufacturing techniques applied on commercial prototype and production parts, and provide technical 
consultancy services. As such, AML specializes in delivering flexible manufacturing capability at the leading edge 
of machining technologies and efficiencies, with a particular focus on aerospace and power generation components.  
The company has a particular focus in the machining of titanium and nickel alloy complex gas turbine products. The 
specialist techniques developed by the company have allowed manufacturing costs to be significantly reduced, not 
only in hard metals but also other alloys such as aluminum. Services include the manufacture of complex metallic 
parts, precision sub-assembly manufacture, bespoke engineering services and R&D projects. Specific capabilities 
include: 
 
 CAD/CAM expertise for complex 5-axis manufacture 
 5-axis milling and mill turn machining 
 2D part making 
 CMM and Non-Contact inspection 
 Specialist in resonance testing and machining dynamics for process optimization 
 Adaptive probing and machining 
 Scanning capability and stock 'best-fit' control 
 Specialization in manufacturing strategies for difficult to machine mate rials and complex geometries e.g. 
rotatives, gearboxes, and aerostructures 
 All work is undertaken at AML’s production facility located in Sheffield, UK in close proximity to the 
Advanced Manufacturing Park. AML currently has six large 5- axis machine tools,  and is currently 
expanding to further enhance this capacity.  
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
AML will be an upstream partner in the LightMe project. As a metal processing for aerospace upstream partner in 
the project, AML will provide two test case components from aerospace applications, that will leverage the required 
services of the ecosystem in order to provide additive technology to the geometries in order to leverage component 
weight and machining cycle time gains. As such AML will be heavily involved in phase 2 providing engineering 
support and machining of test case examples. They will start  their test case under the implementation of WP6 that 
concerns the machining of lightweight Ti and Al composites. More specifically they will use components produced 
by LPDC, WMAM and SPS to evaluate their machinability and facilitate their application in aerofoils and rotative 
components in T6.1. As all partners they will be involved in WP12 that deals the open call working with the Building 
Bloch 6 (Innovation Management) they will create a showcase which will be used in the commercialization strategy 
of 
the ecosystem. The latter will address clients to enter the project through the open call in M30 and secondly post 
project. In WP13 they will participate in standardization, clustering as well as training activities. Dissemination and 
exploitation (WP14) will include activities sharing the outcomes the project results to a wider network

4.1.6 COSKUNOZ KALIP MAKINA SANAYI VE TICARET A.S

Short name Cosk 
Country Turkey

Description of the legal entity 
Coşkunöz Holding is active in 5 different sectors (Automotive, Energy, Defence  & Aerospace, Transport and 
Heating) with her 11 companies, 3 foreign partners and more than 2300 employees. Coşkunöz Holding has its own 
R&D Center with over 50 full-time researchers to develop solutions for customers. Coşkunöz R&D Center has been 
accredited as a co -designer by local and international OEMs such as Volkswagen and Renault. Coşkunöz R&D is 
able to execute all the chain of new product development process effectively, from the design space to product 
validation steps of structure and closure automotive parts. Coşkunöz R&D has extensive knowledge in; cost effective 
and weight saving product and process design, including carbon fiber composites, sheet forming analysis, thermal 
and non-thermal joining techniques. 
R&D interests are: 
 
 Light weight and/or cost effective component development for automotive industry by using; new forming 
technologies such as roll forming, hot or warm forming and hybrid forming techniques, with different materials 
such as new generation high strength steels, non ferritic alloys and composite materials . 
 Thermal and non-thermal joining techniques such as laser welding, friction stir welding, clinching process using 
for improving joining process efficiency for light weight design. 
 Developing of full system suspension group with its metal and rubber parts. 
 Customized products with combined metal and rubber materials for automotive and railway industries. 
 Additive manufacturing of Metal powders  
 Hybrid Manufacturing of Conventional Parts with Additive manufacturing. 
 
Coşkunöz R&D is also capable developing its own technologies in innovative joining applications with the strong 
background in resistance welding machine, resistance spot gun, assembly and measurement control fixtures, and 
customer-specific machines. Coşkunöz has necessary infrastructures to design welding test bench according to 
project requirements. 
The group’s first joint-stock company, Coşkunöz Metal Form A.Ş., was formed in 1973. It continues to activities in 
the area of manufacturing mainly for the automotive industry. Coşkunöz Kalıp Makina AŞ was formed as a sister 
company of Coşkunöz Metal Form in 2016. The main products of Coskunoz Kalıp Makina are: sheet metal forming 
tools, assembly and measurement control fixtures, standard and customer-specific hydraulic, mechanical presses and 
resistance welding machines. Forming and assembly of steel and aluminium compound sheet metal materials in the 
tools are produced in-house. Coşkunöz Kalıp Makina A.Ş. uses its own dies, press and welding machines to produce 
single parts or assemblies for the automotive sector. Today, with its Quality Management certificates, Coşkunöz 
A.Ş. deserves to be where it is , amongst the first 500 largest companies in Turkey. With its more than 50 years’ 
experience in the industry; importance is given to customer satisfaction; policy to ensure continuous development 
of its personnel, products, process, and environmental quality. 
Additive manufacturing is considered as one of the key tools to provide competitiveness into the automotive market. 
Even though the up- to-date cost structure does not seem competitive compared to the well -known conventional 
techniques, with respective A.M technology, design freedom and lightweight is Coskunoz’s main motivation to 
provide a breakthrough for automotive market. Therefore, hybrid technology shows a good potential in terms of 
initial steps on shift to this new technology. 
Coskunoz wants to be one of frontiers in design of composite products (conventional and A.M together ) and one of 
the first companies with novel production lines and increased productivity in Additive Manufacturing. 
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal

Description of the legal entity 
DIAD Group ES is a fast growing company in the sector of the advanced technologies for automotive and aeronautic 
sector, with a strong partnership all over the world, and find its success factor in the constant transformation of the 
knowledge produced by applied innovation into products , technologies and services. The Italian division DIAD 
Group is member of the Board of the Advanced Manufacturing Research Centre with Boeing (AMRC). Chair of 
the "Industrialisation and Nanomanufacturing" working group on the NANOFutures ETIP. Member of th e Board 
of the International Research Center in Critical Raw Materials for Advanced Industrial Technologies (ICCRAM). 
Partner of the NanoSafety Cluster and Cost Action CRM-Extreme (critical raw materials for extreme applications). 
The main activities of DIAD Group ES (short name DIGRO ES) are in the design, the development, the testing and 
the application of advanced body parts and mechanical components for the automotive and motorsport sectors, 
using the most advanced engineering tools and innovative mater ials (like high performance lightweight metal 
composites and reinforced polymers, exotic materials, hyperfunctionalized surfaces, nanostructured based massive 
and coating materials). This target is achieved with a integrated approach that cover the design and engineering 
excellency and the setup of the related manufacturing technologies (intelligent and reconfigurable production 
systems and processing) always looking at the environmental aspects and the total life cycle approach. Our targeted 
customers and markets are large tier1 suppliers, high tech small and medium companies, as well as motorsport 
teams, interested to sustainable and clean manufacturing and assembly of high tech components. 
 
The DIAD Group ES offers a series of industrial and highly qualified engineering services: 
 Full design and development of advanced automotive and motorsport components and the optimization of 
the related manufacturing systems, using innovative materials, custom technologies and state of the art 
functionalized surface engineering; 
 Automotive testing in extreme conditions and weather (like Nordic and desert climates). 
 Development of technologies for sustainable and clean manufacturing and assembly of high tech 
components; 
 Product and Process Life Cycle and recovery /recycling methods; 
 Industrial implementation of energy saving policies; 
 Methods to reuse innovative materials; 
 Nanotechnology engineering to manufacturing and processing industry;  
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
DIAD participates in LightMe as a downstream industry and provides test cases that will contribute to the validation 
of the operation of the ecosystem. Their main business is on operating in the motorsport sector, where the weight 
reduction is a crucial opportunity not only for decreasing the fuel consumption of the vehicles, but in increasing 
their performances and for improving their handling (optimisation of masses distribution). The Company is highly 
interested to the manufacturing of lightweight powertrain components (engine and driveline) and suspension parts 
adopting lightweight metal composites, in particular Ti based MMCs. They have in the past collaborated with MBN 
working in the development of materials for the automotive sector through AM. Also, they have a sire of established 
collaborations with PoliMi, AIMEN, AML, EWF and AXIA. They already request ed to access in Borealis (IRIS) 
and SPS (INOP) lines in order to produce Ti6Al4V MMC for conrods & gear box casing, which will start in M20 
under WP11. Based on the automotive industry standards they will be in charge of validating in field tests the 
composite components manufactured by utilizing Ti6Al4V/SiC MMC. They will also collaborate with the 
characterisation building block in order to test the components. The components manufactured in the Ecosystem 
will be validated in extreme conditions using the D IAD Group ES lab cars. As epilogue of this activity, the 
Company will pro- actively participate to the optimisation and validation of the LightMe ecosystem for the

4.1.8 EUROPEAN FEDERATION FOR WELDING JOINING AND CUTTING 
 
Participant No 8 
 
Short name EWF 
Country Belgium 
Organization type Association 
webpage http://www.ewf.be/ 
Description of the legal entity 
EWF is a European organisation established as an international non-profit association that acts as a representative of 
manufacturing community in Europe, providing the exchange of scientific and technical information and 
contributing to the removal of technical barriers. EWF, was creat ed in 1992 by all the welding institutes of the 
European Community with the aim of updating and harmonisation training and education in the field of welding 
technology. 
The EWF network is composed by 31 European + 16 Non- European members – the national Wel ding Institutes. 
Members of EWF, in each European and EFTA country are organizations active in Training, in RTD and transfer of 
technology and cover a wide range of industrial sectors in its membership which includes automotive, aerospace, 
metalworking, na val, appliances, etc. EWF also manages a harmonized system for training, qualification and 
certification of personnel, with more than 260.000 diplomas awarded and covering different level of qualification 
and different industrial requirements. 
 
 
 
Figure 1 - EWF Qualifications (Including the ones used at an International level) 
Current EWF membership includes approximately 50,000 companies where around 75% are SMEs (approximately 
37,500). Through its members, EWF aims to address technological issues  and needs, improving quality and 
stimulating competitiveness, by disseminating the opportunities created by the results of RTD projects to potential 
users and by training professionals in the use of the new technologies developed. 
 
EWF provides world class, European focussed, value-added products and support services to its members and their 
communities in the field of joining, welding and related technologies on an international basis. EWF is also member 
of EFFRA and one of the founding organisations of the Joining Sub- Platform to ManuFuture. This will ensure a 
wider dissemination of the project results to relevant stakeholders. 
 
EWF is also a liaison member to CEN and ISO with involvement in standardization activities at the European and 
International level. Particularly relevant is the fact that EWF is a Liaison Organisation to CEN/TC 121 - Welding 
and allied processes, to CEN/TC 438 - Additive Manufacturing and Liaison Member to ISO/TC 261 – Additive 
Manufacturing. 
 
EWF Overview: 
Manages a Qualification, Training and Certification system of personnel in Joining, Welding, AM and Cutting

4.1.9 HIDRIA D.O.O. PODJETJE ZA USTANAVLJANJE IN UPRAVLJANJE DRUZB 
 
Participant No 9 
 
Short name HIDRIA 
Country Slovenia 
Organization type IND 
webpage http://www.hidria.com/ 
Description of the legal entity 
The Hidria Group is one of the largest automotive industry suppliers in Slovenia and one of the country’s biggest 
exporters with approx. 240 million EUR in sales and 1.800 employees. Hidria will be participating in the LihtMe 
project through its Hidria Alutec business unit (BU). The BU has two manufacturing sites in Slovenia, with 350 
employees making approx. 45 million EUR of annual turnover. Hidria manufactures the most demanding 
components on its field in vehicles. Its product portfolio can be divided into three f ields:  electromechanical 
components for vehicle steering systems, oil - and water pump components for ICE and components for HEV and 
EV drivetrains out from which the steering system segment is the biggest. Hidria’s customers in HPDC automotive 
die-cast parts include VW, Porsche, Continental, Bosch, Brose, Nidec, Pierburg. Steering segments includes steering 
system manufacturers such as JTEKT, Nexteer, ZF/TRW and NSK. Today the Hidria Alutec BU covers the whole 
manufacturing process, which includes the cast
ing process, machining process, cleaning, measurements and 
validations. In addition to this Hidria is able to plan, design and produce its HPDC tools in- house in its own fully 
equipped tool- shop.  The manufacturing process in Hidria Alutec BU is highly robotized and the company has been 
upgrading its manufacturing process in the last years in accordance with the principles of Industry 4.0 and the leakage 
testing equipment itself is fully made internally with internal knowledge in Hidria. R&D support to Hidria Alutec is 
given   via   high-tech   laboratories   situated   in the   Hidria   Institute for   Materials   and Technologies in Spodnja 
Idrija with its 7 laboratories.  
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
Hidria enters the ecosystem as a downstream industry and provides test cases that will contribute to the validation 
of the operation of the ecosystem. Hidria will access the LightMe Ecosystem in area of HPDC technologies and will 
be responsible for providing an industrial use -case from the automotive industry centered on HPDC technologies 
and processes needed to produce latest hi -tech EPS steering system housings (primarily steering pinions, also 
steering columns) . Hidra is interested on requesting access to HPDC and GSC Pilot lines in order to produce 
composite AlSi9Cu3(Fe) steering pinions reinforced by SiC nanoparticles, in the WP9. They will also collaborate 
with the characterisation building block in order to test porosity criteria for housings as well as mechanical properties. 
They will contribute in the training and clustering activities in WP13. In collaboration with AXIA they will work on 
the exploitation strategy of their product ensuring the IP rights and business strategy they intent to gain from direct 
sales and licensing. Additionally, for the Dissemination (WP14) they will design and development of their role in 
the ecosystem, project description, publication considering events worldwide.

4.1.10 INSTYTUT OBROBKI PLASTYCZNEJ 
 
Participant No 10 
 
Short name INOP 
Country POLAND 
Organization type RTD 
webpage www.inop.poznan.pl 
Description of the legal entity 
The Institute founded in 1948, performs research, development, implementation works and participates in domestic 
and international projects on non-metallurgical metal forming. The Institute has well experienced and creative staff 
backed with advanced computer systems, modern scientific and investigation facilities. High quality of the 
investigation and development works is ensured by the Quality Management System conforming with ISO 
9001:2008 and the Accredited Investigation Laboratory meeting the requirements of PN-EN ISO/IEC 17025:2005. 
The Institute’s scope of activity includes:  
 innovative technologies, machines, devices and tools for: net shape forging, orbital forging, extrusion, semi-
open and die forging, stamping, spinning and flow forming, forming of precision metal powder parts, 
including the application of nanotechnology,  
 mechanizing and automating devices, special centres and production lines, 
 investigation of metal structures and properties,  
 biomaterials and biotribology,  
 heat and thermochemical treatment, tools and machine parts,  
 communication technologies,  
 standardization activity,  
 scientific and technical information – publications, data bases,  
 assessment of machine and device conformance,  
 consulting, training and promotion activity,  
 manufacturing of prototype machines and devices,  
 manufacturing of parts by the metal forming methods. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
 
PILOT LINE 6 FOR SPS-KOBO EXTRUSION PL  
 
INOP will provide to the LightMe ecosystem its pilots facilities of Building block 1 “Pilot lines and fast prototyping 
units for spark plasma sintering machine which will be used to process various Al and Ti alloys and MMCs. The 
main aims of INOP SPS-KOBO pilot line modification: i) increase of SPS machine productivity by two-three times; 
ii) increase of SPS tool life; iii) increase of the length of KOBO extruded profiles; iv) improvement of KOBO die 
design for extrusion of light weight Al alloy and Ti based composites. It is planned to produce: i) the light weight Ti 
based composite bearing rings for aircraft/automotive industry and brake pads with SPS of nanostructured HEBM 
composite powders, and ii) Al alloy (AA6061 and AA7077) based composite profiles with SPS and KOBO extrusion 
for further production of aircraft and automotive fasteners and other powder components by cold forging. They are 
thus involved in Building Block 3 that is related to the Testing and environmental assessment services. SPS will also 
become a test case for improvement in terms of modelling & simulation under the Building Block 4. In T3.1 they 
will have a very impotent role and effort since this is the task during which they will prepare the upgrade and proceed

Volf Leshchynsky (male): prof., PhD, Dr.sc. hab. Area of expertise - material science and engineering (45 year  
experience), scientific consultant of EUREKA, FP 5, 6, 7 projects. Dr. Leshchynsky is a visiting professor of Metal 
Forming Institute, Poznan, Poland. Dr. Leshchynsky received his Ph.D. degree in the theory of plasticity from the 
Physical Technical Instit
ute in 1968 and his Doctor of Science degree in the powder technology from the Institute 
of Metallurgy of Russian Academy of Sciences, Moscow in 1989. Dr. Leshchynsky’s research interests concern the 
fundamentals of nanotechnology and nanostructured materials, development and application of powder metallurgy, 
Spark Plasma Sintering and Cold spraying.  Analysis of the interface from the viewpoint of materials science, 
mechanics of solids and  surfaces, description of the materials behavior  at interacting surfaces under a contact load 
at the various scales are in the scope of research in particular for Spark Plasma Sintering and Cold Spraying.  The 
new powder metallurgy, nanostructuring and cold spray techniques developed by Dr. Leshchynsky during last 15 
years in Canada and Poland are being applied and disseminated in automotive, household, and high- tech industry. 
More than 200 publications, 2 monographs  and 30 patents.

Short name IRES

Description of the legal entity 
IRES is an independent Belgian project management firm (SME) administering all peripheral aspects of research 
projects, providing specialized services in the fields of innovation management, technology transfer and international 
research projects. IRES’s interdisciplinary team is capable to address a variety of tasks pertinent and supportive to 
research projects, crucial for their market applicability and sustainability. The company employs a team involving 
scientists from the financial and economic  discipline, management science, engineering and statistics, while is co -
operating with faculty members of European Universities and Research Institutes employing ad hoc experts to be 
involved in particular projects. 
The company's activities are focused on: 
 surveys and statistical analysis  
 applications of management 
 science methods and impact assessment 
 supporting research organizations and private companies to evaluate and to exploit their innovations at 
international level;  
In addition, through its international network, IRES supports the development of innovative technologies and the 
optimization of p
roducts. Indicatively the company professionals have expertise in Project Risk, Ethics and 
Knowledge management, market trend analysis, feasibility studies, Impact assessment and Technology Transfer, 
Research in Materials Science, Development of tailored materials, Nanomaterials, Processing and Upscaling, Design 
and setup of prototypes, demonstrators, Ethics and integrity in research, Exploitation and Dissemination towards 
high technology readiness level. 
 
Finally, IRES has a direct link to EMMC ( https://emmc.info/), EMCC ( http://characterisation.eu/), CFPC 
(http://www.technologycluster.eu/) and relevant cluster initiatives.  
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
IRES will have an active role in the LightMe Ecosystem, regarding the efficient data management and processing 
flow, focusing not only on maximizing data sharing and usage among stakeholders, but also ensuring data and 
metadata privacy and integrity. They will start their involvement at very early stages of the project since they will 
have to handle a big amount of data planning all process controls, flows and data mapping. Thus, IRES will be the 
WP Leader of work package 3, leading Task 3.1: Data Managemen t Plan, in which the collection of data to the 
objectives of the project and the establishment of an open innovation environment will enable future access, 
integration and harmonization of the produced data, Task 3.2: Data Mapping, that will be used as a first step for data 
integration, providing a unified view of the produced data. In collaboration with RDC and TimeLex they will work 
on task 3.4 that handles the communication platform of Ecosystem this is intended to create revenues providing 
supporting services to the NPO and the other partners based on the Joint Agreement in the field of data management, 
IT solutions, IPR issues and legal advocacy. In WP12 they will assure the handling of confidential data that will be 
collected during the open call considering all aspects of GDPR. Additionally, in collaboration with EWF they will 
be involved in WP13 regarding clustering and training activities. As all partners they will be involved in the 
dissemination and exploitation (WP14) activities sharing the outcomes of LightMe to the wider scientific and 
technical audience. Data Management Plan will be developed to facilitate these activities, without setting in jeopardy 
the generated IPs of the clients which will be considered under WP14 in collaboration with AXIA.
