4.1.12 IRIS SRL 
 
Participant No 12 
 
Short name IRIS 
Country ITALY 
Organization type SME 
webpage http://www.irissrl.org/ 
Description of the legal entity 
IRIS s.r.l ., founded in 2012, is an innovative SME specialised in developing applications of laser and plasma 
technologies focusing on advanced manufacturing and clean tech sector. 
IRIS employs engineers and scientists with a strong and multidisciplinary background in industrial laser, plasma 
technology, CNC machining, materials, energy, waste and water management. From this knowledge and expertise 
and successful partnerships with local and international SMEs and research organisations are born IRIS’ most 
successful ideas and projects. 
IRIS core business is today the development and qualification of new processes/equipment solution for laser and 
plasma processing technologies. The process qualification includes cost and energy consumption assessment, eco 
labeling certification, construction and characterisation of prototype equipment.  
The company is co-applicant in two patent applications submitted to the European Patent Office in November 2014: 
“Device, system, and method for the treatment of liquid waste waters” (BEP 18027) and “Device and system for 
plasma treatment of solid waste" (BEP 18028). 
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
 
PILOT LINE 5 FOR ADDITIVE MANUFACTURING (BOREQALIS) 
 
IRIS will provide to the LightMe ecosystem its pilots facilities of Building block 1 “Pilot lines and fast prototyping 
units for wire AM (Laser Metal Deposition (LMD). Materials that will be used are mainly Al and Ti alloys and 
MMCs. Following they will also be involved in the Building Block 4 that handles the modelling and simulation 
services. A modelling tool developed by IRIS within the OpenFOAM toolbox will provide a CFD simulation will 
be applied ensuring a homogeneous and constant concentration of pre -mixed materials rather than a variable and 
controlled concentration. In common with the other fife Pilot line leaders they will be deeply involved in Task 1.2 
that covers the Technical management of LightMe. In WP4 Test case they will use the pre alloyed powders delivered 
by MBN for AM. They will lead T4.2 which addresses the Scaling up and validation of Al and Ti pre -alloyed 
powders. In WP 10 they will in close collaboration with Cosconuz in order to produce through the modified AM 
process brad braces for the aerospace sector. Close collaboration with other building blocks of the ecosystem will be 
handled in order to ensure the compliance of the components to the high demands and standards of the industry. 
Shifting to the automotive test case they will collaborate with DIAD and under T11. Produce appropriate work flows 
for the production of composit lightweight conrods and gear boxes. For WP12 they will mobilize their contact 
starting to engage them in the Open call. They will be also involved in the Clustering & training activities producing 
protocols of use cases. In collaboration with AXIA they will work on the exploitation strategy of their Pilot lines 
ensuring the IP rights and business development action. Additionally, for the Dissemination they will d esign and 
development of their role in the ecosystem, project description, publication considering events worldwide.

Relevant publications, and/or products, services or other achievements 
IRIS was involved I several European and National R&D projects involving three main focus areas: 
Plasma for Environment: plasma technology applications for water/food sanitisation and liquid/solid waste 
treatment. IRIS patent pending solutions focus on small scale, low impact treatment technologies for off grid, highly 
efficient communities in isolated contexts (mountain villages, islands).  
Laser Processing Design: smart self -adaptive solutions for the efficient exploitation of laser processes: cutting, 
welding, direct metal deposition. 
Additive Manufacturing: IRIS specialises on process definition and characterisation  using performance indicators 
such as production time reduction, cost savings and energy & resource efficiency. This is a business growth area and 
we are expanding our workforce.

4.1.13 INSTITUTO DE SOLDADURA E QUALIDADE 
 
Participant No 13 
 
Short name ISQ 
Country Portugal 
Organization type RTO 
webpage www.isq-group.com 
Description of the legal entity 
ISQ is an independent, private, non-profit, technical, scientific and industrial oriented organization founded in 1965 with 
international presence in 16 countries, covering 4 continents. ISQ’s main activities includes techn ical inspections, 
consultancy, testing, metrology, training and research and development in a wide range of technical areas such as 
materials, structural integrity and risk assessment, sustainability, eco and energy efficiency, health and safety, quality 
assurance, production technologies, industrial automation and robotics. ISQ provides support to different industrial 
sectors such as Process Industries, Energy (including renewables) and Oil &Gas, Aeronautical and Aerospace, 
Automotive, Construction and inf rastructures, among others. It is one of the largest Portuguese technological 
infrastructure. ISQ’s know-how is supported by 16 accredited laboratories (accordingly with EN ISO/IEC 17025) and by 
a large involvement in National, European and International R &D projects, having participated in more than 400 R&D 
projects, in the last 30 years, in different funding programs (LIFE, LIFE+, RFCS, IEE, FP5, FP6, FP7, H2020), with a 
strong background of collaboration with a large number of Universities, Scientific Re search Institutes, industrial 
companies and other institutions worldwide. Research and Development at ISQ supports all operational in- house 
technical areas in the enhancement of existing technologies and new solutions. It also encourages the development of  
breakthrough technologies and solutions that lead to new products/technologies/methodologies/services, promoting new 
Business areas and thus contributing to the technological development and competitiveness of the industry.  
ISQ headquarters are at Porto Salvo, Oeiras, Portugal, with national delegations in Oporto, Castelo Branco, Loulé and 
Sines. At international level ISQ is represented at: Angola, Brazil, Cape Verde, China, French Guiana, Mozambique, 
Norway, Saudi Arabia, Spain, United Arab Emirates, Turkey, Timor and USA.  
 
 
 
ISQ is a leading European Technological Infrastructure of applied research, a strong and reliable long life partner for 
industry contributing to its technological development. ISQ has been selected by relevant scientific organisations as a 
competent and reliable partner to be involved in the main International Scientific projects as LHC-Large Hadron Collider 
(CERN), International Thermonuclear, Experimental Reactor (ITER), IXV - Intermediate eXperimental Vehicle (ESA) 
and E-ELT-Extremely Large Telescope (ESO). 
The large experience and know-how of ISQ staff, allows us to face the future challenges in the ceaseless search for new 
solutions towards sustainability. 
Background expertise relevant for Ligt Ecosystems 
ISQ is considered the largest Portuguese inspection and testing organisation, having an industrial background with almost 
50 years of expertise. Therefore, ISQ is able to offer quality support to the proposed project activities and interface with 
the main end- user and stakeholders of the interest ot LigthMe ecosystem. ISQ has a large expertise in welding 
specifications and processes, inspection and in testing, with expertise in tailor made testing development (non-standard 
testing), in which specific setups needs to be developed. 
Structural Testing: ISQ is the largest Testing organisation in Portugal providing a wide range of structural testing for 
qualification and certification purposes. During the last 20 years has been collaborating with relevant  Aerospace 
stakeholders in the area of testing, particularly for Space. ISQ has a dedicated Large scale structural Testing Centre in 
Castelo Branco (Centre of Portugal). Worked with Embraer in Portugal in development projects in large scale testing. 

[DT-NMBP-01-2018]  
[LightMe]    [ 106 of 10] 
ISQ is supported by a large range of testing laboratories namely Electrical, EMC, Materials, NDT and others, associated 
to a large background knowledge for instrumentation and data acquisition of tailor made testing.  
 
Materials qualification testing: ISQ has a strong materials and thermodynamics laboratories used to perform tailor made 
testing in advanced materials particularly for space and aeronautics as well as for other industries as automotive, Oil and 
Gas and Energy. ISQ is providing outsourcing service support on Materials Laboratory to the plants of EMBRAER in 
Évora-Portugal. ISQ Material laboratory has been involved in several works and projects for Airbus, Snecma, Astrium 
and ESA among other stakeholders in tes ting of A/C and aerospace parts, as well as in the characterisation of space 
vehicles specific coatings.  
 
Non destructive Inspection: ISQ NDT laboratory is the largest in terms of participation in R&D projects with strong 
background in the development of dedicated solutions for inspection. NDT lab was also involved with EMBRAER and 
TAP (Portuguese Airlines MRO Operator) in the development of NDI solutions for advanced composite materials. 
Relevant work was carried out also with Airbus Military and other relevant research programmes, such as ITER, for the 
nuclear reactor, and CERN in the inspection of LHC. 
 
Sustainability: ISQ is strongly involved in LCA studies applied to different industries, namely with ESA in the 
assessment of manufacturing processes, sp ace materials and propellants. In addition, coordinates the MAESTRI 
(H2020), project within the PPP- SPIRE focussed on the development of models for the eco -efficiency in terms of 
materials reduction and energy for the Process industry. ISQ has large experience also in eco-efficiency methodologies, 
decision support tools, energy efficiency, innovative business models, hygiene and safety, and training. ISQ provides 
technical expertise to support companies on research and innovation activities, promote sustainability and contribute to 
their constant improvement. ISQ has a long-term relationship with Industry, due to more than 20 years of work supporting 
their sustainable development. This synergetic collaboration with industry allows ISQ to understand the industrial 
demands and concerns in terms of energy & environmental, safety, economic and social aspects of their sustainability. 
ISQ participates in a number of International Networks/Associations namely The European Steel Technology Platform 
(ESTEP); Energy M aterials Industrial Research Initiative (EMIRI); ENERGY IN; Production Technologies Cluster 
(PRODUTECH); Sustainable Process Industry Through Resource Efficiency (SPIRE), National Group for Process 
Integration (GNIP), The European Virtual Institute for Int egrated Risk Management (EU -VRi); European technology 
platform on industrial safety (ETPIS); Portuguese Aeronautic, Space and Defense Cluster (AED Portugal)., among 
others. 
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
ISQ will be a core member of the LightMe Ecosystem and participates in 3 building block of the ecosystem: Building 
Block 2:  Monitoring of PLs; Building Block 3: Testing and environmental assessment services and Building Block 5: 
H&S, nanosafety, regulation & standardization services. In the Building block 2, ISQ will collaborate with AIMEN in 
the development of an on- line NDT inspection system to be integrated in the pilot line MWAM, within task T3.1. In 
building block 3, ISQ will support industry with characterization and NDT inspection methods of the manufactured 
materials and composite components, in selected test cases, based on the workflows that will be defined. It is also 
responsible, within the building block 5 to support industry on safety offering Environment and worker's safety services 
(particularly in the Task 3.1) and Consulting services on nanosafety, on the test cases based on industry needs. This 
building block will cover transversal activities within the test bed, offering expertise support to ecosystems and test cases 
and consulting services to the open calls, and external clients (on request). ISQ will also lead the task T13.3 promoting 
liaisons with nanosafety initiatives to promote and establish liaisons with relevant entities and initiatives related to safety 
and nanosafety, in order to promote synergies and knowledge exchange and to foster potential partnerships to strengthen 
both the LightMe ecosystems and its clients, as well the EHS community. Will also collaborate in the different WP 
related to the set -up of ecosystem structure & procedures and set up of ecosystems tools. In the validation phase, ISQ 
will support, through the building blocks 3 and 5, the different test cases WP.  Finally, ISQ will also be involved in the 
dissemination of the LightMe activities and achieved results supporting the divulgation through scientific and technical 
publications, in journals, as well as, by participating in conferences and industrial fairs.

Description of any significant infrastructure and/or any major items of technical equipment 
ISQ headquarters are at Porto Salvo, Oeiras, Portugal 
Laboratories: ISQ has 16 laboratories, all accredited according to the EN ISO 17025 norm including: Materials and 
Metallurgy Laboratory, Electrical Appliances and CE type approval Lab, Thermodynamics Laboratory, Non‐destructive 
testing, Metrology (pressure, force, temperature, mass, electromagnetic compatibility, electronics, volume and flow, 
chemical analysis and pollution control, etc...)  
Training: ISQ is accredited for training services and training of trainers and is certified under Quality, Environmental 
and Safety management model NP EN ISO 9001:2008, ISO 14001 and OHSAS 18001. Currently, the training offer 
includes Qualification, Certification, Training of Trainers, Continuous Training and Postgraduate courses with an 
increasing focus on dual certification – academic and professional – and also in work based learning: learning in practical 
working environments, network of accredited laboratories aiming skills achievement. ISQ has long experience providing 
training, being accredited according to EU regulations. ISQ has achieved in 2010 the number of 100.000 trainees since 
its creation in 1989. ISQ has 5 training facilities across Portugal (Oeiras, Vila Nova de Gaia, Loulé, Sines and Castelo 
Branco) covering the whole country.

Description of the legal entity 
The main activities of J-VST are placed in the fields of technology and engineering service and production of powder 
and forged structure parts using cold die- forging processes and also thread screw rolling technologies including 
development and production of anchor bolts and fasteners 
J-VST, s.r.o. offers: 
 
 Fasteners manufacturing 
 Die-forgings manufacturing with technical specification provided, 
 Components high quality, 
 Components ompetitive prices, 
 On-time delivery, 
 Packaging and transport of die-forging, 
 Making tools for die-forging and their regeneration. 
 
J-VST, s.r.o. is also a supplier of components for Volkswagen. The company obtained TÜV certificate certifying 
that J-VST has established and applies a Quality System for Development and Pr oduction of Parts for Forming, 
Development, Production and Implementation of Tools. 
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
JVST will be a test case (downstream industry) of the LightMe Ecosystem responsible for the pilot production of 
special fasteners made of Al alloy composites in WP7. The JVST goal is the development, testing and validation of 
Al alloy based nanostructured composite produced by SPS-KOBO in INOP with cold forging technology to obtain 
light weight fastene rs and components with targeted mechanical properties. Al and Al -alloy will be used as 
lightweight materials for structural components.  One of the most economical manufacturing processes to be applied 
will be extrusion, especially when it will come to complex profile geometries for lightweight constructions. In the 
field of vehicle technologies, ways to increase component strength and stiffness due to use of composite materials 
will be defined at the pilot stage. They will lead WP7 and validate Al-based composites profiles reinforced with BC
4 
NPs meeting all requirements of the automotive sector. Collaborating with the characterization building block they 
will evaluation of Al/BC4 reaching structural and functional characteristics. For WP12 they will mobilize their 
contact starting to engage them in the Open call. They will be also involved in the Clustering & training activities 
producing protocols of use cases. In collaboration with AXIA they will work on the exploitation strategy of their 
Pilot lines ensu ring the IP rights and business development action. Additionally, for the Dissemination they will 
design and development of their role in the ecosystem, project description, publication considering events 
worldwide.

SA is a leading company in the production of wear resistant alloys for use in the Mining, Cement, Power and Defence 
Industry. With exports to 15 countries, Kampakas SA is one of the key players in this market. Kampakas SA is one

TiO
2 nanoreinforced of door knobs produced via LPDC &  GSC. PoliMi has collaborated in the past with Kamp in

Relevant publications, and/or products, services or other achievements 
Kampakas S.A., as a part of the metal manufacturing sector of Europe, faces the common problems that this sector 
has like the competition of Asian metal manufacturers due to the lower labour cost, especially after the economic 
crisis. By participating in the MM C-Casting project and becoming a link in the supply chain, the company aims to 
produce products with more durable characteristics that will be more competitive due to their enhanced wear 
resistance. The idea of this proposal has lunched few year ago where Kampakas started their collaboration with

commercialized under the framework of Fast Track to innovation.

his company in the related field. Patents: Int. Cl. B22D 19/08, B22D 19/14

Description of the legal entity 
MagnesiumCom OU was registered in 2012 in Estonia. The company holds a vast intellectual property portfolio -
- holds numerous patents and registered industrial designs -- and conducts advanced materials R&D activities, with 
several progressive projects underway toward  commercialization. MagnesiumCom owns SMW Wheels SIA in 
Latvia and several stakes in other assets. Magnesium.com is a comprehensive online resource for engineers and 
others interested in the history, development and applications of magnesium and strives to give you the latest field-
related news in an accessible and convenient way, including:  a searchable, constantly-updated data bank of articles 
and profiled newsletters featuring summaries and links to the top stories in your field. 
SMW manufactures the prototypes at its facilities in Latvia under the direction of MagnesiumCom.  
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
Mgcom is an upstream industry, in LightMe they will act in short as a provider of composite materials for MWAM 
HPDC and GSC. They have inhouse facility for semi-continuous-casting of magnesium alloy billets, which are to 
be extruded and drawn into wire of Magne sium-based metal matrix composites (MMCs) using carbon 
nanomaterials (e.g. graphene), as reinforcements. Thus, they will have a leading role in WP5 and will be in close 
collaboration with Mg composites for use in WMAM, HPDC and GSC exploring different requirement. More 
specifically they will produce Mg/ Graphene castable alloys with enhanced stiffness and yield strength, the wires 
will be appropriate for the MWAM. The metal deposition additive manufacturing processes will be developed for 
manufacturing airc raft landing gear structural parts. MWWM AM processes will be utilized for producing a) 
Aircraft machined parts holding a great potential for justification by means of cost as a result of relatively low 
annual quantities. Additionally, Mg/CNTs castable alloys will be developed for HPDC and GSC lines. In order to 
achieve a homogeneous distribution of Graphene and CNTs into molten Mg alloy and integration into the lattice, 
electromagnetic stirring (EMS) with special ultrasonic cavitation will be implemented. The validation of the 
workflows vs the operation of the ecosystem will thus be evaluated by the strong collaboration of Pilot holders 
AIMEN, Ubrun and OGI. In WP12 they will work on open call they will contribute in training activities for the 
ecosystems. Finally, in WP14, they will contribute as all partner in the dissemination/exploitation and knowledge 
management including the task related to attraction of additional funding. 
SMW produces the prototypes at its facilities in Latvia under the direction of MagnesiumCom.

Description of any significant infrastructure and/or any major items of technical equipment 
Magnesium wheels and other large parts/components are forged from a billet 
(referred to as ERB).  Increasing its properties (by strengthening the lattice) is 
instrumental for succes sfully replacing other materials with Mg alloys for 
various applications where lightweighting is essential. In some cases, stiffness 
is crucial -- such as in F1 wheels or some bicycle parts. Magnesiumcom has 
developed a proprietary direct chill casting pro cess to produce the billets with 
improved microstructure and possessing higher properties, including 
reinforcing them with SiC particles. This enables to achieve higher mechanical 
properties for the resulting products – due to the high underlying metallurgical 
characteristics of the billet, and also the innovative wire drawing technology. 
 
Magnesiumcom is implementing important R&D projects with high growth potential, such as projects to create 
new materials, particularly graphene-reinforced magnesium MMC. The DC cast billets get extruded into bars, then 
drawn into wire – to be deployed for additive manufacturing. The AM process is being tested with Fraunhofer 
Institute in Dresden. 
 
Numerous applications for sports products are under development, including innovative sheet production process, 
bicycle parts, etc. One of the applications is for ballistic protection (armor). Reinforced magnesium syntactic foam 
prototypes are undergoing testing. 
 
Magnesiumcom is collaborating with Tallinn University of Technology and University of Tartu in a joint R&D 
project to develop shielding material for space and earth applications. One solution is the use of protective 
materials, for which EMbloq is specifically designed. Additionally, protection against electromagnetic exposure is 
relevant for data services security -- against wiretapping and EMP attacks. Recently electromagnetic pulse weapons 
have been developed aimed at disabling a car's microprocessors/electronics and also an engine of any vehicle. 
EMbloq will offer protection against such engine-stoppers, etc. 
SMW operates the laboratory in Riga, able to perform various experimental works, in addition to small -scale 
production of powder for SLM (by plasma synthesis) and wire for cladding (AM), as well as manufacturing 
capacity to implement production of over 50000 forgings per annum, and experimental 3D-printing.

4.1.17 MBN NANOMATERIALIA SPA 
 
Participant No 17 
 
Short name MBN 
Country Italy 
Organization type SME 
webpage http://www.mbn.it 
Description of the legal entity 
Founded in 1994 MBN Nanomaterialia (www.mbn.it) is a producer of nanostructured powder materials trough a 
proprietary mechano- chemical synthesis process technology (Mechanomade®). With an installed industrial 
production capacity of more than 100 ton/range on 6 production plants, MBN is offering to the market innovative 
materials that can be treated using the conventional powder metallurgy and deposition processes. Typical output of 
the process is constituted by agglomerated powders in the micron-size range (i.e. 5-100μm) constituted by aggregates 
of nanocrystals and nanoparticles (i.e. <100nm). The powder materials produced find application in a number of 
manufacturing chains as, conventional and fast sintering, laser sintering (AM) and coating  deposition. Beside the 
industrial production of ferrous and nonferrous alloys for diamond grinding tools and thermal spraying powders (Ti 
based and carbides based), since last years MBN has been working on novel nanostructured materials and 
nanocomposites for high temperature alloys (pressing and extrusion) and for high strength Al and Ti composite by 
powder metallurgy and Additive Manufacturing. In particular, MBN is producing ODS materials with unrivalled 
resistance to high temperature, oxidation and creep resistance and new powders for additive manufacturing by laser 
metal deposition process for aerospace (TiAl based) and mechanical applications. MBN is a ISO 9001:2008 certified 
company which ensure the supply of high quality grade raw materials for the industry. MBN is also a validated 
supplier of biomedical Titanium powder conforming standard specification ASTM F1580-12. MBN aims have been 
always to combine competitiveness and sustainable development placing great emphasis on the improvement of the 
quality of life through the development of green materials. in different industrial sectors. In this context MBN have 
developed an organization, management and control model (231 Model) which ensures it is in compliance with the 
Italian legislation requirements. 
 
MATRES is the third party linked to MBN. Matres is a R&D company focused on the development of applied 
research in the advanced processing and powder metallurgy field. Matres team consists of material scientists, 
chemists and engineers with experience in working in collaborative projects with companies, research institutes and 
universities. Matres have state of the art equipment for physical and morphological characterization of the material 
developed and produced: specific surface area measurements (BET), average crystal size (XRD), average particle 
size distribution (Laser Diffraction), elemental analysis (EDS, LECO), imaging (SEM), optical properties (UV-Vis-
NIR spectrometer), thermal properties (TG -DTA) and equipment for mechanical characterization (Toughness, 
Tensile strength, Hardness). Matres have prototype facilities for powder material post processing (thermal treatment, 
classification) and consolidation (pressing, HIP, sintering). 
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
MBN is acting as an upstream industry, provider of special powder materials for advanced production techniques. 
They will start thein involvement at early stages of the project since they will lead T3.5 preparation of the test cases 
collaborating very close with all test cases. Thus, they will have a leading role in WP4 and validate the combination 
of different families of composite powders made of Al and Ti matrixes with ceramic nanoparticles to be used as 
reinforcing means via the utilization of SPS and powder AM t echniques. MBN produces powders for feedstock in 
additive manufacturing and sintering processes. Their materials find applications in the automotive and aerospace 
industry. The main objective of the MBN’s test case is to produce via HEBM novel pre-alloyed powders for use in 
two PL: The Borealis AM line and the SPS line. The powders will result as the combination of two families of 
ceramic NPs (carbides and 2D NPs) with Titanium and Aluminum alloys. In WP11 which is the test case of DIAD 
they will work on T11.2 during which the scale up and Validation of conrods & gear box will be done. DIAD and 
MBN have already collaborates in the past in the EC funded projects MMTech and intend now to extend their 
experience in the pilot scale production of Ti nano reinforced alloys. The materials and processes will validate the 
ecosystem passing across T11.3. MBN will have a pivotal role in WP13 and especially in T13.1 due to the fact that 
they are leading NanoFutures and are members in EPPN and nanosafety platforms. In c ollaboration with the 
Innovation Management Building Block they will work on training and showcasing activities. Finally, they will 
contribute in the dissemination of the LightMe by participating in conferences and industrial fairs during WP14.  
MATRES: Post processing equipment for morphological refinement of the powders, classification and shape, under

4.1.18 Verein für praktische Gießereiforschung, Österreichisches Gießerei-Institut 
 
Participant No 18  
 
Short name ÖGI 
Country Austria 
Organization type SME/RTD 
webpage http://ogi.at/ 
Description of the legal entity 
The ÖGI is a non-university, non-profit research organisation aiming to increase the fundamental understanding of 
materials and processes related to castings. The annual turnover in 2017 was € 4,300,000.- achieved with 45 members 
of staff. At the ÖGI extensive casting facilities are available on industrial scale involving gravity, low pressure and 
high pressure die casting machines and the required peripheral and downstream equipment. Its main research activity 
is on casting processes to obtain thin wall castings for light weight designs using as scientific tools integrated process 
control, simulation and verification by computed tomography. Major research effort is on the characterisation of 
materials related to their processing route. This involves a detailed study of obtained microstructures and 
characterisation of static and dynamic properties which are used in FEM to model properties of castings under 
different loading conditions. Particular, research effort was on the dynamic properties of Al -alloys dependent on 
processing route and temperature in power -train application as well as on the characterisation of the dynamic 
properties. The ÖGI is a leading European knowledge transfer centre for SME working in the area of casting and 
foundry technology in particular for light metals.  
In the field of casting and foundry consultancy the ÖGI offers its clients following services: 
• Pilot scale casting facilities.  This includes all major casting methods of sand casting, gravity die, low 
pressure die and high pressure die casting. 
• Simulation and modelling. By measuring thermo-physical data and incorporating these into finite element 
simulation virtual process control can be achieved over the above casting processes. 
• Characterization. Within ISO 17025 accredited framework chemical, physical, mechan ical and 
microstructural properties of casting and other materials can be determined for customers. 
Strategic support and counsel. Based on the pilot scale casting internal and external know how and the simulation 
results the ÖGI offers its clients consult ancy services how to obtain the crucial properties of casting by control of 
the foundry or subsequent processes. 
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
 
PILOT LINE 1 FOR LOW PRESSURE DIE CASTING PL (LPDC) 
PILOT LINE 3 FOR GREEN SAND CASTIN (GSC) 
 
The ÖGI will be a core member of the LightMe Ecosystem responsible for the pilot line services in sand casting 
(GSC) and low pressure die casting (LPDC), being members of Building block 1 Pilot lines and fast prototyping. 
They will set a prototype of an industrial facility for manufacturing of medium / large size components using WLAM 
principle capable of processing non -
ferrous alloys and develop and test process parameters for processing of 
advanced composite materials provided by the SME partners. In WP5 they will be in close collaboration with Mgcom 
in order to test the Mg composite bars reinforced by CNTs. The will also participate in WP6 collaborating with AML 
for the test cases produced in the pilots of LPDC. In WP6 they will collaborate with AML and provide them 
components for precise machining these will be casted Ti & Al aluminium alloys for applications addressing mainly 
the aerospace sector. In WP8 that is the test case of Kampakas they will work on the upscaling pilots of LPDC and 
GSC in order to manufacture Al/TiO2 MMC exhibiting self-cleaning and anti-bacterial properties. They will further 
occupy their two pilots and collaborate with Hidria to produce lightweight steering pinions. Mechanical properties 
and porosity is of crucial importance for the commercialization of new Al and Mg alloys reinforced with SiC NPs 
will be done by the characterization their facilities and results produced from tall test cases.  Finally, in WP14, they 
will contribute as all partner in the dissemination/exploitation and knowledge management including the task related 
to attraction of additional funding.

Relevant publications, and/or products, services or other achievements 
The ÖGI was established in 1953 as a non -profit research organisation  and has worked over the years in close 
collaboration with the Austrian and European foundry industry.  Research focus of the ÖGI is on ferrous and non- 
ferrous casting alloys produced by casting and their properties. The ÖGI has long tradition to act as an external R&D 
facility for SME based foundries in Austria, Germany and south east of Europe to transfer foundry related know how 
into foundries and their customers. The ÖGI works in close collaboration with the University of Leoben and 
disseminates it's r esearch in over 20 publications annually as well as in the organisation of an annual conference 
aimed at the SME sector of foundries and other metal working industries.

Description of any significant infrastructure and/or any major items of technical equipment 
The location of the ÖGI is in the centre of Europe, Leoben, with easy access to the main centres of automotive 
OEMs. The ÖGI hosts pilot lines for sand casting and low pressure die casting and additionally has an operating 
high pressure die casting cell. On the pilot line for sand casting, a green sand intensive mixer (Eirich) and a twin 
screw mixer for an -organically or organically bounded sand (Wöhr) are available to produce environmentally 
friendly moulding materials. Additionally existing induction and resistance furnaces will be used to cast into the 
produced sand moulds. The pilot line for the low pressure die casting consist of a self -contained low pressure die 
caster with excellent control of the filling rates into permanent and non- permanent (to be developed during the 
project) moulds.

4.1.19 GLOBAL EQUITY & CORPORATE CONSULTING SL (SD PARTNERS)

Short name SD Partners

Web page http://www.sdpartners.eu/ 
Description of the legal entity 
SD Partners is a financial consulting firm and M&A boutique based in Madrid (Spain) and specialized in attracting 
private capital for Start Ups with a technological base. SD Partners is integrated into the Incotec Group, which has 
more than 80 employees and whose core business is the R&D consultancy to leading national and international 
technology companies. SD Partners team is comprised of professionals  with extensive international experience in 
investment banking. SDP has access to national and international Venture Capitals and have successfully closed 
several deals in recent years.  Because SD Partners is included within the INCOTEC Group, the participating projects 
in LightMe can benefit from a series of products and synergies, highlighting the area of technology transfer. This 
area aims to connect and facilitate the transfer of knowledge and innovations generated to the market. For this, 
Incotec is responsible for: 
 
Development of processes, methodologies and tools that contribute to organize and manage innovation processes in 
the company. 
 Making available to our customers the emerging technologies of leading research centres and the most 
suitable industrial partners. 
 Innovating at minimum cost thanks to public and private financing instruments. 
 Thus, LightMe companies will be able to seek financial advice and those with the most promising technology 
that have the need to grow financially could be advised on seeking private capital. 
 SD Partners offers LightMe companies comprehensive financial advice in all areas of the business. 
 Elaboration of a business plan that allows achieving the objectives of the shareholders using the mixture of 
private resources and financial debt that supposes lower possible cost to the company. 
 Access to international fund providers. 
 Advice on the planning and elaboration of the documentation to attend a round of financing. 
 Accompanying the company during the entire process of financing search until the signing of the transaction. 
 Strategic advice to maximize the value of the company in the shortest time possible before seeking private 
financing     
 
Role in the project  
SD Partners are specialized in attracting private capital for Start Ups with a technological base. Thus, they will lead 
Task 14.5 which is related to the post project sustainability of the ecosystem. SD will secure access to additional funding 
which is envisaged to be achieved through the combination of public and private funding. A preliminary plan has 
been scheduled and presented in the business plan of section 2. The LightMe has already taken action for contacting 
investing groups which demonstrated the importance and the market needs of the market. During the project further 
actions and contacts of additional funding groups, banks and crowdfunding platforms will take place. They will also 
be in charge of creating value chain related business plans and provide services to costumers entering the ecosystem. 
In WP12 they will get involved in outreach activities and Clustering. Finally, they will also contribute in WP14 
Dissemination, Communication & Exploitation in collaboration with AXIA thus identifying additional exploitation

Description of the legal entity 
STAM (www.stamtech.com) is a private engineering company, with a staff of more than 15 people, based in Genoa, 
Italy. The main mission of the company is to provide engineering services to industries. Since its establishment in 
1997, the company has been specializing in design and manufacturing of innovative mechanical systems, based on 
conventional and non-conventional robotics and mechatronics. 
 
STAM is specialized in high-tech sector, providing turnkey solutions in the following fields: automation & robotics, 
defence & security, aerospace, transports, energy. STAM has established partnerships with key players in the 
manufacturing industry: Faac, Kuka, CRF, OtoMelara, Comau and since 1997 is technological provider of the 
European Space Agency. 
STAM invests a significant part of its turnover in R&D thus providing their customers with most qualified and 
edging competencies to drive development based on availability and affordability of technological trends. 
STAM is a SME member of E2BA and has been collaborating with the European Space Agency since 1999, both as 
technology provider and in Technology Transfer. The company has also developed a strong experience in working 
with the funding instruments of the European Commission under FP5, FP6, FP7, H2020, Eureka and ERA -Net 
frameworks, being involved in more than 50 Projects over the last 15 years, in the fields of: automation, 
mechatronics, adaptive production equipment, high precision manufacturing technologies, new materials and energy. 
 
The Company performs all stages of the product design cycle, from conception through validation with CAD and 
FEA tools, to component and subsystem design and specification, down to the definition of tools, and production 
cycles. Regarding the process design and definition, STAM also works in the development of production process 
control and monitoring systems, including both the hardware and the software. During recent y ears, the Company 
has also matured a good expertise in working with databases, from creation to management and update.

4.1.22 Time.lex 
 
Participant No 22 
 
Short name Time.lex 
Country Belgium 
Organization type SME 
Webpage http://www.timelex.eu 
Description of the legal entity 
Time.lex is a boutique law firm based in Brussels, specialised in information and technology law in the broadest 
sense, including privacy protection, data and information management, e- business, intellectual property and 
telecommunications. Its activities cover all legal issues encountered in the creation, management and exploitation of 
information and technology, in all of its diverse forms. 
 
Time.lex as an independent firm was founded in 2007, but all its lawyers started their career in international law 
firms and multinational companies. The team is internationally recognised, being both a Legal 500 Top Tier firm in 
Information Technology, and a Cham bers Europe Recommended Firm for TMT - Information Technology, 
Intellectual Property, Data Protection and Entertainment. Time.lex has a proven track record in every aspect of 
information and technology law, from an academic, business and policy perspective.  
 
At time.lex, all legal facets of the modern information society are our area of expertise, which we continuously 
cultivate by assisting policy makers, public and private organizations with all their legal problems in this area. 
 
The time.lex team provides support from a pragmatic perspective as lawyers at the bar of Brussels, and from a policy 
perspective as advisors to various governments, public administrations and legislative bodies in Belgium, at the 
European level, and internationally. 
 
The time.lex team is specifically known for its European policy studies in a variety of subjects, including data 
protection, electronic signatures, electronic identity management, e -business and e-government, in which they can 
rely on an extensive network of IT law experts covering all European countries.  
 
From a business perspective, time.lex frequently assists companies in establishing suitable policies and legal 
frameworks in their data management activities, including with regard to the cross border transfer and processing of 
personal data, data security and liability management issues. Its clients include private companies and public sector 
bodies in the IT sector, financial services, e-health, marketing and e-commerce. 
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
Time.lex will be a core member of the LightMe Ecosystem responsible for legal compliance and legal support which 
will consist the 1st phase of the LightMe ecosystem. This will be covered under the activities of WP2 and WP3 that 
connects the set up the structural and operational aspects. They will thus lead Task 2.1 which will be the 
administrative structure of the Ecosystem and SEP set up, officially the target is to establish the LightMe NPO in 
M20. As a layer firm they will also be in charge of Task 14.3 which will cover all knowledge Management and IPR 
protection issues which services will also be provided to the clients entering the open call. Thus, their work will 
focus principally on intellectual property management, licensing, and corporate law for the establishment and 
operation of the non- profit organisation which will support LightMe’s exploitation. Time.lex will assist in 
establishing the legal and administrative steps in ensuring the creation of the entity (drafting its statutes/articles of 
association, meeting approval and publication requirements, establishing its mission statement and a governance 
structure with a clear definition of the powers of the executive committee. Secondary tasks include data protection 
and ethics compliance, contractual support in establishing business relations with third parties with whom the non-
profit will interact, and liability management in accordance with the strategic choices of the consortium.

4.1.23 UNIVERSITY BRUNEL LONDON  
 
Participant 
No 23  
  
 
Short name Ubrun

Description of the legal entity 
Brunel University London (Ubrun) is a university located in west London, UK. It was established in 1966 and has 
currently approximately 13000 students and 2,500 staff. In 2014/15 it had a total income of £200.7 million of 
which 25% came from grants and research contracts.  BUL has a strong history in engineering and in 2017 was 
ranked in the top 200 best universities in the world, in the field of engineering and technology. BCAST (Brunel 
Centre for Advanced Solidification and Technology), is a research centre within the University which was founded 
in 2001. The Centre specializes in solidification and casting of metals (especially light metals). The Centre is the 
home of the Constellium UTC (University Technology Centre) and currently has almost 100 members of staff. 
BCAST is recognised as a centre of excellence, housing the EPSRC Centre – LiME, in liquid metal engineering. 
Recently >£75M has been invested in an Advanced Metals Casting Centre (AMCC) and Advanced Metals 
Processsing Centre (AMPC) and associated state-of-the- art equipment, creating a national scale -up facility to 
bridge the gap between fundamental, laboratory- scale research and full -scale industrial trials. Brunel University 
London (BUL) has demonstrated its commitment to Solidification Research by injecting over £21M into BCAST 
in the past 20 years. An initial investment of £3M was injected in 2001 to create the centre. This was followed in 
2010 by £1.5M which was spent on creating state -of-the-art research labs and £500k which was invested in new 
processing/casting equipment. An additional £1.7M was specified for a new Jeol 2100F HRTEM (commissioned 
September 2012) equipped with EDX, STEM, Tomography, HAADF and GIF image filtering in addition to a 
sample preparation lab. Brunel also committed £6M in 2013 for a 1500m2 purpose built laboratory for the new 
Advanced Metal Casting Centre (AMCC) providing a new building, additional state-of-the-art equipment such as 
High Pressure Die Caster, Low Pressure Die Caster, and Extruder, and additional £2M for supporting staff. To 
support the HeFCE UKRIP investment (total £60M) for phase 2 of t he development and the creation of the 
Advanced Metal Processing Centre housing  sand casting, Computer Tomography, Mechanical testing, advanced 
joining and shaping techniques, heat treatment and aging, Brunel has invested another £3M on staff and £7M for 
the building. The university has also committed another further £4.8M to support the EPSRC Manufacturing Hub 
grant with £2.4M of this earmarked for 20 PhD studentships in the Doctoral Training Centre (CDT – LiME). With 
this unrivalled support, the partners are well positioned to deliver on the research proposed in terms of facilities, 
technical know-how and staff support for this application to be fully successful. 
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
 
PILOT LINE 2 FOR HIGH PRESSURE DIE CASTING PL (HPDC) 
 
Ubrun’s role in LightMe is to provide access for the partners to state-of-the- art casting, characterisation and 
modelling facilities. In particular Ubrun will provide Industrial Partners with access to its HPDC capabilities within 
the LightMe Ecosystem. In Phase 2 Ubrun will take a role in the validation of the ecosystem (WP 5 & 9). In 
collaboration with the other five Pilot line leaders they will be deeply involved in Task 1.2 that covers the Technical 
management of LightMe. Ubrun will be involved in pilot line adaption to enable the introduction of nanoparticles, 
it will assist in providing data for die design optimisation through experimental and modelling approaches in order 
to produce high quality die cast components thus a constant collaboration with almost all Building Blocks will be 
established. In WP5 they will .be in close collaboration with Mgcom and evaluate composited Mg nanoreinforced 
alloys with CNTs. In WP09 they will produce appropriate work flows for the production of composite lightweight 
housing for steering pinions. For this they will collaborate with Hidria in order to produce Al composite 
components for the automotive sector. Close colla boration with other building block of the ecosystem will be

For WP12 they will mobilize their contact starting to engage them in the Open call. They will be also involved in

Description of personnel´s profile 
Dr Brian McKay (Male): Brian McKay is a Senior Lecturer (Associate Professor) at BCAST, Brunel University. 
Prior to this he was a university assistant at the Institute of Casting Research, University of Leoben, Austria (2003-
2009) and a research fellow at UMIST (2003). He obtained his DPhil from Oxford University and has more than 
20 years’ experience in solidification research, with 1 Patent on novel metal composites (UK Patent No. 
1714401.5), 1 trademarked product (Basaltium), and over 30 papers and two co- edited monographs published in 
the field.  His main expertise lies in the fields of castings, composites, interfaces, coatings, and their 
characterisation using advanced electron microscopy techniques. Whilst his research interests in the past have been 
centred on understanding heterogeneous nucleation during solidification, these interests now also include Metal 
Matrix Composites/Nano-composites, Powder Metallurgy and Electroplating. Over the past 9 years Brian has been 
involved in 10 successful grant awards totalling ~£20M. He was the Co-ordinator and PI of a €1.6M EU-FP7 grant, 
HardAlt, involving 12 partners from 6 countries that focused on finding an alternative nano-composite coating for 
Hard Chrome, a CoI on the £4.5M EPSRC - LiME grant that investigated solidification me chanisms, PI on the 
£150k “Characterization and Processing of High Thermal Conducting Al-MMCs” grant sponsored by the Korean 
Institute of Technology (KITECH) that examined the potential of CNT MMCs for High Power Light emitting 
Diodes (HPLeD’s), PI on the £300k STORM Innovate UK/EPSRC in which a new composite Al core was 
produced for offshore marine energy mooring connectors and Co-I on the £10M EPSRC Manufacturing Hub grant. 
He is a Fellow of the Higher Education Academy and Institute of Cast Metal Engineers and has sat on the 
Technical/Educational Board of the latter as an adviser since 2012. In addition he is a member of the EPSRC Peer 
Review College and an Associate Editor of the International Journal of Cast Metal Engineers. Over the years Brian 
has col
laborated with many companies including, LSM, BMW, Alcoa and Alcan. He has given several invited 
presentations throughout Europe and in 2006 he received a TMS Magnesium Application Award for his work in 
nucleation and more recently has been a recipient of the Rushlight Responsible Product or Service Award 2017-
18 for the STORM connector.  
 
Prof. Dmitry Eskin (Male): Prof. Dmitry Eskin is a world renowned expert in aluminium solidification processing 
with focus on alloy development, casting properties, structure evolution and defect formation, a leading expert in 
direct-chill casting and in ultrasonic melt treatment. He authored and co -authored 6 monographs, more than 250 
research papers (H-factor 28; 36 if books are included) and 5 patents. He has considerable experience in leading 
research projects including international collaboration. In recent years BCAST (Prof. D.G. Eskin) plays leading 
role (WP leader) in European FP7 projects on ultrasonic degassing (Ultragassing), application of external fields to 
the processing of metal -
matrix nanocomposite materials (Exomet), and DEMO project on the development of 
ultrasonic degassing machines for foundries (Doshormat) with a total funding allocated to UBRUN in excess of 
1M Euro. He also currently leads two EPSRC projects on fundamental studies of ultrasonic cavitation in liquid 
metals with a total funding of 1M Euro. He is a recipient of two Warren Patterson Cast Shop for Aluminum 
Production Awards and an Aluminum Technology Award from TMS (USA). More information can be found at 
http://www.brunel.ac.uk/people/dmitry-eskin 
 
Eric Nyberg (Male): Mr. Eric Nyberg holds a M.S. deg ree and a B.S. degree, both in Materials Science & 
Engineering, from Washington State University.  Mr. Nyberg worked for at the Danish National Laboratory, Risø, 
in Roskilde, Denmark (1989 – 1991) establishing their capability to produce gas atomized alumi nium powder.  
Following this he then spent the next 24 years with progressively increasing responsibility at the Pacific Northwest 
National Laboratory in Richland, WA where he eventually retired as Chief Engineer.  His work at PNNL involved 
important light weight alloy and process development including superplastic aluminium forming, rapid 
solidification and extrusion of magnesium alloys and joining technology for dissimilar metals.  Currently, Mr. 
Nyberg is the Director of Programmes at Brunel University’s Centre for Advanced Solidification Technology.  He 
has more than 50 technical publications, 3 patents and is the current Chairman of the Light Metals Division of The 
Minerals, Metals and Materials Society (TMS). 
 
Alain Jacot (Male): Dr. Alain Jacot is professor of solidification research at the Brunel Centre for Advanced 
Solidification Technology (BCAST), Brunel University, London. His field of expertise is numerical simulation of 
materials manufacturing, with a focus on phase transfo rmations in metallic materials. His particular interests are 
the development of numerical models that can be applied to industrial alloys and manufacturing processes, more 
specifically for solidification and heat treatment. Alain Jacot earned his MSc and PhD degrees in materials science 
from the Ecole Polytechnique Fédérale de Lausanne (EPFL, Switzerland). He shares his time between Brunel 
University and Lausanne office of ESI Group, where he is in charge of Materials Technology.

4.1.25 Iris Technology Solutions, Sociedad Limitada 
 
Participant No 25 
 
Short name Iris Tech 
Country Spain 
Organization type SME 
webpage http://www.iristechnologygroup.com/ 
Description of the legal entity 
IRIS is an advanced engineering company that specialises in process monitoring and control, and process 
optimisation.     
Our Commercial Division develops and integrates turnkey advanced process monitoring and control solutions based 
on: NIR chemical monitoring (handheld device and in -line solutions); hyperspectral imaging solutions for foreign 
body detection and chemical composition analysis; data management solutions for data processing, decision support, 
automation and data analysis (big production data). Our ambition is to the first choice for industry who want to 
transition their product models to the Industry4.0 paradigm, whereby real-time access to data about critical process 
parameters and product quality attributes can contribute to improved quality, and process efficiencies 
Our Innovation Division has three core research lines that we are actively persuing  as part of our Innovation 
Roadmap for generating new knowledge and IPRs that we can channel into new products, services and solutions for 
our Commercial Division in the future: 
1. Optical and spectroscopic technologies (e.g. MEMs spectrophotometers, fluor escence and Raman) for 
leveraging affordable, rapid and high performamce process monitoring for in/on-line and PAT applications in food, 
pharmaceuticals, the process industries, environmental monitoring and other applications 
2. Data Processing & Information Systems (Development of intelligent data management and decision support 
systems for smart manufacturing, processing and agriculture) 
3. Novel processing technologies (ultrasound, plasma, microwave…) for process intensification and non-
thermal decontamination   
4. Sustainable processing technologies: waste valorisation strategies, biocompounds and biopackaging and 
new bio-based materials for the Circular Economy 
The company was established in 2007 and currently employs 50+ staff with a turnover of > €4 M. We are based over 
two sites (Barcelona and Dublin) and we are fully equipped with our engineering and production workshops, food 
testing and wet chemistry laboratory, optics labs (2), and an electronics/telecommunications lab.  
IRIS is ISO 9001:2008 certified and also is certified under UNE -EN-ISO 166002: Management Systems R&D&i. 
IRIS is an industry member if the following sectorial networks: SPIRE, SPIE and SECPHO in additional to regional 
industrial collectives such as AEBALL- the industry association of Baix Llobregat and Smart Space (Association of 
companies and organisations that specialise in ‘smartification’). 
 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
Iris Tech will test novel advanced sensors for monitoring selected process parameters and will integrate them at plant 
level together with a bespoke control system. They will also collaborate in the study of the relevant parameters to be 
analysed in order to select the most suitable sensor technologies. They are under the building block of monitoring. 
Iris Tech will also develop data mining tools to produce relevant decision support tools for optimally controlling 
production based on relevant process data. In Task 3.1 Iris Tech will be in close collaboration with STAM, ISQ and 
the owners of the Pilot Lines in order to plan and implement all modifications during the first phase of the project. Their 
main responsibility will be to run and fine tune the pilot lines preparing them for the demonstration activities and the test 
cases which will enter after M20. They will also lead T3.2 customization of Ecosystem groups setting and arranging 
internal collaboration routs and communication with all the building blocks. They will be also involved in the Clustering 
& training activities creating guidelines and protocols of the pilot line operators which will be showcased.

4.1.26 UNIVERSIDAD DE BURGOS (ICCRAM) 
 
Participant No 24 
 
Short name ICCRAM 
Country sSpain 
Organization type University 
webpage www 
 
Description of the legal entity 
The University of Burgos (UBU) was founded in 1994 and has assumed its role in the local and regional economy 
and in the larger scientific development responding to market demands (e.g. new grades in accordance to the needs 
of the labor market) and developing wide research networks (e.g. integrated research between the university, the 
private sector, public institutions, and  civil society organizations). UBU has 67 research groups classified in five 
main research fields: Sciences, Social sciences, Engineering -Construction, Humanities and Health sciences. These 
Research groups have a consolidated prestige not only at national but also at international level with a relevant 
number of publications in the best research journals. Under this structure, two interdisciplinary groups of the 
University of Burgos would be joining LIGHT ME project: the International Research Center in Cri tical Raw 
Materials for Advanced Industrial Technologies (ICCRAM) and the Corporate Finance Group (CORFIN).  
ICCRAM is a part of privileged research and innovation core, integrated by the Research Center in Food 
Biotechnology (CIBA), the Center for Innovation and Research in Industrial Technology (CITI), a new Excellence 
International Center in Critical Raw Materials for Industrial Technologies (ICCRAM), as well as a new experimental 
facility in Applied Nanotechnology, and Nano/Toxicity (within the Science and Technology Park). 
ICCRAM takes part of the international strategy of industrial resource efficiency management, energy efficiency, 
eco-innovation and critical materials substitution, being directly related to the European Innovation Partnership in 
Raw Materials (EIP-Raw), and the Knowledge and Innovation Community in Raw Materials from the EIT (KIC -
Raw Materials) as Task Partner. ICCRAM was born conceived to integrate within its structure an "intrinsic path into 
innovation", and it is supported by an industrial board of more than 26 industries, SMEs and clusters. Moreover, 
ICCRAM coordinates an industrial platform with the City Council in the context of transition into Circular Economy. 
Among other disciplines, ICCRAM is an expert partner in advanced materials, nanomaterials, graphene technology, 
materials testing, integrated computational engineering, multiscale modelling,  biophysics, biotechnology ,  eco -
innovation, circular economy, resource efficiency, life -
cycle modelling and assessment, value chain design, 
innovation policies, materials safety, environmental compatibility and Nanotoxicity assessment of products and 
processes.  In this thematic areas, ICCRAM is participating in H2020 projects (MSCA-RISE, MSCA-ITN, MSCA-
IF, FET- OPEN, NMBP, SC5 and Spreading Excellence) being the coordinator of the H2020- MSCA-RISE 
NANOGENTOOLS and the H2020-FET-OPEN ICARUS.  
CORFIN (Corporate Finance) research group started in 2012 in the Department of Business Management of UBU. 
The group is leaded by prof. Oscar López -de-Foronda has 8 members and works on the research of Life -cycle cost 
analysis (LCCA) and circular economy, especially in the years after the 2007 -2008 financial crisis. The group has 
developed research activities in the field on business plan, corporate risk taking, overinvestment problems and 
antifraud activities for European companies considering the institutional and law factors in collaboration w ith 
research groups in Portugal, France and Germany. The group has published more than 50 papers in impact journals 
(JCR) in the field of business and law during the last 8 years. 
All in all, since 2008, UBU has been very active in several Research & Innovation European Programmes (H2020 
and previous FPs, LIFE, Justice, ERASMUS+, Interreg, CIP, COST, LLP, IEE, Research Fund for Coal and Steel, 
D. G. for Competition Policy and Strategy…) with over 40 European projects;  with the role of coordinator in 12 
projects and over 6.9 M€ overall funding. Currently, UBU participates in 26 on- going projects (i.e. H2020 (15), 
Erasmus+ (4), LIFE (1), Interreg SUDOE (2), Justice Programme (2); Research Programme of the Research Fund 
for Coal and Steel (1), D. G. for Competition Policy and Strategy (1)). In 2017, the funding awarded in different EU 
programmes is estimated over 1.2 M€ 
Description of the entity ´s main tasks in the proposal 
ICCRAM is participating in the LigthCoce project and will intensively participate in the Testing and environmental 
assessment services Building Block 3, due to their high expertise in LCA and LCC. level. Evaluation of the 
environmental impact of the new materials will take place by LCA/LCC. In close collaboration with end users real 
field test will be applied, bringing the technologies up to TRL7. The active involvement of end users (large 
companies, representative of automotive and aerospace sector, are already included in the consortium) will h ave a 
significant positive impact in the fast adoption of the new technologies by the market. During all upscaling WPs 4-
11 they will produce test case specific Life cycle cost (LCC) in order first to evaluate the economic feasibility of the 

[DT-NMBP-01-2018]  
[LightMe]    [ 149 of 10] 
ecosystem. Environmental life cycle analysis (LCA) will be also conducted for all test cases. In the final phase of the 
project they will also provide similar servicers to the test cases entering the ecosystem during WP12, thus support 
companies on environmental LCA .and LCC aspects correlated to product development and exploitation. In WP 13 
they will transversal get involved in aspects related to regulatory and legal assessments in nanosafety aspects being 
in close collaboration with ISQ. Closing, similar to all core partners of the ecosystem they will work on dissemination 
and exploitation activities attending stakeholder meeting, workshops conferences and fairs. 
Additionally, expertise of ICCRAM in complementary fields as exploitation and dissemination within the related 
sectors can contribute to maximize the impact of the Action. Recently, ICCRAM was awarded with a FET Innovation 
Launchpad (ICARUS-SW) led by BRIMATECH (the Austrian ESA Broker) to exploit the results of the Coordinated 
FET OPEN ICARUS  within the aerospace industry, which can bring interesting synergies to Light Me.  
ICCRAM brings also additional expertise in coordinating activities directed to the constitution of reliable and stable 
networks and stable cooperation models in thematic areas in the field of materials. This expertise brings together 
scientific knowledge, stakeholders of ICCRAM and also Project Management and Administration capabilities , 
assessing the implications of the new entities constitution. In this sense, the Project SUPERMAT (CSA-TWINNING) 
has as main result the constitution of a “Virtual Centre for Integration of Innovative synthesis and processing methods 
for Sustainable advanc ed Materials operating under Extreme Conditions”. In this regard, ICCRAM supported the 
Coordinator of the Project in the legal and governance implications of the network in order to meet the partners and 
project needs in order to boost the Virtual Center a
nd promote the fluent and reliable exchange of knowledge, 
technology and services. Another related project is SCRREEN (SC5- 2016), where ICCRAM is involved in the 
development of a “Long Lasting Network” able to provide policy assessment, as well as consultancy services based 
on the partners’ complementary expertise in the field of Critical Raw Materials. ICCRAM is leading the task for the 
establishment of this long lasting network devoted to the definition of the value proposition, methodology, 
governance, legal constitution, structure, funding and revenue streams of the network as well as the activity plan of 
this autonomous body that will last beyond the project’s life. 
 
Description of personnel´s profile 
 
 
 
MsC Sonia Martel (female). She holds a Master of Science in Forestry. Affiliated to the University of Burgos in the 
“International Research Center in Critical Raw Materials for Advanced Industrial technologies” (ICCRAM) since 
2015 within the Sustainability Research Line, she has been involved in the development of the LCA and sustainability 
analysis for the European projects ICARUS, NOVAMAG and REFRAM. Wide experience in project management 
in different areas related industrial development and promoting sustainability and circular approaches across different

4.1.27 INNOVACION Y CONSULTING TECNOLOGICO DE LEVANTE, S.L. 
Participant No 19  
 
 
Short name Innovación y Consulting Tecnológico de 
Levante, S.L. 
Country Spain 
Organization 
type 
SME 
Web page http://www.incotec.es 
Description of the legal entity 
INCOTEC Group is an independent initiative with more than 15 years’ experience in business innovation. 
Since the set up of the company in 2000, with the automotive sector as the main target, the INCOTEC’s 
activity has expanded to other areas making it one of the leading Spanish consultancy firms in the Agri-Food, 
Chemical, Ceramic, Automotive and Health sectors, among others. INCOTEC counts with near 100 
employees, most of them with a technical background (e.g industrial, electronical and agricultural engineers, 
chemists, pharmacists, etc). INCOTEC supports companies to structure their innovation in order to improve 
their competitiveness and market positioning. It analyses the business strategy of the companies and support 
them in the definition of their main R&D lines and action plans in the medium and long term, with the aim of 
building a solid innovation strategy driven by the market demand. 
Moreover, INCOTEC offers also technology transfer services to support Start ups, SMEs and research 
centres, working on the development of innovative solutions and disruptive technologies, in the identification 
of industrial partners potentially interested in investing or adopting the technologies. Additionally, one of the 
companies of the INCOTEC group is a financial consultan cy firm and Merger and Acquisition (M&A) 
boutique specialized in attracting private capital for Start Ups and SMEs with a technological base. 
 
INCOTEC offers business -oriented services, supporting businesses to commercially apply their innovations and 
transform their business, including the access to financing and investors. Related to the project objectives, INCOTEC 
has experience in overcoming barriers in the upscaling and market adoption of innovative technologies. This is done 
through the services provi ded to SMEs and Large Industry aiming to raise the investment interest of the industry. 
INCOTEC’s actions include the identification of target markets and segments and the definition of the value 
proposition. Apart from these activities for the market analysis, in line with the innovation management, INCOTEC 
works on the development of dedicated business plans and applies other useful tools like PEST, CANVAS and 
SWOT analysis. The results of the previous activities facilitate the access to additional fundin g, both public and 
private, understood to be the first pull to support the business opportunities. In this sense, INCOTEC counts on a 
well-established contact network including funding groups as well as banks and crowdfunding platforms.  
 
Role in the project  
 
INCOTEC will work to transform the developed innovative technologies into real business opportunities, 
helping companies to evaluate its technical and economic feasibility and the exploitation possibilities. The 
main objective will be to connect and facilitate the transfer of LIGHTME knowledge and results to the 
market. These contributions will be enclosed within Work Package 14 for the Exploitation, Dissemination and 
Communication.  
More specifically, the focus will be on Task 14.1, contributing to the exploitation activities and Task 14.5, 
leading the access to additional funding. Additionally, support will be given in the rest of Work Packages in 
all activities related to market orientation and innovation management. 
 
INCOTEC will collaborate in the development and evolvement of the Ecosystem’s business plan and its 
penetration strategies among the industry of the relevant sectors. Support will be given to the monitorization 
of the market situation and the assessment of business opportunities. Within WP12, INCOTEC will 
participate in outreach activities and clustering.  
 
INCOTEC will take appropriate measurements for the facilitation of access to funding for the potential clients 
of the ecosystem. LightMe has already taken action for contacting investing gr oups which demonstrated the 
importance and the market needs of the market. In this line, further actions and contacts of additional funding 
groups, banks and crowdfunding platforms will take place. Three main tasks can be defined to be done for 

[DT-NMBP-01-2018]  
[LightMe]    [ 153 of 10] 
both the different Pilot Lines and the Ecosystem as a whole: the market segmentation and characterization, 
the value proposition and business model definition and the profiling and mapping of investors.

Laura Zacarés (Female): Master in Business Innovation (Deusto University), PhD in Biochemistry and Plant 
Molecular Biology (Polytechnic University of Valencia) and Agricultural Engineering Degree (Polytechnic 
University of Valencia). Professional with more than 10 years of experience in management positions in the area of 
R&D and innovation, in national and international environments. Laura has a deep knowledge regarding R&D

Relevant previous projects or activities 
 
•LEE BED (GA 814485, 2019-2023): this project is aimed at developing a network of Innovative Test Beds for the 
development and production of nanomaterials for lightweight embedded electronics. INCOTEC participates in the 
development of Business plan, adaptation to market trends and economic outlook. It will support the owners of the 
Test beds and the developers of the technologies in finding private and public capital for startups to leverage the 
outcomes of the project.  
•BIOBEAUTY (Grant agreement ID: 606508). Development of a bioplastic package for organic cosmetic creams. 
The main aim is to develop biopackaging for organic and eco product lines that offers the same environmental 
credentials as the product that it contains through a combination of nanotechnology and active packaging. It will be 
based on an environmentally friendly biomaterial such as a Poly(lactic acid) (PLA) bionanocomposite and a natural 
active agent with antioxidant properties. The incorporation of nanoclays to the biocomposite is to improve the barrier 
properties of the PLA, while the incorporation of natural antioxidants in the packaging is to delay the degradation of 
cosmetic creams. Main activities were focused in the development of the protection and exploitation strategies of 
the project results.  
•ACTICOSPACK. (Grant agreement ID: 315720). Reducing the levels of preservatives in cosmetic products through 
active packaging technologies. ACTICOSPACK project focused at the development of active packaging solutions 
for three target cosm etic products. Each cosmetic product required different packages to be developed: Active 
polyethylene (PE) bottle for sun lotion, Active polypropylene (PP) pot for facial cream, Active polyethylene 
terephthalate (PET) bottle for shampoo. Main activities were focused in the development of the protection and 
exploitation strategies of the project results.  
•EASYFRUIT. (Grant agreement ID: 315565). Active packaging for extended shelf life of peeled and cut fruit. The 
aim of this project is to combine the search of positive interactions between the active compound and product with 
minimal processing treatments  and atmosphere packaging to reduce the rate of the spoilage mechanisms. The 
EASYFRUIT packaging solution combine minimal processing treatments with liberation of active compounds 
through the packaging. The agents will be incorporated to the package polymer matrix or as a coating. The package 
formulation will be optimized to provide target release kinetics and dosage for each fruit type. Furthermore the active 
species will be selected and optimized for each fruit type. Main activities were focused in the development of the 
protection and exploitation strategies of the project results.

22. TimeLex 
 
Does the participant plan to subcontract certain tasks (please note that core tasks of the 
project should not be sub-contracted) Y 
The workforce of TimeLex are lawyers at the Bar of Brussels. Based on the fact that (a) the  Art 6.2 
A2 cannot be applied to Bar lawyers and as such they cannot be charged as personnel costs, (b) 
that Bar Lawyers cannot be considered as in-house consultants and similar persons (i.e. self-
employed natural persons) and that (c) the Belgium rule regarding Bar Members not to have 
employment contracts, also apply to this “similar contractual (employment) arrangements”; 
Timelex staff that are Bar Members, would have to be subcontracted as such. Therefor the budget 
of Timelex should be: 
- Direct personnel costs: 0,0 € 
- Direct costs for subcontracting: 135.937,50 € 
- Direct costs: 12.000,00 € 
- Indirect costs: 3.000,00 €

ANNEX I 
Letters of Intent for LightMe ecosystem  
 
 
 
 
  

[DT-NMBP-01-2018]  
[LightMe]    [ 161 of 10] 
The partners of the LightMe project have already taken activities to increase the awareness stakeholders around 
the lightweight metal sector for the proposes of the LightMe Ecosystem. The partners have discussed with 
stakeholder from their network and have share the concept o f the ecosystem. 4 types of stakeholders have been 
approached: 
1. SMEs and Large Enterprises that could have potential interest to access the Ecosystem and take 
advantage of its future services 
2. End users (mainly Large Enterprises) that have explicit interest in the outcome of the future innovative 
activities of the Ecosystem, concerning new materials and products of lightweight MMCs 
3. Group of Investors, that could have potential interest in funding new concepts and products brought by 
SMEs and start ups 
4. Various stakeholders including associations, chamber of commerce and clusters as well as research 
institutes having potential interest in technology transfer services. 
The response and interest of the stakeholders around the lightweight metals was more tha n impressive as 65 
Letters of Intent have been collected in a period of 2 months. This, proves the significant importance of the 
LightMe ecosystem and is a indirect indication of the sustainability of it.

Initial Pricing of LightMe services to customers

[LightMe]    [ 165 of 10] 
The core partners of the Ecosystem have set up a list of service categorized on the six building block of the Ecosystem. The cost in most of the 
cases is given in ranges and it will be finalized with the activities undertaken in the WP2. The partners were committed to provide fair - low 
cost prices for their services. The services will be available to the client in no more than 30 days,
